Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Disliked Imams: Ruling and Proofs
Ruling on disliked imams with three proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leading prayer by a slave, Bedouin, sinner, illegitimate child, and blind person, and identify the proofs for this ruling.

Core Idea
It is makruh to appoint a deficient imam, but the prayer is valid if they lead.

In this passage from Al-Quduri, we encounter a clear ruling on who should not be put forward as imam and the evidence behind it. The text presents a hadith threatening non-acceptance, yet confirms validity if such individuals lead. Let's examine the ruling and its proofs to understand the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five categories of disliked imams.
List the types: slave, Bedouin, open sinner, illegitimate child, blind person. Note the term 'yukrahu' indicates dislike.
The blind person is included due to potential impurity issues, but some later scholars exempt him.
2
State the ruling: valid if they lead.
The text says 'fa in taqaddamu jaza' — if they lead, it is permissible. Understand the distinction between dislike and invalidity.
3
Analyze the first proof: hadith of three whose prayer is not accepted.
The hadith states Allah does not accept the prayer of one who leads while disliked. Identify the evidence for dislike. Note thubut and dalala.
The hadith is ahad, so it indicates makruh tahrimi, not haram.
4
Examine the second proof: action of Aisha.
Aisha was led by her slave Dhakwan from the Mushaf. This shows permissibility of a slave leading even a highly knowledgeable woman.
This demonstrates that the dislike is not absolute.
5
Review the third proof: Uthman's response on praying behind an imam of fitna.
Uthman advised praying behind an imam even if he is a sinner, as long as the prayer is correct. This reinforces permissibility.
The proof strengthens the jaza ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الجَمَاعَة
وَيُكْرَهُ تَقْدِيمُ الْعَبْدِ وَالْأَعْرَابِي وَالْفَاسِقِ وَوَلَدِ الزِّنَا وَالْأَعْمَى فَإِنْ تَقَدَّمُوا جَازَ وَيَنْبَغِي لِلْإِمَامِ أَنْ لَا يُطَوِّلَ بِهِمُ الصَّلَاةَ وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ أَنْ يُصَلِّينَ وَحْدَهُنَّ جَمَاعَةً فَإِنْ فَعَلْنَ وَقَفَتِ الْإِمَامَةُ وَسْطَهُنَّ.
وجه (١) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ تَقْدِيمُ الْعَبْدِ وَالْأَعْرَابِي عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَانَ يَقُولُ: «ثَلَاثَةٌ لَا يَقْبَلُ اللَّهُ مِنْهُمْ صَلَاةً، مَنْ تَقَدَّمَ قَوْمًا وَهُمْ لَهُ كَارِهُونَ» (سنن أبي داود، باب الرجل يؤم القوم وهم له كارهون، رقم ٦٨٥)
وجه (٢) قول الصحابية لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ تَقْدِيمُ الْعَبْدِ وَالْأَعْرَابِي: وَكَانَتْ عَائِشَةُ يَؤُمُّهَا عَبْدُهَا ذَكْوَانُ مِنَ الْمُصْحَفِ (صحيح البخاري، باب إمامة العبد والمولى، رقم ٦٩٢)
وجه (٣) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ تَقْدِيمُ الْعَبْدِ وَالْأَعْرَابِي: عَنْ عُبَيْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَدِيِّ بْنِ خِيَارٍ أَنَّهُ دَخَلَ عَلَى عُثْمَانَ بْنِ عَفَّانَ وَهُوَ مَحْصُورٌ فَقَالَ: إِنَّكَ إِمَامُ عَامَّةٍ وَنَزَلَ بِكَ مَا تَرَى وَيُصَلِّي لَنَا إِمَامُ فِتْنَةٍ وَنَتَحَرَّجُ؟ فَقَالَ: الصَّلَاةُ أَحْسَنُ مَا يَعْمَلُ النَّاسُ فَإِذَا أَحْسَنَ النَّاسُ فَأَحْسِنْ مَعَهُمْ وَإِذَا أَسَاءُوا فَاجْتَنِبْ إِسَاءَتَهُمْ (صحيح البخاري، باب إمامة المفتون والمبتدع، رقم ٦٩٥)
وجه (١) الحديث لثبوت وَيَنْبَغِي لِلْإِمَامِ أَنْ لَا يُطَوِّلَ بِهِمُ الصَّلَاةَ: أَخْبَرَنِي أَبُو مَسْعُودٍ أَنَّ رَجُلًا قَالَ: وَاللَّهِ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ إِنِّي لَأَتَأَخَّرُ عَنْ صَلَاةِ الْغَدَاةِ مِنْ أَجْلِ فُلَانٍ مِمَّا يُطِيلُ بِنَا فَمَا رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي مَوْعِظَةٍ أَشَدَّ غَضَبًا مِنْهُ يَوْمَئِذٍ ثُمَّ قَالَ: «إِنَّ مِنْكُمْ مُنَفِّرِينَ فَأَيُّكُمْ مَا صَلَّى بِالنَّاسِ فَلْيَتَجَوَّزْ فَإِنَّ فِيهِمُ الضَّعِيفَ وَالْكَبِيرَ وَذَا الْحَاجَةِ» (صحيح البخاري، باب تخفيف الإمام في القيام وإتمام الركوع والسجود، رقم ٧٠٢؛ مسلم، باب الدعاء في صلاة الليل وقيامه، رقم ٧٦٦)
وجه (١) قول الصحابية لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ أَنْ يُصَلِّينَ وَحْدَهُنَّ جَمَاعَةً: عَنْ رَيْطَةَ الْحَنَفِيَّةِ قَالَتْ: «أَمَّتْنَا عَائِشَةُ فَقَامَتْ بَيْنَهُنَّ فِي الصَّلَاةِ الْمَكْتُوبَةِ» (سنن الدارقطني، باب صلاة النساء جماعة وموقف إمامهن، رقم ١٥٠٧)
وجه (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ أَنْ يُصَلِّينَ وَحْدَهُنَّ جَمَاعَةً: عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «خَيْرُ صُفُوفِ الرِّجَالِ أَوَّلُهَا وَشَرُّهَا آخِرُهَا وَخَيْرُ صُفُوفِ النِّسَاءِ آخِرُهَا وَشَرُّهَا أَوَّلُهَا» (مسلم، باب تسوية الصفوف وإقامتها، رقم ١٤٤٠؛ سنن أبي داود، باب صف النساء وكراهية التأخر عن الصف الأول، رقم ٦٧٨)
وجه (٣) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ أَنْ يُصَلِّينَ وَحْدَهُنَّ جَمَاعَةً: عَنْ عَلِيٍّ قَالَ: «لَا تَؤُمُّ الْمَرْأَةُ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، من كره أن تؤم المرأة النساء، رقم ٤٩٥٧)
أصول: تنہا عورتوں کی جماعت مکروہ ہے، لہذا عورتیں تنہا ہوں یعنی مرد نہ ہو تو تنہا نماز پڑھے، جماعت نہیں، اور اگر تنہا جماعت کرے تو امام صف کے درمیان میں کھڑی ہو یعنی مردوں کی طرح مقتدی سے آگے نہیں۔
Section on Congregational Prayer. It is disliked to put forward a slave, a Bedouin, a sinner, an illegitimate child, and a blind person. If they do lead, it is permissible. It is appropriate for the imam not to lengthen the prayer for them. It is disliked for women to pray alone in congregation; if they do, the imam stands in the middle of them. Evidence (1) Hadith for the dislike of putting forward a slave and Bedouin: from Abdullah ibn Amr that the Messenger of Allah would say: 'Three persons whose prayer is not accepted: one who leads a people while they dislike him.' (2) Statement of a female companion: Aisha was led by her slave Dhakwan from the Mushaf. (3) Hadith: from Ubaydullah ibn Adi ibn Khiyar that he entered upon Uthman ibn Affan while he was besieged and said: You are the imam of the public, and this has happened to you; an imam of fitna leads us, should we refrain? He said: Prayer is the best of deeds; if people do good, do good with them; if they do evil, avoid their evil. Evidence for 'the imam should not lengthen the prayer': Abu Mas'ud informed me that a man said: By Allah, O Messenger of Allah, I am late for the morning prayer because of so-and-so who lengthens it; I never saw the Prophet more angry in a sermon; then he said: Among you are those who cause aversion; whoever leads people in prayer should be brief, for among them are the weak, the old, and those with needs. Evidence for 'it is disliked for women to pray alone in congregation': from Rayta al-Hanafiyya: Aisha led us, standing between us in the prescribed prayer. Also from Abu Huraira: The best rows for men are the first and the worst the last; the best rows for women are the last and the worst the first. Also from Ali: A woman should not lead. Principle: The congregation of women alone is disliked; therefore, women alone (without men) should pray individually, not in congregation. If they do form a congregation, the imam stands in the middle of the row, not ahead like for men.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof section on congregational prayer. The author first states the matn (core rulings) from Al-Quduri, then provides multiple proofs. The first ruling: it is makruh (disliked) to appoint a slave, Bedouin, open sinner, illegitimate child, or blind person as imam, but if they do lead, the prayer is valid (jaza). The Hanafi position is that these individuals are deficient in social status or religious character, so their imamate is disliked but not invalid. Proofs include a hadith that Allah does not accept the prayer of one who leads while disliked, but scholars interpret this as severe dislike; also Aisha being led by her slave shows permissibility. The second ruling: the imam should not lengthen the prayer; the hadith of Abu Mas'ud shows the Prophet's anger at those who make people flee. The third ruling: women praying together alone (without men) is makruh; they should pray individually. If they do form a congregation, the female imam stands in the middle of the row. Proofs include Aisha leading women standing in the middle, the hadith about rows (the worst rows for men are the last, but for women the best are the last), and Ali's statement that a woman should not lead. The Urdu summary reiterates the ruling.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): An action that is disliked; in this context, makruh tahrimi (close to haram) due to hadith threat, but prayer is valid.
جاز (jaza): It is permissible; the act is legally valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what is the status of the prayer if a Bedouin leads the congregation?
A) The prayer is invalid (batil).
B) The prayer is valid but it is disliked (makruh) for the Bedouin to lead.
C) The prayer is valid and recommended.
D) The prayer is valid only if the congregation is all Bedouins.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that while it is makruh to put forward a deficient person as imam, the prayer behind them remains valid, based on a balance of textual evidence.

Imam Shortening the Prayer
Ruling on imam shortening prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the imam should not lengthen the prayer and identify the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
The imam should be brief in prayer to accommodate the weak and needy.

This short passage from the congregation section emphasizes the importance of the imam considering the congregation's capacity. The Prophet's anger at those who cause aversion is a strong evidence for this etiquette. Let's analyze the hadith and the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended action for the imam.
The text says 'yambaghi li al-imam an la yutawwila bihim al-salat' — it is appropriate for the imam not to lengthen the prayer for them.
The term 'yambaghi' indicates a strong recommendation, not obligation.
2
Examine the proof: hadith of Abu Mas'ud.
A man complained that a particular imam lengthened the dawn prayer, causing him to delay. The Prophet became very angry and said 'Among you are those who cause aversion' and instructed brevity.
The Prophet's anger shows that lengthening is severely disliked.
3
Understand the rationale.
The Prophet mentioned reasons: the weak, the elderly, and those with needs. This establishes that the imam should consider the congregation's diversity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الجَمَاعَة
وَيُكْرَهُ تَقْدِيمُ الْعَبْدِ وَالْأَعْرَابِي وَالْفَاسِقِ وَوَلَدِ الزِّنَا وَالْأَعْمَى فَإِنْ تَقَدَّمُوا جَازَ وَيَنْبَغِي لِلْإِمَامِ أَنْ لَا يُطَوِّلَ بِهِمُ الصَّلَاةَ وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ أَنْ يُصَلِّينَ وَحْدَهُنَّ جَمَاعَةً فَإِنْ فَعَلْنَ وَقَفَتِ الْإِمَامَةُ وَسْطَهُنَّ.
وجه (١) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ تَقْدِيمُ الْعَبْدِ وَالْأَعْرَابِي عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَانَ يَقُولُ: «ثَلَاثَةٌ لَا يَقْبَلُ اللَّهُ مِنْهُمْ صَلَاةً، مَنْ تَقَدَّمَ قَوْمًا وَهُمْ لَهُ كَارِهُونَ» (سنن أبي داود، باب الرجل يؤم القوم وهم له كارهون، رقم ٦٨٥)
وجه (٢) قول الصحابية لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ تَقْدِيمُ الْعَبْدِ وَالْأَعْرَابِي: وَكَانَتْ عَائِشَةُ يَؤُمُّهَا عَبْدُهَا ذَكْوَانُ مِنَ الْمُصْحَفِ (صحيح البخاري، باب إمامة العبد والمولى، رقم ٦٩٢)
وجه (٣) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ تَقْدِيمُ الْعَبْدِ وَالْأَعْرَابِي: عَنْ عُبَيْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَدِيِّ بْنِ خِيَارٍ أَنَّهُ دَخَلَ عَلَى عُثْمَانَ بْنِ عَفَّانَ وَهُوَ مَحْصُورٌ فَقَالَ: إِنَّكَ إِمَامُ عَامَّةٍ وَنَزَلَ بِكَ مَا تَرَى وَيُصَلِّي لَنَا إِمَامُ فِتْنَةٍ وَنَتَحَرَّجُ؟ فَقَالَ: الصَّلَاةُ أَحْسَنُ مَا يَعْمَلُ النَّاسُ فَإِذَا أَحْسَنَ النَّاسُ فَأَحْسِنْ مَعَهُمْ وَإِذَا أَسَاءُوا فَاجْتَنِبْ إِسَاءَتَهُمْ (صحيح البخاري، باب إمامة المفتون والمبتدع، رقم ٦٩٥)
وجه (١) الحديث لثبوت وَيَنْبَغِي لِلْإِمَامِ أَنْ لَا يُطَوِّلَ بِهِمُ الصَّلَاةَ: أَخْبَرَنِي أَبُو مَسْعُودٍ أَنَّ رَجُلًا قَالَ: وَاللَّهِ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ إِنِّي لَأَتَأَخَّرُ عَنْ صَلَاةِ الْغَدَاةِ مِنْ أَجْلِ فُلَانٍ مِمَّا يُطِيلُ بِنَا فَمَا رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي مَوْعِظَةٍ أَشَدَّ غَضَبًا مِنْهُ يَوْمَئِذٍ ثُمَّ قَالَ: «إِنَّ مِنْكُمْ مُنَفِّرِينَ فَأَيُّكُمْ مَا صَلَّى بِالنَّاسِ فَلْيَتَجَوَّزْ فَإِنَّ فِيهِمُ الضَّعِيفَ وَالْكَبِيرَ وَذَا الْحَاجَةِ» (صحيح البخاري، باب تخفيف الإمام في القيام وإتمام الركوع والسجود، رقم ٧٠٢؛ مسلم، باب الدعاء في صلاة الليل وقيامه، رقم ٧٦٦)
وجه (١) قول الصحابية لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ أَنْ يُصَلِّينَ وَحْدَهُنَّ جَمَاعَةً: عَنْ رَيْطَةَ الْحَنَفِيَّةِ قَالَتْ: «أَمَّتْنَا عَائِشَةُ فَقَامَتْ بَيْنَهُنَّ فِي الصَّلَاةِ الْمَكْتُوبَةِ» (سنن الدارقطني، باب صلاة النساء جماعة وموقف إمامهن، رقم ١٥٠٧)
وجه (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ أَنْ يُصَلِّينَ وَحْدَهُنَّ جَمَاعَةً: عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «خَيْرُ صُفُوفِ الرِّجَالِ أَوَّلُهَا وَشَرُّهَا آخِرُهَا وَخَيْرُ صُفُوفِ النِّسَاءِ آخِرُهَا وَشَرُّهَا أَوَّلُهَا» (مسلم، باب تسوية الصفوف وإقامتها، رقم ١٤٤٠؛ سنن أبي داود، باب صف النساء وكراهية التأخر عن الصف الأول، رقم ٦٧٨)
وجه (٣) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ أَنْ يُصَلِّينَ وَحْدَهُنَّ جَمَاعَةً: عَنْ عَلِيٍّ قَالَ: «لَا تَؤُمُّ الْمَرْأَةُ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، من كره أن تؤم المرأة النساء، رقم ٤٩٥٧)
أصول: تنہا عورتوں کی جماعت مکروہ ہے، لہذا عورتیں تنہا ہوں یعنی مرد نہ ہو تو تنہا نماز پڑھے، جماعت نہیں، اور اگر تنہا جماعت کرے تو امام صف کے درمیان میں کھڑی ہو یعنی مردوں کی طرح مقتدی سے آگے نہیں۔
Section on Congregational Prayer. It is disliked to put forward a slave, a Bedouin, a sinner, an illegitimate child, and a blind person. If they do lead, it is permissible. It is appropriate for the imam not to lengthen the prayer for them. It is disliked for women to pray alone in congregation; if they do, the imam stands in the middle of them. Evidence (1) Hadith for the dislike of putting forward a slave and Bedouin: from Abdullah ibn Amr that the Messenger of Allah would say: 'Three persons whose prayer is not accepted: one who leads a people while they dislike him.' (2) Statement of a female companion: Aisha was led by her slave Dhakwan from the Mushaf. (3) Hadith: from Ubaydullah ibn Adi ibn Khiyar that he entered upon Uthman ibn Affan while he was besieged and said: You are the imam of the public, and this has happened to you; an imam of fitna leads us, should we refrain? He said: Prayer is the best of deeds; if people do good, do good with them; if they do evil, avoid their evil. Evidence for 'the imam should not lengthen the prayer': Abu Mas'ud informed me that a man said: By Allah, O Messenger of Allah, I am late for the morning prayer because of so-and-so who lengthens it; I never saw the Prophet more angry in a sermon; then he said: Among you are those who cause aversion; whoever leads people in prayer should be brief, for among them are the weak, the old, and those with needs. Evidence for 'it is disliked for women to pray alone in congregation': from Rayta al-Hanafiyya: Aisha led us, standing between us in the prescribed prayer. Also from Abu Huraira: The best rows for men are the first and the worst the last; the best rows for women are the last and the worst the first. Also from Ali: A woman should not lead. Principle: The congregation of women alone is disliked; therefore, women alone (without men) should pray individually, not in congregation. If they do form a congregation, the imam stands in the middle of the row, not ahead like for men.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof section on congregational prayer. The author first states the matn (core rulings) from Al-Quduri, then provides multiple proofs. The first ruling: it is makruh (disliked) to appoint a slave, Bedouin, open sinner, illegitimate child, or blind person as imam, but if they do lead, the prayer is valid (jaza). The Hanafi position is that these individuals are deficient in social status or religious character, so their imamate is disliked but not invalid. Proofs include a hadith that Allah does not accept the prayer of one who leads while disliked, but scholars interpret this as severe dislike; also Aisha being led by her slave shows permissibility. The second ruling: the imam should not lengthen the prayer; the hadith of Abu Mas'ud shows the Prophet's anger at those who make people flee. The third ruling: women praying together alone (without men) is makruh; they should pray individually. If they do form a congregation, the female imam stands in the middle of the row. Proofs include Aisha leading women standing in the middle, the hadith about rows (the worst rows for men are the last, but for women the best are the last), and Ali's statement that a woman should not lead. The Urdu summary reiterates the ruling.

Key Terms
ينبغي (yambaghi): It is appropriate or recommended; indicates a strong recommendation (mandub) but not obligation.
منفرين (munaffirin): Those who cause aversion; people who make others dislike something.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet say about imams who lengthen the prayer?
A) They will be rewarded for their devotion.
B) They are among those who cause aversion.
C) They should be removed from leadership.
D) They should only lead if asked.

Key Takeaway
The imam should be brief in prayer as a recommendation to accommodate the congregation, based on the Prophet's instruction.

Salah — Prayer

Women's Congregational Prayer
Ruling on women's congregation with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women praying in congregation alone (without men) and describe the positioning of the female imam.

Core Idea
Women praying alone in congregation is disliked; if they do, the imam stands in the middle.

This section addresses a specific scenario: women forming their own congregation without any men. The Hanafi ruling is that it is disliked, but if they do, the female imam stands in the middle of the row. The proofs include the practice of Aisha, the hadith on rows, and Ali's statement. Let's examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on women's congregation.
The text says 'yukrahu li al-nisa an yusallina wahdatahunna jama'atan' — it is disliked for women to pray alone in congregation (i.e., without men).
Dislike here is makruh tanzih (lightly disliked) according to later Hanafis.
2
State the permissibility if done.
'fa in fa'alna waqafat al-imamu wastahunna' — if they do, the imam stands in the middle of them.
This is a practical concession.
3
Analyze the first proof: Aisha leading women.
Rayta al-Hanafiyya reported that Aisha led them standing in the middle for the prescribed prayer. This shows permissibility and the positioning.
The middle position distinguishes from men's congregation where imam stands ahead.
4
Examine the second proof: hadith on rows.
The best rows for men are the first, worst the last; for women, best are the last, worst the first. This indicates women should be behind men, so their own congregation without men is not preferred.
5
Review the third proof: Ali's statement.
Ali said 'La ta'ummu al-mar'atu' — a woman should not lead. This supports the dislike.
Some interpret this as absolute prohibition, but Hanafis take it as dislike.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الجَمَاعَة
وَيُكْرَهُ تَقْدِيمُ الْعَبْدِ وَالْأَعْرَابِي وَالْفَاسِقِ وَوَلَدِ الزِّنَا وَالْأَعْمَى فَإِنْ تَقَدَّمُوا جَازَ وَيَنْبَغِي لِلْإِمَامِ أَنْ لَا يُطَوِّلَ بِهِمُ الصَّلَاةَ وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ أَنْ يُصَلِّينَ وَحْدَهُنَّ جَمَاعَةً فَإِنْ فَعَلْنَ وَقَفَتِ الْإِمَامَةُ وَسْطَهُنَّ.
وجه (١) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ تَقْدِيمُ الْعَبْدِ وَالْأَعْرَابِي عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَانَ يَقُولُ: «ثَلَاثَةٌ لَا يَقْبَلُ اللَّهُ مِنْهُمْ صَلَاةً، مَنْ تَقَدَّمَ قَوْمًا وَهُمْ لَهُ كَارِهُونَ» (سنن أبي داود، باب الرجل يؤم القوم وهم له كارهون، رقم ٦٨٥)
وجه (٢) قول الصحابية لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ تَقْدِيمُ الْعَبْدِ وَالْأَعْرَابِي: وَكَانَتْ عَائِشَةُ يَؤُمُّهَا عَبْدُهَا ذَكْوَانُ مِنَ الْمُصْحَفِ (صحيح البخاري، باب إمامة العبد والمولى، رقم ٦٩٢)
وجه (٣) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ تَقْدِيمُ الْعَبْدِ وَالْأَعْرَابِي: عَنْ عُبَيْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَدِيِّ بْنِ خِيَارٍ أَنَّهُ دَخَلَ عَلَى عُثْمَانَ بْنِ عَفَّانَ وَهُوَ مَحْصُورٌ فَقَالَ: إِنَّكَ إِمَامُ عَامَّةٍ وَنَزَلَ بِكَ مَا تَرَى وَيُصَلِّي لَنَا إِمَامُ فِتْنَةٍ وَنَتَحَرَّجُ؟ فَقَالَ: الصَّلَاةُ أَحْسَنُ مَا يَعْمَلُ النَّاسُ فَإِذَا أَحْسَنَ النَّاسُ فَأَحْسِنْ مَعَهُمْ وَإِذَا أَسَاءُوا فَاجْتَنِبْ إِسَاءَتَهُمْ (صحيح البخاري، باب إمامة المفتون والمبتدع، رقم ٦٩٥)
وجه (١) الحديث لثبوت وَيَنْبَغِي لِلْإِمَامِ أَنْ لَا يُطَوِّلَ بِهِمُ الصَّلَاةَ: أَخْبَرَنِي أَبُو مَسْعُودٍ أَنَّ رَجُلًا قَالَ: وَاللَّهِ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ إِنِّي لَأَتَأَخَّرُ عَنْ صَلَاةِ الْغَدَاةِ مِنْ أَجْلِ فُلَانٍ مِمَّا يُطِيلُ بِنَا فَمَا رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي مَوْعِظَةٍ أَشَدَّ غَضَبًا مِنْهُ يَوْمَئِذٍ ثُمَّ قَالَ: «إِنَّ مِنْكُمْ مُنَفِّرِينَ فَأَيُّكُمْ مَا صَلَّى بِالنَّاسِ فَلْيَتَجَوَّزْ فَإِنَّ فِيهِمُ الضَّعِيفَ وَالْكَبِيرَ وَذَا الْحَاجَةِ» (صحيح البخاري، باب تخفيف الإمام في القيام وإتمام الركوع والسجود، رقم ٧٠٢؛ مسلم، باب الدعاء في صلاة الليل وقيامه، رقم ٧٦٦)
وجه (١) قول الصحابية لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ أَنْ يُصَلِّينَ وَحْدَهُنَّ جَمَاعَةً: عَنْ رَيْطَةَ الْحَنَفِيَّةِ قَالَتْ: «أَمَّتْنَا عَائِشَةُ فَقَامَتْ بَيْنَهُنَّ فِي الصَّلَاةِ الْمَكْتُوبَةِ» (سنن الدارقطني، باب صلاة النساء جماعة وموقف إمامهن، رقم ١٥٠٧)
وجه (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ أَنْ يُصَلِّينَ وَحْدَهُنَّ جَمَاعَةً: عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «خَيْرُ صُفُوفِ الرِّجَالِ أَوَّلُهَا وَشَرُّهَا آخِرُهَا وَخَيْرُ صُفُوفِ النِّسَاءِ آخِرُهَا وَشَرُّهَا أَوَّلُهَا» (مسلم، باب تسوية الصفوف وإقامتها، رقم ١٤٤٠؛ سنن أبي داود، باب صف النساء وكراهية التأخر عن الصف الأول، رقم ٦٧٨)
وجه (٣) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ أَنْ يُصَلِّينَ وَحْدَهُنَّ جَمَاعَةً: عَنْ عَلِيٍّ قَالَ: «لَا تَؤُمُّ الْمَرْأَةُ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، من كره أن تؤم المرأة النساء، رقم ٤٩٥٧)
أصول: تنہا عورتوں کی جماعت مکروہ ہے، لہذا عورتیں تنہا ہوں یعنی مرد نہ ہو تو تنہا نماز پڑھے، جماعت نہیں، اور اگر تنہا جماعت کرے تو امام صف کے درمیان میں کھڑی ہو یعنی مردوں کی طرح مقتدی سے آگے نہیں۔
Section on Congregational Prayer. It is disliked to put forward a slave, a Bedouin, a sinner, an illegitimate child, and a blind person. If they do lead, it is permissible. It is appropriate for the imam not to lengthen the prayer for them. It is disliked for women to pray alone in congregation; if they do, the imam stands in the middle of them. Evidence (1) Hadith for the dislike of putting forward a slave and Bedouin: from Abdullah ibn Amr that the Messenger of Allah would say: 'Three persons whose prayer is not accepted: one who leads a people while they dislike him.' (2) Statement of a female companion: Aisha was led by her slave Dhakwan from the Mushaf. (3) Hadith: from Ubaydullah ibn Adi ibn Khiyar that he entered upon Uthman ibn Affan while he was besieged and said: You are the imam of the public, and this has happened to you; an imam of fitna leads us, should we refrain? He said: Prayer is the best of deeds; if people do good, do good with them; if they do evil, avoid their evil. Evidence for 'the imam should not lengthen the prayer': Abu Mas'ud informed me that a man said: By Allah, O Messenger of Allah, I am late for the morning prayer because of so-and-so who lengthens it; I never saw the Prophet more angry in a sermon; then he said: Among you are those who cause aversion; whoever leads people in prayer should be brief, for among them are the weak, the old, and those with needs. Evidence for 'it is disliked for women to pray alone in congregation': from Rayta al-Hanafiyya: Aisha led us, standing between us in the prescribed prayer. Also from Abu Huraira: The best rows for men are the first and the worst the last; the best rows for women are the last and the worst the first. Also from Ali: A woman should not lead. Principle: The congregation of women alone is disliked; therefore, women alone (without men) should pray individually, not in congregation. If they do form a congregation, the imam stands in the middle of the row, not ahead like for men.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof section on congregational prayer. The author first states the matn (core rulings) from Al-Quduri, then provides multiple proofs. The first ruling: it is makruh (disliked) to appoint a slave, Bedouin, open sinner, illegitimate child, or blind person as imam, but if they do lead, the prayer is valid (jaza). The Hanafi position is that these individuals are deficient in social status or religious character, so their imamate is disliked but not invalid. Proofs include a hadith that Allah does not accept the prayer of one who leads while disliked, but scholars interpret this as severe dislike; also Aisha being led by her slave shows permissibility. The second ruling: the imam should not lengthen the prayer; the hadith of Abu Mas'ud shows the Prophet's anger at those who make people flee. The third ruling: women praying together alone (without men) is makruh; they should pray individually. If they do form a congregation, the female imam stands in the middle of the row. Proofs include Aisha leading women standing in the middle, the hadith about rows (the worst rows for men are the last, but for women the best are the last), and Ali's statement that a woman should not lead. The Urdu summary reiterates the ruling.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; here makruh tanzih (lightly disliked).
وسط (wast): Middle; the female imam stands in the middle of the row, not ahead.

According to the passage, where should the female imam stand when leading women in congregation?

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Positioning Followers in Congregational Prayer
Rulings on where followers stand

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended positioning of one or two followers relative to the imam and cite the supporting hadiths.

Core Idea
One follower stands to the imam's right; two followers stand behind the imam.

When you pray in congregation, where you stand matters. The Prophet (peace be upon him) taught specific positions to maintain order. This lesson covers the sunnah positioning for one or two followers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for one follower
Find the statement: 'wa man salla ma'a wahidin aqamahu 'an yaminih' – he places him on his right.
This is a recommended act, not obligatory.
2
Identify the ruling for two followers
Find: 'fa in kana ithnayni taqaddama 'alayhima' – he steps forward, and they stand behind.
The imam goes ahead, followers form a row behind.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
For one follower: Ibn Abbas hadith (Bukhari) where the Prophet placed him on his right. For two: Anas hadith (Bukhari) where he, an orphan, and Umm Sulaim prayed behind the Prophet, indicating the imam ahead.
These actions establish the sunnah.
4
Understand the legal status
These positions are mustahabb (recommended) in the Hanafi school, not fard or wajib.
Deviating does not invalidate the prayer but contradicts the better practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ صَلَّى مَعَ وَاحِدٍ أَقَامَهُ عَنْ يَمِينِهِ فَإِنْ كَانَا اثْنَيْنِ تَقَدَّمَ عَلَيْهِمَا وَلَا يَجُوزُ لِلرِّجَالِ أَنْ يَقْتَدُوا بِامْرَأَةٍ وَلَا بِصَبِيٍّ.
رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: خَيْرُ صُفُوفِ الرِّجَالِ أَوَّلُهَا وَشَرُّهَا آخِرُهَا وَخَيْرُ صُفُوفِ النِّسَاءِ آخِرُهَا وَشَرُّهَا أَوَّلُهَا. (مسلم، باب تسوية الصفوف، رقم ١٤٤٠؛ سنن أبي داود، باب صف النساء، رقم ٦٧٨)
وجه (١) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ صَلَّى مَعَ وَاحِدٍ أَقَامَهُ عَنْ يَمِينِهِ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: صَلَّيْتُ مَعَ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ ذَاتَ لَيْلَةٍ فَقُمْتُ عَنْ يَسَارِهِ فَأَخَذَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ بِرَأْسِي مِنْ وَرَائِي فَجَعَلَنِي عَنْ يَمِينِهِ (صحيح البخاري، باب إذا قام الرجل عن يسار الإمام، رقم ٧٢٦)
وجه (١) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ كَانَا اثْنَيْنِ تَقَدَّمَ عَلَيْهِمَا: عَنْ أَنَسِ بْنِ مَالِكٍ قَالَ: صَلَّيْتُ أَنَا وَيَتِيمٌ فِي بَيْتِنَا خَلْفَ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَأُمِّي أُمُّ سُلَيْمٍ خَلْفَنَا (صحيح البخاري، باب المرأة وحدها تكون صفًا، رقم ٧٢٧؛ سنن أبي داود، باب إذا كانوا ثلاثة كيف يقومون، رقم ٦١٢)
وجه (٢) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ كَانَا اثْنَيْنِ تَقَدَّمَ عَلَيْهِمَا: قَالَ: اسْتَأْذَنَ عَلْقَمَةُ وَالْأَسْوَدُ عَلَى عَبْدِ اللَّهِ وَقَدْ كُنَّا أَطَلْنَا الْقُعُودَ عَلَى بَابِهِ فَخَرَجَتِ الْجَارِيَةُ فَاسْتَأْذَنَتْ لَهُمَا فَأَذِنَ فَهُمَا ثُمَّ قَامَ فَصَلَّى بَيْنِي وَبَيْنَهُ ثُمَّ قَالَ: هَكَذَا رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَعَلَ (سنن أبي داود، باب إذا كانوا ثلاثة كيف يقومون، رقم ٦١٣)
وجه (١) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَجُوزُ لِلرِّجَالِ أَنْ يَقْتَدُوا بِامْرَأَةٍ: عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: خَيْرُ صُفُوفِ الرِّجَالِ أَوَّلُهَا وَشَرُّهَا آخِرُهَا وَخَيْرُ صُفُوفِ النِّسَاءِ آخِرُهَا وَشَرُّهَا أَوَّلُهَا (مسلم، باب تسوية الصفوف، رقم ١٤٤٠)
أصول: مرد حضرات کی نماز عورت اور غیر مکلف مثلا نا بالغ کی اقتدا میں درست نہیں ہے۔
And whoever prays with one person, he places him on his right. If there are two, he steps forward of them. It is not permissible for men to follow a woman or a minor. The Messenger of Allah said: The best rows of men are the first and the worst are the last, and the best rows of women are the last and the worst are the first. Evidence for 'whoever prays with one person, he places him on his right': from Ibn Abbas: I prayed with the Prophet one night and stood on his left; he took me by the head from behind and placed me on his right. Evidence for 'if there are two, he steps forward': from Anas ibn Malik: I and an orphan prayed in our house behind the Prophet, and my mother Umm Sulaim behind us. Another evidence: Alqamah and al-Aswad requested permission to enter upon Abdullah, and we had sat long at his door; a young girl came out and sought permission for them; he allowed them; then he stood and prayed between me and him, then said: Thus I saw the Messenger of Allah do. Evidence for 'men may not follow a woman': from Abu Huraira: The best rows for men... Principle: The prayer of men is not valid behind a woman or a non-mature person, such as a minor.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof section continuing the chapter on congregational prayer. It covers two main rulings: (1) Positioning of followers: if one person prays with the imam, he stands to the imam's right. If two persons pray with the imam, the imam steps forward and they stand behind him in a row. The hadith of Ibn Abbas shows the single follower on the right; the hadith of Anas and of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud show that with two or more, the imam goes forward. (2) It is not permissible for men to follow a woman or a child (non-mature) in prayer. The proof is the hadith about the best rows, which implies that women belong at the back, and also the general principle that women cannot lead men. The Urdu clearly states that men's prayer is not valid behind a woman or a non-mature person. The Hanafi position is that a woman or a boy who has not reached puberty cannot lead men in prayer because they lack the proper authority (wilaya).

Key Terms
صَف (saff): Row in congregational prayer.
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the imam in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should the imam do if he has two followers?
A) He remains in front and they stand behind him in a row.
B) He steps forward, leaving the followers behind.
C) He places one on his right and one on his left.
D) He steps back and they stand on either side.

Key Takeaway
Follow the Prophet's way: one follower on the right, two followers behind the imam.

Prohibition of Men Following Women or Minors in Prayer
Ruling on impermissibility of men following women or minors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why men may not follow a woman or a non-mature boy in prayer and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Only a mature male can lead men; a woman or minor invalidates the prayer.

The imam must be a mature male. This lesson explores the evidence for why women and minors cannot lead men, and the consequences of doing so.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Locate the statement: 'wa la yajuzu li al-rijali an yaqtadu bi imra'atin wa la bi sabiyyin' - it is not permissible for men to follow a woman or a minor.
This is a clear prohibition.
2
Identify the hadith evidence
The hadith: 'Khairu sufufi al-rijali awwaluha...' (best rows for men first, worst last; best rows for women last, worst first) is cited as evidence.
This hadith is from Sahih Muslim and others.
3
Understand the face of evidence (wajh al-dalalah)
The hadith places women's best rows at the back, indicating they should not be in front of men. Hence, a woman cannot lead men, as the imam is at the front.
For minors, they lack full responsibility and authority.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'i school also prohibits women leading men, but permits a discerning minor boy (mumayyiz) if his recitation is good.
Hanafis reject this; a non-mature person cannot lead.

رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: خَيْرُ صُفُوفِ الرِّجَالِ أَوَّلُهَا وَشَرُّهَا آخِرُهَا وَخَيْرُ صُفُوفِ النِّسَاءِ آخِرُهَا وَشَرُّهَا أَوَّلُهَا. (مسلم، باب تسوية الصفوف، رقم ١٤٤٠؛ سنن أبي داود، باب صف النساء، رقم ٦٧٨)

وجه (١) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ كَانَا اثْنَيْنِ تَقَدَّمَ عَلَيْهِمَا: عَنْ أَنَسِ بْنِ مَالِكٍ قَالَ: صَلَّيْتُ أَنَا وَيَتِيمٌ فِي بَيْتِنَا خَلْفَ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَأُمِّي أُمُّ سُلَيْمٍ خَلْفَنَا (صحيح البخاري، باب المرأة وحدها تكون صفًا، رقم ٧٢٧؛ سنن أبي داود، باب إذا كانوا ثلاثة كيف يقومون، رقم ٦١٢)
وجه (٢) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ كَانَا اثْنَيْنِ تَقَدَّمَ عَلَيْهِمَا: قَالَ: اسْتَأْذَنَ عَلْقَمَةُ وَالْأَسْوَدُ عَلَى عَبْدِ اللَّهِ وَقَدْ كُنَّا أَطَلْنَا الْقُعُودَ عَلَى بَابِهِ فَخَرَجَتِ الْجَارِيَةُ فَاسْتَأْذَنَتْ لَهُمَا فَأَذِنَ فَهُمَا ثُمَّ قَامَ فَصَلَّى بَيْنِي وَبَيْنَهُ ثُمَّ قَالَ: هَكَذَا رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَعَلَ (سنن أبي داود، باب إذا كانوا ثلاثة كيف يقومون، رقم ٦١٣)

Row Arrangement and Invalidation Due to Adjacent Woman
Ruling with two hadith and a companion narration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on row order in congregational prayer and apply the condition under which a man's prayer becomes invalid due to an adjacent woman.

Core Idea
A woman beside a man in the same row invalidates his prayer, not hers, per Hanafi school.

This passage from Al-Quduri addresses two interconnected rulings: the proper arrangement of rows in congregational prayer and the effect of a woman standing directly beside a man. The Hanafi school holds that men must stand first, then boys, then women, and if a woman stands beside a man in the same prayer, the man's prayer becomes invalid. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proofs, and the cross-madhhab difference with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the row order ruling
Read the matn statement: 'And he arranges the men, then the boys, then the women.' Understand that this establishes a hierarchical order in congregational prayer rows.
The order is based on age and gender, with the most virtuous (men) in front.
2
State the invalidation rule
Find the clause: 'if a woman stands beside a man... she spoils his prayer.' Note that the invalidation applies only to the man, not the woman, and requires both to be in the same prayer (mushtarikan).
The ruling is specific to a woman directly adjacent (beside) the man, not behind.
3
Analyze the proofs (dalil)
Examine the two hadith for row order (from Anas and Abu Hurayrah) and the narration from Ghudayf for the invalidation. The hadith from Anas shows the Prophet's practice; the hadith from Abu Hurayrah praises women's last rows; the narration advises a barrier between a man and his wife.
These proofs are classified as Sunnah ahad (single-route) and Qawl Sahabi (companion's statement).
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Contrast the Hanafi position (man's prayer invalid) with the Shafi'i position (prayer valid but disliked). Understand that the thamarah (practical consequence) is whether the man must repeat his prayer.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الجَمَاعَة
وَيَصُفُ الرِّجَالَ ثُمَّ الصَّبْيَانَ ثُمَّ النِّسَاءَ ١٠ فَإِنْ قَامَتْ امْرَأَةٌ إلى جَانِبِ رَجُلٍ وَهُمَا مُشْتَرِكَانِ فِي صَلَاةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ أَفْسَدَتْ عَلَيْهِ صَلَاتُهُ
وجه (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَيَصُفُ الرِّجَالَ ثُمَّ الصَّبْيَانَ ثُمَّ النِّسَاءُ عَنْ أَنَسِ بْنِ مَالِكٍ قَالَ: صَلَّيْتُ أَنَا وَيَتِيمَ فِي بَيْتِنَا، خَلْفَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم، وَأُمِّي أُمُّ سُلَيْمٍ خَلْفَنَا.
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَيَصُفُ الرِّجَالَ ثُمَّ الصَّبْيَانَ ثُمَّ النِّسَاءُ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ؛ قَالَ: قَالَ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: خَيْرُ صُفُوفِ الرِّجَالِ أَوَّلُهَا. وَشَرُّهَا آخِرُهَا وَخَيْرُ صُفُوفِ النِّسَاءِ آخِرُهَا. وَشَرُّهَا أَوَّلُهَا.
وجه : (۱) قول التابعي لثبوت فَإِنْ قَامَتْ امْرَأَةٌ إِلَى جَانِبِ رَجُلٍ وَهُمَا مُشْتَرِكَانِ عَنْ غُضَيْفِ بنِ الْحَارِثِ قَالَ: قُلْتُ لِأَمِيرِ الْمُؤْمِنَينَ: إِنَّا نَبْدُو فَإِنْ خَرَجْتُ قُرِرْتُ، وَإِنْ خَرَجَتِ امْرَأَتِي قُرَّتْ قَالَ: «فَاقْطَعْ بَيْنَكَ وَبَيْنَهَا بِتَوبٍ، ثُمَّ صَلِ وَلْتُصَلِّ» يَعْنِي اقْطَعْ فِي الْخَبَاءِ.
Chapter on Congregation. And he arranges the men, then the boys, then the women. Then if a woman stands beside a man while both are sharing in one prayer, she spoils his prayer. Aspect (1) the hadith for the proof of 'And he arranges the men, then the boys, then the women': from Anas ibn Malik who said: I prayed with an orphan in our house behind the Prophet (peace be upon him), and my mother Umm Sulaym was behind us. Aspect (2) the hadith for the proof of the same: from Abu Hurayrah who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: The best of men's rows is the first, and the worst is the last; and the best of women's rows is the last, and the worst is the first. Aspect (1) the saying of a Tabi'i for the proof of 'if a woman stands beside a man while both are sharing': from Ghudayf ibn al-Harith who said: I said to the Commander of the Faithful: We go out to the desert; if I stay, I stay, and if my wife goes out, she stays. He said: 'Then place a cloth between you and her, then pray and let her pray.' Meaning, place a partition in the tent.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on the arrangement of rows in congregational prayer and the specific case where a woman stands adjacent to a man. The matn states that men stand first, then boys, then women. If a woman stands directly beside a man while both are in the same prayer, it invalidates the man's prayer. This is a ruling from the Hanafi school. The commentary then provides three proofs: two hadith for the row arrangement, and one narration (athar) from a companion (interpreted as a Tabi'i saying) for the invalidation ruling. The hadith from Anas shows the practice of the Prophet with men, an orphan, and a woman behind. The hadith from Abu Hurayrah emphasizes the virtue of the first row for men and the last row for women, implying separation. The narration from Ghudayf advises creating a barrier (like a cloth) between a man and his wife when praying together, indicating that direct adjacency is problematic. The Hanafi school holds that the man's prayer becomes invalid if a woman stands beside him in the same row without a barrier, as per the principle that proximity of a woman to a man in prayer disturbs the concentration and is akin to an impurity (hukm al-taharah). The ruling applies only to the man, not the woman.

Key Terms
صف (saff): A row in congregational prayer; the order of standing.
مشتركان (mushtarikan): Both participants sharing in the same congregational prayer.
أفسدت (afsadat): She spoils/invalidates (the man's prayer).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a woman stands beside a man in the same row during congregational prayer, what happens to their prayers?
A) Both prayers become invalid.
B) The man's prayer becomes invalid, but the woman's remains valid.
C) The woman's prayer becomes invalid, but the man's remains valid.
D) Both prayers are valid, though it is disliked.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a man's prayer is invalidated if a woman stands directly beside him in the same row without a barrier, while the woman's prayer remains valid.

Women Attending Congregational Prayer: Dislike and Exceptions
Ruling with proof for women's mosque attendance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women attending congregational prayers, identify the exceptions, and cite the key proofs from the hadith.

Core Idea
Women's mosque attendance is disliked due to fitnah, but old women may attend certain prayers without adornment.

This passage from Al-Quduri presents the Hanafi position on women and congregational prayers. The matn declares a general dislike for women attending, but makes an exception for old women (ajuz) who may attend Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, Jumu'ah, and Eid prayers. The commentary then provides multiple proofs: three hadith supporting the general dislike, and additional proofs – including a hadith and a companion statement – supporting the exception. Understanding this ruling requires balancing explicit prophetic permissions with the school's emphasis on preventing fitnah (temptation).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its categories
Start by extracting the matn's ruling: 'it is disliked for women to attend congregations'. Note that Hanafi jurists differentiate between young women (makruh tahrimi) and old women (makruh tanzihi, permissible with conditions). Recognize the exception for old women and the specific prayers mentioned.
The matn uses the term 'yukrah' indicating karahah (dislike). Later Hanafi works clarify the degree.
2
Examine the proofs for the general ruling
The commentary cites three ahadith: (1) Aisha's statement that the Prophet would have prevented women due to later innovations, (2) the hadith that a woman's best prayer is in her innermost chamber, and (3) the hadith allowing women to go to mosques but without perfume. Analyze how each proof supports the ruling of dislike.
The third hadith is often cited by opponents; note the condition 'tafilat' (without perfume).
3
Analyze the proofs for the exception
The exception for old women is supported by (1) a hadith prohibiting women wearing incense from attending Isha, implying that old women without perfume may attend, (2) Ibn Mas'ud's statement explicitly excepting old women, and (3) the hadith not to prevent women from mosques if they ask permission. Understand how these limit the general ruling.
Ibn Mas'ud's statement also excludes the two noble mosques from the general preference for home prayer.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The commentary ends with the principle (asl): 'Women's prayer at home is appropriate; going to the mosque is disliked due to fear of fitnah.' This highlights the school's reliance on the concept of fitnah as the operative cause (illa) for the ruling.
The exception for old women is based on their reduced potential for fitnah and the need for them to attend loud prayers where they can be heard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ حُضُورُ الْجَمَاعَاتِ الصَّفِ الأَوَّلِ وَالْمُسَابَقَةِ إِلَيْهَا، وَتَقْدِيم أُولِي الْفَضْلِ وَتَقْرِيبِهِمْ مِنَ الإِمَامِ
وَلَا بَأْسَ أَنْ تَخْرُجَ الْعَجُوزُ فِي الْفَجْرِ وَالْمَغْرِبِ وَالْعِشَاءِ وَالْجُمُعَةِ وَالْعِيدَيْنِ
وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ حُضُورُ الْجَمَاعَاتِ أَنَّهَا سَمِعَتْ عَائِشَةَ زَوْجَ النَّبِيِّ تَقُولُ: لَوْ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم رَأَى مَا أَحْدَثَ النِّسَاءُ لَمَنَعَهُنَّ الْمَسْجِدَ كَمَا مُنِعَتْ نِسَاءُ بَنِي إِسْرَائِيلَ
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ حُضُورُ الْجَمَاعَاتِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «صَلَاةُ الْمَرْأَةِ فِي بَيْتِهَا أَفْضَلُ مِنْ صَلَاتِهَا فِي حُجْرَتِهَا، وَصَلَاتُهَا فِي مَخْدَعِهَا أَفْضَلُ مِنْ صَلَاتِهَا فِي بَيْتِهَا»
وجه: (٣) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ حُضُورُ الْجَمَاعَاتِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لَا تَمْنَعُوا إِمَاءَ اللَّهِ مَسَاجِدَ اللَّهِ، وَلَكِنْ لِيَخْرُجْنَ وَهُنَّ تَفِلَاتٌ»
وجه : (١) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ أَنْ تَخْرُجَ الْعَجُوزُ فِي الْفَجْرِ عَنْ أَبِي هريرة؛ قال: قال رسول الله الله "أَيُّمَا امْرَأَةٍ أَصَابَتْ بَخُورًا، فَلَا تشهد معنا العشاء الآخرة"
وجه : (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ أَنْ تَخْرُجَ الْعَجُوزُ فِي الْفَجْرِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ قَالَ: " وَالَّذِي لَا إِلَهَ غَيْرُهُ، مَا صَلَّتِ امْرَأَةٌ صَلَاةً خَيْرًا لَهَا مِنْ صَلَاةٍ تُصَلِّيهَا فِي بَيْتِهَا إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَسْجِدَ الْحَرَامِ أَوْ مَسْجِدَ الرَّسُولِهِ ، إِلَّا عَجُوزًا فِي مَنْقَلِهَا "
وجه: (3) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ أَنْ تَخْرُجَ الْعَجُوزُ فِي الْفَجْرِ أن عبد الله بن عمر قال : سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: "لا تمنعوا نسائكم الْمَسَاجِدَ إِذَا اسْتَأْذَنَّكُمْ إِلَيْهَا". قَالَ فَقَالَ بِلَالُ بْنُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ : وَاللَّهِ! لَنَمْنَعُهُنَّ
اصول : خواتین کی نماز گھروں میں مناسب ہے ، مسجد میں جانا مکروہ ہے فتنے کے اندیشہ سے۔
And it is disliked for women to attend congregations, [striving for] the first row and racing to it, and giving precedence to people of virtue and bringing them near the imam. And there is no harm for an old woman to go out for Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, Jumu'ah, and the two Eids. Aspect (1) the hadith for the proof of 'it is disliked for women to attend congregations': that she heard Aisha, the wife of the Prophet, saying: If the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) saw what women have innovated, he would have prevented them from the mosque as the women of Bani Israel were prevented. Aspect (2) the hadith for its proof: from Abdullah, from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: A woman's prayer in her house is better than her prayer in her courtyard, and her prayer in her inner chamber is better than her prayer in her house. Aspect (3) the hadith for its proof: from Abu Hurayrah that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Do not prevent the female servants of Allah from the mosques of Allah, but let them go out without perfume. Aspect (1) the hadith for the proof of 'there is no harm for an old woman to go out for Fajr': from Abu Hurayrah who said: The Messenger of Allah said: Any woman who applies incense, let her not attend the Isha prayer with us. Aspect (2) the saying of the companion for its proof: from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud who said: By Him besides whom there is no god, no woman has prayed a prayer better for her than a prayer she prays in her house, unless it be in the Masjid al-Haram or the Masjid of the Messenger, except an old woman in her going out. Aspect (3) the hadith for its proof: that Abdullah ibn Umar said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: Do not prevent your women from the mosques if they ask your permission to go. He said: Then Bilal ibn Abdullah said: By Allah, we will prevent them. Principle: Women's prayer at home is appropriate; going to the mosque is disliked due to fear of fitnah.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling on women attending congregational prayers. The matn states that it is disliked (makruh) for women to attend congregations, especially seeking the first row and racing to it. However, there is an exception for old women (ajuz) who may attend Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, Jumu'ah, and the two Eid prayers without harm. The commentary provides multiple proofs: Aisha's statement that the Prophet would have prevented women from mosques due to later innovations; a hadith that a woman's best prayer is in the innermost part of her house; a hadith allowing women to go to the mosque but without perfume; a hadith prohibiting women wearing perfume from attending Isha; Ibn Mas'ud's statement emphasizing home prayer except for old women; and the hadith not to prevent women from mosques if they ask permission, with Bilal's opposition. The principle (asl) concludes that women's prayer at home is appropriate, and going to the mosque is disliked due to fear of fitnah. The Hanafi school distinguishes between old women (who may attend certain loud prayers) and young women (who are discouraged due to fitnah). The ruling is that attending is makruh tahrimi for young women and makruh tanzihi for old women under specific conditions.

Key Terms
كراهة (karahah): Legal dislike; an act that is not sinful but discouraged.
عجوز (ajuz): An old woman past the age of desirability.
فتنة (fitnah): Trial, temptation, especially sexual temptation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented, which women may attend congregational prayers without harm?
A) All women, as long as they ask permission.
B) Only young women who are not married.
C) Old women (ajuz) for Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, Jumu'ah, and Eid prayers.
D) Women who wear perfume and fine clothes.

Key Takeaway
Women's mosque attendance is disliked due to fitnah, but exceptions exist for old women without adornment for certain prayers.

Old Women Attending Congregational Prayers: Ruling and Proofs
Ruling on old women attending mosque with hadith proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on old women attending congregational prayers, identify the supporting hadith proofs, and explain the conditions for permissibility.

Core Idea
An old woman, no longer a source of fitnah, may attend congregational prayers without perfume.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on female attendance in mosques, focusing on the exception for elderly women. Al-Quduri's matn permits old women to attend certain congregational prayers, and the commentator brings multiple hadith proofs to support this position. Understanding the conditions and evidence will clarify the nuanced Hanafi view on women in mosques.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Note the specific prayers listed (Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, Jumu'ah, two Eids) and the category of woman (al-ajuz). The ruling is permissibility (la ba'sa), not recommendation.
2
Examine the proofs
The commentator provides several hadith and a companion statement. Key hadith: 'Do not prevent the female servants of Allah... but let them go out not wearing perfume.' This establishes general permissibility with conditions.
3
Understand the Hanafi differentiation
The prohibition or discouragement for young women is due to fitnah; the exception for old women is because they are no longer a source of temptation. The Urdu principle clarifies 'an old and desolate woman in whom there is no desire.'
4
Synthesize the conditions
The permissibility is contingent on avoiding adornment: no perfume, no colorful clothes, no fitnah. This aligns with the hadith condition 'tafilat' (not perfumed).
5
Recognize cross-madhhab difference
Some schools allow all women to attend mosques unconditionally, while Hanafis restrict it. The difference stems from weighing the hadith 'Do not prevent' against the general principle of avoiding fitnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الجَمَاعَة
وَلَا بَأْسَ أَنْ تَخْرُجَ الْعَجُوزُ فِي الْفَجْرِ وَالْمَغْرِبِ وَالْعِشَاءِ وَالْجُمُعَةِ وَالْعِيدَيْنِ تَقُولُ: لَوْ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم رَأَى مَا أَحْدَثَ النِّسَاءُ لَمَنَعَهُنَّ الْمَسْجِدَ كَمَا مُنِعَتْ نِسَاءُ بَنِي إِسْرَائِيلَ قَالَ فَقُلْتُ لِعَمْرَةَ : أَنِسَاءُ بَنِي إِسْرَائِيلَ مُنِعْنَ الْمَسْجِدَ ؟ قَالَتْ: نعم،(مسلم شریف، باب خُرُوجِ النِّسَاءِ إِلَى الْمَسَاجِدِ إِذَا لَمْ يَتَرَتَّبْ عَلَيْهِ فِتْنَةٌ، وَأَنَّهَا لَا تَخْرُجْ مُطَيِّبَةً، رقم 445\ سنن ابوداود، بَابُ التَّشْدِيدِ فِي ذَلِكَ، رقم 569)
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ حُضُورُ الْجَمَاعَاتِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «صَلَاةُ الْمَرْأَةِ فِي بَيْتِهَا أَفْضَلُ مِنْ صَلَاتِهَا فِي حُجْرَتِهَا، وَصَلَاتُهَا فِي مَخْدَعِهَا أَفْضَلُ مِنْ صَلَاتِهَا فِي بَيْتِهَا» ( سنن ابوداود، بَابُ التَّشْدِيدِ فِي ذَلِكَ، رقم 569)
وجه: (٣) الحديث لثبوت وَيُكْرَهُ لِلنِّسَاءِ حُضُورُ الْجَمَاعَاتِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لَا تَمْنَعُوا إِمَاءَ اللَّهِ مَسَاجِدَ اللَّهِ، وَلَكِنْ لِيَخْرُجْنَ وَهُنَّ تَفِلَاتٌ» ( سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الخُرُوجِ النِّسَاءِ إِلَى الْمَسْجِدِ، رقم 1565)
وجه : (١) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ أَنْ تَخْرُجَ الْعَجُوزُ فِي الْفَجْرِ \ عَنْ أَبِي هريرة؛ قال: قال رسول الله الله "أَيُّمَا امْرَأَةٍ أَصَابَتْ بَخُورًا، فَلَا تشهد معنا العشاء الآخرة" (مسلم شريف، باب خُرُوجِ النِّسَاءِ إِلَى الْمَسَاجِدِ إِذَا لَمْ يَتَرَتَّبْ عَلَيْهِ فِتْنَةٌ، وَأَنَّهَا لَا تَخْرُجْ مُطَيِّبَةً، رقم 444) وجه : (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ أَنْ تَخْرُجَ الْعَجُوزُ فِي الْفَجْرِ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ قَالَ: " وَالَّذِي لَا إِلَهَ غَيْرُهُ، مَا صَلَّتِ امْرَأَةٌ صَلَاةً خَيْرًا لَهَا مِنْ صَلَاةٍ تُصَلِّيهَا فِي بَيْتِهَا إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَسْجِدَ الْحَرَامِ أَوْ مَسْجِدَ الرَّسُولِهِ ، إِلَّا عَجُوزًا فِي مَنْقَلِهَا "(السنن الكبري للبيقهي، بَابُ خَيْرِ مَسَاجِدِ النِّسَاءِ قَعْرُ بُيُوتِهِنَّ ، رقم 5364)
وجه: (3) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا بَأْسَ أَنْ تَخْرُجَ الْعَجُوزُ فِي الْفَجْرِ \ أن عبد الله بن عمر قال : سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: "لا تمنعوا نسائكم الْمَسَاجِدَ إِذَا اسْتَأْذَنَّكُمْ إِلَيْهَا". قَالَ فَقَالَ بِلَالُ بْنُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ : وَاللَّهِ! لَنَمْنَعُهُنَّ، (مسلم شریف ، باب خُرُوجِ النِّسَاءِ إِلَى الْمَسَاجِدِ إِذَا لَمْ يَتَرَتَّبْ عَلَيْهِ فِتْنَةٌ، وَأَنَّهَا لا تَخْرُجْ مُطَيِّبَةً، رقم (442)
اصول : ایسی بوڑھی اور کھوسٹھ عورت جس میں رغبت نہ ہو وہ تمام جہری نمازوں میں شرکت کر سکتی ہیں بشر طیکہ خوشبو اور بھر کیلے کپڑے زیب تن نہ کی ہوں۔
Chapter on Congregation. There is no harm for an old woman to go out for Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, Friday, and the two Eids. She says: If the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) had seen what women have innovated, he would have prevented them from the mosque as the women of Banu Israel were prevented. He said: I said to Amra: Were the women of Banu Israel prevented from the mosque? She said: Yes. (Muslim, Chapter: Women going out to mosques when no fitnah results, and that she should not go out perfumed, no. 445; Abu Dawud, Chapter: Severity regarding that, no. 569) Proof: (2) The hadith establishing it is disliked for women to attend congregations: from Abdullah, from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'A woman's prayer in her house is better than her prayer in her courtyard, and her prayer in her inner chamber is better than her prayer in her house.' (Abu Dawud, Chapter: Severity regarding that, no. 569) Proof: (3) The hadith establishing it is disliked for women to attend congregations: from Abu Huraira, that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not prevent the female servants of Allah from the mosques of Allah, but let them go out not wearing perfume.' (Abu Dawud, Chapter: What has come about women going out to the mosque, no. 1565) Proof: (1) The hadith establishing 'there is no harm for an old woman to go out for Fajr': from Abu Huraira; he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Any woman who applies incense, let her not attend the night prayer with us.' (Muslim, no. 444) Proof: (2) The statement of a Companion establishing 'there is no harm for an old woman to go out for Fajr': from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud who said: 'By Him besides whom there is no deity, a woman has not prayed a prayer better for her than a prayer she prays in her house, except that it be the Sacred Mosque or the Mosque of the Messenger, except an old woman in her house.' (Baihaqi, no. 5364) Proof: (3) The hadith establishing 'there is no harm for an old woman to go out for Fajr': that Abdullah ibn Umar said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'Do not prevent your women from the mosques if they ask your permission.' He said: Bilal ibn Abdullah said: By Allah! We will prevent them. (Muslim, no. 442) Principle: An old and desolate woman in whom there is no desire can participate in all loud prayers, provided she does not wear perfume or colorful clothes.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This is a passage of rulings with proofs from Al-Quduri's matn, expanded by the commentator with supporting hadith. The main ruling states that it is permissible (la ba'sa) for an old woman (al-ajuz, an elderly woman past childbearing age and no longer an object of desire) to go out and attend the following congregational prayers: Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, Jumu'ah, and the two Eid prayers. The commentator then provides multiple proofs. First, a hadith from Aisha (radiyallahu anha) indirectly supports the permissibility for old women, as she expressed that if the Prophet saw what women later innovated, he would have prevented them, implying that before such innovations, it was allowed. Another hadith from Abdullah (ibn Mas'ud or ibn Umar) states that a woman's prayer in her house is superior, but it doesn't forbid the mosque entirely. Another hadith from Abu Huraira instructs not to prevent women from mosques but they should go out without perfume. The commentator also cites a statement of Ibn Mas'ud that no prayer is better for a woman than in her house except for the two sacred mosques, and except an old woman in her house (meaning an old woman may be an exception). Finally, a hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar commands not to prevent women from mosques if they ask permission. The Urdu principle concludes: an old, unattractive woman may participate in all loud (jahri) prayers provided she does not wear perfume or colorful clothes. This is the Hanafi position: for women who are not a source of fitnah, attendance is permissible, but for young women it is discouraged.

Key Terms
العجوز (al-ajuz): An old, postmenopausal woman who is no longer an object of sexual desire.
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): Congregational prayer, specifically the five daily prayers and optional group prayers like Eid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, which prayers may an old woman attend without harm?
A) Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, Jumu'ah, and the two Eids
B) Only Fajr and Maghrib
C) All five daily prayers
D) Only Jumu'ah and Eid

Key Takeaway
An old woman may attend congregational prayers without perfume, provided she is no longer a source of fitnah, based on explicit hadith evidence and the Hanafi principle of avoiding temptation.

Who May Not Lead in Prayer: Deficiencies in Purity and Recitation
Rulings on who may not lead in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four cases where a pure follower cannot follow an imam with a deficiency, and explain the legal basis using the hadith 'al-imam damin'.

Core Idea
An imam must have at least equal purity and competency as the follower; deficiency in the imam invalidates the following.

This passage from Al-Quduri lists specific scenarios where the follower's state is superior to the imam's, making the prayer behind such an imam impermissible. The ruling hinges on the principle that the imam is a guarantor (damin) of the prayer's validity, so he must be in a state at least as valid as the follower.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four prohibited scenarios
Read the text: a pure person behind one with urinary incontinence (sals al-bawl), pure women behind a mustahadah (chronic bleeding), a reciter behind an illiterate person, a clothed person behind a naked person.
Each involves a deficiency in the imam compared to the follower.
2
Extract the common element
Recognize that in each case, the imam's state of purity, recitation ability, or covering is deficient relative to the follower.
The follower's validity is complete; the imam's is partial or lacking.
3
Locate the dalil
The hadith 'al-imam damin' (the imam is a guarantor) is cited as proof. Find it in Sunan al-Tirmidhi.
The imam bears responsibility for the prayer's validity.
4
Understand wajh al-dalalah
The imam's role as guarantor implies he must be in a state at least as valid as the follower. If his purity or ability is inferior, he cannot guarantee the prayer.
This justifies prohibiting the pure from following the deficient imam.
5
Note the permissible exceptions
Contrast with the next sentence: tayammum can lead wudu, masah can lead ghusl, standing can lead sitting. These are not deficiencies; the follower's state is equal or inferior.
Exceptions confirm the rule: the imam's deficiency must be real.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الجَمَاعَة
وَلَا يُصَلِّي الطَّاهِرُ خَلْفَ مَنْ بِهِ سَلَسُ الْبَوْلِ وَلَا الطَّاهِرَاتُ خَلْفَ الْمُسْتَحَاضَةِ وَلَا الْقَارِئُ خَلْفَ الْأُمِّيِّ وَلَا الْمُكْتَسِي خَلْفَ الْعُرْيَانِ ١٢ وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يَؤُمَ الْمُتَيَمِّمُ الْمُتَوَفِّئِينَ وَالْمَاسِحُ عَلَى الْخَفَّيْنِ الْعَاسِلِينَ ١٥ وَيُصَلِّي الْقَائِمُ خَلْفَ الْقَاعِدِ
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُصَلِّي الطَّاهِرُ خَلْفَ مَنْ بِهِ سَلَسُ الْبَوْلِ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الإِمَامُ ضَامِنٌ، وَالْمُؤَذِّنُ مُؤْتَمَنٌ، اللَّهُمَّ أَرْشِدِ الْأَئِمَّةَ، وَاغْفِرْ لِلْمُؤَذِّنِينَ» (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ أَنَّ الإِمَامَ ضَامِنٌ، وَالْمُؤَذَنَ مُؤْتَمَنٌ، رقم 207)
Chapter on Congregation. A person in a state of purity should not pray behind one who suffers from urinary incontinence, nor pure women behind a woman with chronic uterine bleeding (istihadah), nor a reciter behind an illiterate person, nor a clothed person behind a naked one. It is permissible for one who performed tayammum to lead those who performed wudu, and for one who wiped over his khuffs to lead those who washed their feet. A standing person may pray behind a sitting person. Proof: (1) The hadith establishing 'a person in a state of purity should not pray behind one who suffers from urinary incontinence': from Abu Huraira, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The imam is a guarantor, and the mu'adhdhin is entrusted. O Allah, guide the imams and forgive the mu'adhdhinun.' (Tirmidhi, no. 207)
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage presents a set of rulings about who may follow whom in congregational prayer. The first ruling states that a person who has wudu (a pure person) should not pray behind an imam who suffers from sals al-bawl (urinary incontinence, a condition where urine drips continuously, excusing the person from wudu for each prayer). The reason is that the imam's state of ritual purity is deficient compared to the follower's complete purity. Similarly, a woman with istihadah (chronic uterine bleeding, who can pray with wudu after washing) should not lead women who have complete purity (free from such conditions). A person who can recite the Quran properly should not follow an illiterate imam who cannot recite correctly. A clothed person should not follow a naked imam who has no covering. The commentator cites a hadith about the imam being a guarantor, implying the imam must be in a state of purity equal or superior to the follower. The next rulings (permissibility of tayammum leading wudu, etc.) are covered in separate lessons.

Key Terms
سَلَسُ الْبَوْلِ (sals al-bawl): Urinary incontinence, a continuous involuntary flow of urine that excuses the person from wudu for each prayer.
مُسْتَحَاضَة (mustahadah): A woman experiencing chronic uterine bleeding (istihadah) beyond the normal menstrual period, who must wash and perform wudu for each prayer.
الْأُمِّيِّ (al-ummi): An illiterate person who cannot recite the Quran correctly.
الْعُرْيَانِ (al-uryan): A naked person who has no covering for the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why should a pure person not pray behind someone with urinary incontinence?
A) Because the imam's impurity nullifies the prayer
B) Because the imam's state of purity is inferior
C) Because the follower must be superior
D) Because it is always forbidden regardless

Key Takeaway
An imam must have at least the same level of purity and competence as the follower; deficiency in the imam invalidates the follower's prayer.

6 min
A Mutayammim or Mas-h al-Khuffayn Leading the Prayer
Ruling with proof from a Companion's action

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a mutayammim leading those with wudu and explain the proof from the hadith of Amr ibn al-Aas.

Core Idea
Excused purification (tayammum/mas-h) is sufficient for leading prayer.

This lesson addresses a common practical question: can a person who performed tayammum (dry ablution) or wiped over leather socks (khuffs) lead others who have full wudu? Many assume the imam must have the most complete purity, but the Hanafi school, following the action of a Companion, allows it. We will examine the ruling, its proof, and the scholarly discussion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The text states two separate rulings: (1) a mutayammim may lead those with wudu, and (2) a person wiping over khuffs may lead those who washed their feet.
2
Locate the proof
The author cites the hadith of Amr ibn al-Aas, who performed tayammum due to fear of harm from cold water and then led his companions in Fajr prayer, with the Prophet’s implied approval.
The hadith is in Sunan Abi Dawud and Sahih al-Bukhari.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet’s tacit approval (taqrir) of Amr’s action shows that tayammum is a valid purification for leadership, even if the followers have full wudu.
The proof is based on fi'li (action) of a Sahabi endorsed by the Prophet.
4
Extend to mas-h al-khuffayn
The same permissibility applies to wiping over khuffs by qiyas (analogy): both are excused forms of purification with the same legal basis.
No specific hadith is cited for mas-h, but the ruling is derived by analogy.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi’i) consider it invalid for a mutayammim to lead if water is available, basing on the idea that the imam’s purity should be at least equal to the followers’.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يَؤُمَ الْمُتَيَمِّمُ الْمُتَوَفِّئِينَ وَالْمَاسِحُ عَلَى الْخَفَّيْنِ الْعَاسِلِينَ
وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يَؤُمُ الْمُتَيَمِّمُ الْمُتَوَضِنِينَ \ عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ الْعَاصِ قَالَ: احْتَلَمْتُ فِي لَيْلَةٍ بَارِدَةٍ فِي غَزْوَةِ ذَاتِ السُّلَاسِلِ فَأَشْفَقْتُ إِنِ اغْتَسَلْتُ أَنْ أَهْلِكَ فَتَيَمَّمْتُ، ثُمَّ صَلَّيْتُ بِأَصْحَابِي الصُّبْحَ (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ إِذَا خَافَ الجُنُبُ الْبَرْدَ أَيَتَيَمَّمُ، رقم 334) صحيح البخاري بَابٌ : إِذَا خَافَ الْجُنُبُ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ الْمَرَضَ أَوِ الْمَوْتَ أَوْ خَافَ الْعَطَشَ تَيَمَّمَ، رقم (345)
It is permissible for one who performed tayammum to lead those who performed wudu, and for one who wiped over his khuffs to lead those who washed their feet. Proof: (1) The hadith establishing 'it is permissible for one who performed tayammum to lead those who performed wudu': from Amr ibn al-Aas who said: I had a wet dream on a cold night during the expedition of Dhat al-Salasil, and I feared that if I performed ghusl I would die, so I performed tayammum, then I led my companions in the Fajr prayer. (Abu Dawud, no. 334; Bukhari, no. 345)
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of a person with a valid water-related excuse leading others who have full wudu. The first ruling states that a person who performed tayammum (dry ablution due to lack of water or illness) may lead those who performed regular wudu. The second ruling states that a person who wiped over his leather socks (khuffs) in the context of wudu may lead those who washed their feet (the default action). The commentator provides a hadith from Amr ibn al-Aas, who was in a state of major impurity (janabah) on a cold night but feared harm from cold water, so he performed tayammum and led his companions in Fajr. This proves that the tayammum is valid for leading others, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not object. The permissibility for mas-h over khuffs is analogically derived, as both are excused forms of purification.

Key Terms
المتيمم (al-mutayammim): One who performs tayammum (dry ablution) due to absence of water or inability to use it.
الماسح على الخفين (al-masih ala al-khuffayn): One who wipes over leather socks as part of wudu instead of washing feet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in the passage, who led the prayer after performing tayammum?
A) The Prophet (peace be upon him)
B) Amr ibn al-Aas
C) Abu Bakr al-Siddiq
D) Umar ibn al-Khattab

Key Takeaway
A person with a valid excuse for tayammum or mas-h al-khuffayn can lead others with complete wudu; the proof is the Prophet's tacit approval of Amr's action.

Standing behind a Sitting Imam
Ruling on a standing follower behind a sitting imam with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a standing follower behind a sitting imam and explain the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
A standing follower may validly pray behind an imam sitting due to illness.

This lesson examines a classic ruling on congregational prayer: when the imam is unable to stand due to illness, the follower who can stand must do so. The Hanafi school permits this based on the practice of the Prophet in his final illness. We will analyze the hadith proofs and the underlying principle that the imam is a guarantor.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The ruling is about a standing follower (qa'im) praying behind a sitting imam (qa'id). The Hanafi position is that this is permissible (ja'iz) and valid, provided the follower stands if able.
The follower does not sit even though the imam sits.
2
Locate the hadith evidence
The commentator cites three hadith narrations. The primary one is the famous hadith of Aisha describing the Prophet's final illness, where Abu Bakr led the people standing while the Prophet prayed sitting.
The hadith is found in Bukhari, Muslim, and Ibn Majah.
3
Understand the evidence
In the hadith, Abu Bakr stood and followed the Prophet's prayer, and the people stood behind Abu Bakr. This clearly demonstrates that standing behind a sitting imam is valid.
The Prophet's sitting was due to illness, not a voluntary act.
4
Note the principle
The Urdu note adds: 'The imam is a guarantor (damin) so it is necessary for the imam to be of a higher level or at least equal to the follower.' This is reconciled by focusing on equality in purity and competence, not posture.
The imam's deficiency in posture is excused by his inability; the follower compensates by standing.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school generally requires the imam to stand if possible; if he sits without excuse, the follower's prayer may be invalid. The Hanafi school is more flexible based on the Prophetic practice.
The difference rests on how each school interprets the hadith and the principle of following the imam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُصَلِّي الْقَائِمُ خَلْفَ الْقَاعِدِ
وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيُصَلِّي الْقَائِمُ خَلْفَ الْقَاعِدِ \ "دَخَلْتُ عَلَى عَائِشَةَ فَقُلْتُ: أَلَا تُحَدِّثِينِي عَنْ مَرَضِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ..... فَلَمَّا رَآهُ أَبُو بَكْرٍ، ذَهَبَ لِيَتَأَخَّرَ، فَأَوْمَا إِلَيْهِ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِأَنْ لَا يَتَأَخَّرَ، قَالَ: أَجْلِسَانِي إِلَى جَنْبِهِ. فَأَجْلَسَاهُ إِلَى جَنْبِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ، قَالَ: فَجَعَلَ أَبُو بَكْرٍ يُصَلِّي وَهُوَ يَأْتَمُّ بِصَلَاةِ النَّبِي ، وَالنَّاسُ بِصَلَاةِ أَبي بَكْرٍ ، وَالنَّبِيُّ ل ،قَاعِدٌ،،"(صحيح البخاري، بَابٌ : إِنَّمَا جُعِلَ الْإِمَامُ لِيُؤْتَمَّ بِهِ رقم (687)

اصول : امام ضامن ہوتا ہے لہذا امام کا اعلی درجہ کا ہونایا کم از کم مقتدی کے برابر ہو نا ضروری ہے
And a standing person may pray behind a sitting person. Proof: (1) The hadith establishing 'a standing person may pray behind a sitting person': 'I entered upon Aisha and said: Will you not tell me about the illness of the Messenger of Allah... When Abu Bakr saw him, he went to step back, but the Prophet gestured to him not to step back. He said: Have me sit beside him. So they seated him beside Abu Bakr. He said: Then Abu Bakr began praying, following the prayer of the Prophet, and the people followed the prayer of Abu Bakr, while the Prophet was sitting.' (Bukhari, no. 687) Proof: (2) The hadith establishing 'a standing person may pray behind a sitting person': 'And Abu Bakr stood up, and Abu Bakr was following the Prophet, and the people were following Abu Bakr. Ibn Abbas said: And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) took from the recitation from where Abu Bakr had reached.' (Ibn Majah, no. 1235; Muslim, no. 418) Proof: (3) The hadith from Anas ibn Malik: 'That the Messenger of Allah...' Principle: The imam is a guarantor, so it is necessary for the imam to be of a higher level or at least equal to the follower.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that a standing person may pray behind a sitting imam. This applies when the imam is sitting due to illness or inability to stand. The follower, who is able to stand, must stand; he does not sit even though the imam is sitting. The commentator provides three hadith proofs. First, the famous hadith of Aisha describing the Prophet's final illness, where he led the prayer sitting while Abu Bakr and the people stood behind him. This clearly shows that a standing follower behind a sitting imam is valid. The second hadith from Ibn Abbas further explains that Abu Bakr was following the Prophet's recitation while standing. The third hadith from Anas is cut off but likely supports the same. The Urdu principle at the end states: 'The imam is a guarantor, so it is necessary for the imam to be of a higher level or at least equal to the follower.' This principle seems to contradict the permissibility of a standing person behind a sitting imam, but the Hanafi explanation is that 'equal' here refers to the state of purity and essential competence, not physical posture. The imam's deficiency in posture (sitting) is excused due to his inability, and the follower compensates by standing.

Key Terms
القائم خلف القاعد (al-qa'im khalfa al-qa'id): A standing follower praying behind an imam who is sitting due to illness or old age.
ضامن (damin): Guarantor; the imam is responsible for the correctness of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) He stood
C) He left the prayer
D) He led from behind

Key Takeaway
A standing follower may validly pray behind an imam sitting due to illness; the follower must stand if able.

8 min
Rules of Valid Imamate in Congregational Prayer
States four rulings on valid imam-mamum pairings with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four Hanafi rulings on valid imam-mamum pairings in congregational prayer and identify the hadith proof for each.

Core Idea
For a valid congregation, the imam and follower must share the same prayer type—except nafl behind fard is allowed.

The imam is appointed to be followed, but not every pairing is valid. Al-Quduri lays out four clear rulings: a person who bows and prostrates cannot follow a gesturer, a person performing fard cannot follow a performer of nafl, a person performing one fard cannot follow another performing a different fard, yet a person performing nafl may follow a performer of fard. These rulings preserve the congruence of intention and action between imam and follower.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four rulings
Read the matn and list each prohibition and the one permission. Note the exact terms: al-muumi (gesturer), al-muftarid (fard performer), al-mutanaqqil/al-mutanaffil (nafl performer).
The permission is the exception: nafl behind fard.
2
Locate the hadith proofs
For each ruling, find the hadith cited in the commentary. The general hadith about following the imam supports the first two prohibitions. The hadith of Mu'adh supports the prohibition of fard behind nafl. The hadith of Jabir supports the permission of nafl behind fard.
Hadith references: Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, Daraqutni, Tirmidhi.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
For each hadith, see how it proves the ruling. The general hadith implies that the follower must not differ from the imam, including in the type of prayer. The Mu'adh hadith shows that Mu'adh's prayer for his people was nafl for him but fard for them, which would be prohibited if it were a valid imamate; the Hanafis argue that it was a special allowance, not a general rule.
Focus on the Hanafi interpretation: the default is that follower’s intention must match imam’s.
4
Note the exception
The fourth ruling allows nafl behind fard. The hadith of Jabir proves that one who has already prayed fard may join the congregation for the same prayer, making it nafl for him. This is the only exception among the four.
This ruling is often used for catching up with the congregation after having already prayed individually.
5
Recognize the Hanafi position and cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi school holds that all four rulings are makruh tahrimi (prohibited). Some other schools, like the Hanbalis, allow fard behind nafl in certain cases, but the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is as stated in the matn.
Know that the difference is legitimate (ikhtilaf).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
