فَيُصَلِّي بِهِمْ تِلْكَ الصَّلَاةَ، ( سنن ابوداود، بَابُ إِمَامَةِ مَنْ يُصَلِّي بِقَوْمٍ وَقَدْ صَلَّى تِلْكَ الصَّلَاةَ، رقم 599) وجه : (٣) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُصَلِّي الْمُفْتَرِضُ خَلْفَ الْمُتَنَفِّلِ \«أَنَّ مُعَاذَا «كَانَ يُصَلِّي مَعَ التي الْعِشَاءَ ، ثُمَّ يَنْصَرِفُ إِلَى قَوْمِهِ فَيُصَلِّي بِهِمْ ، هِيَ لَهُ تَطَوُّعٌ وَلَهُمْ فَرِيضَةٌ»، ( سنن دارقطني، بَابُ ذِكْرٍ صَلَاةِ الْمُفْتَرَض خَلْفَ الْمُتْنَفِل، رقم (1075) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيُصَلِّي الْمُتَنَقِّلُ خَلْفَ الْمُفْتَرِضِ \ عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ يَزِيدَ بْنِ الْأَسْوَدِ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، أَنَّهُ صَلَّى مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ الهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَهُوَ غُلَامٌ شَابٌ، فَلَمَّا صَلَّى إِذَا رَجُلَانِ لَمْ يُصَلِّيَا فِي نَاحِيَةِ الْمَسْجِدِ، فَدَعَا بِهِمَا فَجِئَ بِهِمَا تُرْعَدُ فَرَائِصُهُمَا، فَقَالَ: «مَا مَنَعَكُمَا أَنْ تُصَلِّيَا مَعَنَا؟» قَالَا: قَدْ صَلَّيْنَا فِي رِحَالِنَا، فَقَالَ: «لَا تَفْعَلُوا إِذَا صَلَّى أَحَدُكُمْ فِي رَحْلِهِ ثُمَّ أَدْرَكَ الْإِمَامَ وَلَمْ يُصَلَّ، فَلْيُصَلَّ مَعَهُ فَإِنَّهَا لَهُ نَافِلَةٌ»، ) سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِيمَنْ صَلَّى فِي مَنْزِلِهِ ثُمَّ أَدْرَكَ الْجَمَاعَةَ يُصَلِّي مَعَهُمْ، رقم 575\سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الرَّجُلِ يُصَلِّي وَحْدَهُ ثُمَّ يُدْرِكُ الجَمَاعَةَ رقم (219) اصول : رکوع سجدہ والا اشارہ والے کی اور فرض والا متنفل کی اقتداء نہیں کر سکتا ہے، نیز فرض پڑھنے والا دوسری فرض پڑھنے والے کی اقتداء بھی نہ کرے۔
Chapter on Congregational Prayer. 16. One who bows and prostrates should not pray behind one who gestures. Nor should one performing an obligatory prayer pray behind one performing a supererogatory prayer. Nor should one praying one obligatory prayer pray behind one praying a different obligatory prayer. 18. One performing a supererogatory prayer may pray behind one performing an obligatory prayer. He rode a horse and was thrown from it, and his right side was scratched, so he prayed one of the prayers sitting, and we prayed behind him sitting. When he finished, he said: 'The imam is appointed to be followed; so when he prays standing, pray standing; when he bows, bow; when he raises, raise; when he says Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, say Rabbana wa laka al-hamd; when he prays standing, pray standing; when he prays sitting, pray sitting all together.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter: The imam is appointed to be followed, no. 689; Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter: The imam praying sitting, no. 601) Wajh (1): Hadith to prove that one performing obligatory prayer should not pray behind one performing supererogatory prayer: from Abu Huraira that the Messenger of Allah said: 'The imam is appointed to be followed, so do not differ from him.' (Muslim, Chapter: Following the imam, no. 414) Wajh (2): Hadith to prove that one performing obligatory prayer should not pray behind one performing supererogatory prayer: from Jabir ibn Abdullah that Mu'adh ibn Jabal used to pray Isha with the Messenger of Allah, then come to his people and lead them in that same prayer. (Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter: Imamate of one who leads a people after having already prayed that prayer, no. 599) Wajh (3): Hadith to prove that one performing obligatory prayer should not pray behind one performing supererogatory prayer: that Mu'adh used to pray Isha with the Prophet, then go to his people and lead them; it was supererogatory for him and obligatory for them. (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Chapter: Mention of the prayer of one performing obligatory prayer behind one performing supererogatory prayer, no. 1075) Wajh (1): Hadith to prove that one performing supererogatory prayer may pray behind one performing obligatory prayer: from Jabir ibn Yazid ibn al-Aswad from his father that he prayed with the Messenger of Allah while he was a young boy. When he prayed, there were two men who had not prayed in a corner of the mosque. He called them, and they came trembling. He said: 'What prevented you from praying with us?' They said: 'We prayed in our dwellings.' He said: 'Do not do that; if one of you prays in his dwelling then catches up with the imam and has not prayed, let him pray with him, for it will be a supererogatory prayer for him.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter: Regarding one who prays in his home then catches the congregation and prays with them, no. 575; Sunan al-Tirmidhi, Chapter: What is narrated about a man who prays alone then catches the congregation, no. 219) Principle: One who bows and prostrates cannot follow one who gestures, and one performing obligatory prayer cannot follow one performing supererogatory prayer, and one performing one obligatory prayer should not follow one performing another obligatory prayer.
Source pages p. 109

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's matn on congregational prayer presents four key rulings on the validity of following an imam based on the type of prayer. The first ruling: a person who performs ruku and sujud (i.e., a normal prayer) cannot pray behind an imam who merely gestures (due to illness or inability). The second: one performing an obligatory (fard) prayer cannot follow an imam performing a supererogatory (nafl) prayer, because the imam's intention differs and the follower's obligation is not fulfilled. The third: one performing one fard prayer cannot follow an imam performing a different fard (e.g., Dhuhr behind Asr). The fourth: a person performing nafl can follow an imam performing fard. The commentator then provides hadith proofs for each ruling: the general hadith about following the imam, the hadith of Mu'adh (which shows that the people's prayer was fard but his was nafl), and the hadith of Jabir (which allows nafl behind fard). The Urdu 'usul' at the end summarizes the rulings: one who bows and prostrates cannot follow a gesturer; one performing fard cannot follow a performer of nafl; one performing one fard should not follow another performing a different fard.

Key Terms
الْمُومِي (al-muumi): One who gestures (with head or body) during prayer due to illness instead of performing ruku and sujud
الْمُفْتَرِضُ (al-muftarid): One who is performing an obligatory (fard) prayer
الْمُتَنَقِّلُ / الْمُتَنَفِّلُ (al-mutanaqqil / al-mutanaffil): One who is performing a supererogatory (nafl) prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Is it valid for a person praying Fard to follow an imam who is praying Nafl?
A) Yes, valid
B) No, not valid
C) Valid only if both are the same prayer time
D) Valid only if the follower missed the congregation

Key Takeaway
For a valid congregation, the imam and follower must be performing the same type of prayer (fard or nafl), except that nafl behind fard is allowed.

Following an Impure Imam: Follower Must Repeat Prayer
Ruling that follower must repeat prayer if imam was impure, with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a follower discovers the imam was impure, cite the primary hadith proofs, and explain why the Hanafi school differs from others on this issue.

Core Idea
If the imam was impure, the follower's prayer is invalid and must be repeated.

In this lesson from Al-Quduri's matn, we learn that following an impure imam invalidates the follower's prayer. The commentator provides several hadith proofs, including the well-known story of the Prophet stopping mid-prayer when he realized he was junub. We'll analyze these evidences and understand the underlying principle that ties the follower's prayer to the imam's.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is following an imam who is later discovered to be without purity (junub or without wudu). The ruling is that the follower must repeat his prayer.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith from Abu Hurairah: the Prophet came out to lead in a state of janabah, then stopped, bathed, and led again. This shows that leading in impurity invalidates the prayer.
This is the strongest evidence.
3
Analyze the implication
If the imam's prayer is invalid, the followers' prayer is also invalid because the follower's prayer is contingent on the imam's. The Prophet's action of repeating and commanding the followers to wait supports this.
Hanafi usul: the follower's prayer is included in the imam's.
4
Consider supporting evidence
The action of Ali and the hadith from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib confirm the same ruling.
Multiple chains strengthen the proof.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
Some scholars (e.g., Shafi'is) hold that the followers' prayer is valid if they were unaware, based on a hadith in Daraqutni. The Hanafi response is that this hadith is weaker and the principle of contingency outweighs it.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بَعْدَ الصُّبْحِ حَتَّى تشرق الشَّمْسُ وَبَعْدَ الْعَصْرِ حَتَّى تَغْرُبَ»، صحيح البخاري بَابُ الصَّلَاةِ بَعْدَ الْفَجْرِ حَتَّى تَرْتَفِعَ الشَّمْسُ ، رقم (581) واوجه : (۱)الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ اقْتَدَى بِإِمَامٍ ثُمَّ عَلِمَ أَنَّهُ عَلَى غَيْرِ طَهَارَةِ أَعَادَ الصَّلَاةَ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: «أُقِيمَتِ الصَّلَاةُ، فَسَوَّى النَّاسُ صُفُوفَهُمْ، فَخَرَجَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَتَقَدَّمَ، وَهُوَ جُنُبِّ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: عَلَى مَكَانِكُمْ. فَرَجَعَ فَاغْتَسَلَ ثُمَّ خَرَجَ وَرَأْسُهُ يَقْطُرُ مَاءً فَصَلَّى بِهِمْ.» (صحيح البخاري، بابٌ : إِذَا قَالَ الْإِمَامُ مَكَانَكُمْ حَتَّى رَجَعَ انْتَظَرُوهُ، رقم (640) وجه (۲)قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ اقْتَدَى بِإِمَامٍ ثُمَّ عَلِمَ أَنَّهُ عَلَى غَيْرِ طَهَارَةٍ أَعَادَ الصَّلَاةَ \ عَنْ عَلِيّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنَّهُ " صَلَّى بِالْقَوْمِ وَهُوَ جُنُبٌ فَأَعَادَ ثُمَّ أَمَرَهُمْ فَأَعَادُوا "(السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ إِمَامَةِ الْجُنُبِ ، رقم 4078\ سنن دارقطني، بَابُ ذِكْرِ مَا يَخْرُجُ مِنَ الصَّلَاةِ بِهِ وَكَيْفِيَّةِ التَسْلِيم، رقم 1355) وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ اقْتَدَى بِإِمَامٍ ثُمَّ عَلِمَ أَنَّهُ عَلَى غَيْرِ طَهَارَةِ أَعَادَ الصَّلَاةَ \ عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ الْمُسَيِّبِ ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم صَلَّى بِالنَّاسِ وَهُوَ جُنُبٌ فَأَعَادَ وَأَعَادُوا»،»،(سنن دارقطني بابُ صَلَاةِ الْإِمَامِ وَهُوَ جُنُبٌ أَوْ مُحْدِثُ، رقم (1369) (۴) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ اقْتَدَى بِإِمَامٍ ثُمَّ عَلِمَ أَنَّهُ عَلَى غَيْرِ طَهَارَةِ أَعَادَ الصَّلَاةَ \ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «أَيُّمَا إِمَامٍ سَهَى فَصَلَّى بِالْقَوْمِ وَهُوَ جُنُبْ فَقَدْ مَضَتْ صَلَاتُهُمْ ، ثُمَّ لِيَغْتَسِلْ هُوَ ثُمَّ لِيَعُدْ صَلَاتَهُ ، وَإِنْ صَلَّى بِغَيْرِ وُضُوءٍ فَمِثْلُ ذَلِكَ»»»»، سنن دارقطني، بَابُ صَلَاةِ الْإِمَامِ وَهُوَ جُنُبٌ أَوْ مُحْدِثٌ ، رقم 1368) اصول : احناف : فجر ، عصر اور مغرب کی فرض پڑھ چکا ہو تو دوبارہ نفل کی نیت سے امام کے ساتھ شامل نہ ہو، کیونکہ فجر اور عصر کے بعد کوئی نفل نہیں ہے ، اور تین رکعت نفل نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اصول : اقتداء کرنے والے کی نماز اصلاح و فساد میں امام کی نماز کو متضمن ہوتی ہے، لہذا العام کے فساد سے مقتدی کی نماز بھی متاثر ہو گی۔
Chapter on Congregational Prayer. 19. Whoever follows an imam and then learns that he was not in a state of purity must repeat the prayer. Wajh (1): Hadith to prove that one performing supererogatory prayer may pray behind one performing obligatory prayer: He forbade prayer after Fajr until the sun rises and after Asr until the sun sets. (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter: Prayer after Fajr until the sun rises, no. 581) And wajh (1): Hadith to prove that whoever follows an imam and then learns he was not in a state of purity must repeat the prayer: from Abu Huraira who said: 'The prayer was established, and the people straightened their rows. Then the Messenger of Allah came out and stepped forward while he was in a state of major impurity. Then he said: 'Stay in your places.' So he returned and bathed, then came out with his head dripping water and led them in prayer.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter: When the imam says 'Stay in your places' until he returns, they wait, no. 640) Wajh (2): Saying of the Companion to prove that whoever follows an imam and then learns he was not in a state of purity must repeat the prayer: from Ali that he led the people while he was in a state of major impurity, so he repeated and commanded them to repeat. (Al-Sunan al-Kubra lil-Bayhaqi, Chapter: Imamate of a person in major impurity, no. 4078; Sunan al-Daraqutni, Chapter: Mention of what invalidates prayer and how to say the taslim, no. 1355) Wajh (3): Hadith to prove that whoever follows an imam and then learns he was not in a state of purity must repeat the prayer: from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib that the Messenger of Allah led the people while he was in major impurity, so he repeated and they repeated. (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Chapter: The imam's prayer while he is in major impurity or minor impurity, no. 1369) (4) Hadith to prove that whoever follows an imam and then learns he was not in a state of purity must repeat the prayer: from the Prophet who said: 'Any imam who forgets and leads the people while he is in major impurity, then their prayer is valid, but he must bathe and repeat his prayer; and if he prays without ablution, it is the same.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Chapter: The imam's prayer while he is in major impurity or minor impurity, no. 1368) Principle (Hanafis): If one has already prayed the fard of Fajr, Asr, or Maghrib, he should not join the congregation again intending nafl, because there is no nafl after Fajr and Asr, and three rak'ats cannot be nafl. Principle: The follower's prayer, in terms of validity and corruption, is contingent upon the imam's prayer; therefore, if the imam's prayer is corrupted, the follower's prayer is also affected.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's matn states that if a follower discovers after the prayer that his imam was without purity (either lacking wudu or in a state of janabah), he must repeat his prayer. The commentator provides several proofs: the hadith of Abu Hurairah where the Prophet, while junub, went to lead but then stopped, bathed, and led; the act of Ali who repeated with his followers after leading in janabah; and a hadith from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib. Notably, hadith (4) from al-Daraqutni says the followers' prayer is valid but the imam repeats, but the Hanafi position—based on the other stronger evidences—requires the followers to repeat as well if they discover the impurity later. The first usul note (in Urdu) adds a separate ruling: if one has already prayed the fard of Fajr, Asr, or Maghrib, he should not rejoin the congregation intending nafl because there is no nafl after Fajr and Asr, and Maghrib is three rak'ats which cannot be nafl. The second usul principle explains the underlying reason: the follower's prayer is contingent on the imam's prayer; if the imam's prayer is invalid (due to impurity), the follower's is also invalid, thus requiring repetition.

Key Terms
جُنُب (junub): A state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl
طَهَارَة (taharah): Ritual purity, both from minor (wudu) and major (ghusl) impurities
اقْتَدَى (iqtada): To follow an imam in congregational prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a follower discovers after prayer that the imam was in a state of janabah (major impurity), what should the follower do?
A) Nothing, his prayer is valid
B) Repeat his prayer
C) Repeat only the imam repeats
D) Make up only if he was aware during prayer

Key Takeaway
The follower's prayer is contingent on the imam's; if the imam's prayer is invalid due to impurity, the follower must repeat.

The Principle of Contingency and Prohibited Nafl in Congregation
Additional fiqh principles: contingency of follower's prayer and prohibition of nafl after certain times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi principle that the follower's prayer is contingent on the imam's, and identify when it is prohibited to join congregation intending nafl.

Core Idea
The follower's prayer stands or falls with the imam's; and nafl prayer after Fajr/Asr and Maghrib as nafl are prohibited.

This lesson covers two important fiqh principles extracted from the commentary on Al-Quduri. First, a general rule: the validity of the follower's prayer is tied to the imam's. Second, a specific application: if you have already prayed the fard of Fajr, Asr, or Maghrib, you should not rejoin the congregation with the intention of nafl, because there is no nafl after Fajr and Asr, and a three-rak'at prayer cannot be nafl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contingency principle
The follower's prayer is inherently linked to the imam's prayer. If the imam's prayer is invalid, the follower's is also invalid, and vice versa.
This is a basic principle in Hanafi fiqh for congregational prayer.
2
Apply the principle
This explains why the follower must repeat if the imam was impure, as seen in the previous lesson.
3
Identify the nafl prohibition
It is not allowed to join a congregation for nafl prayer after having already prayed the fard of Fajr or Asr, because nafl after these times is prohibited. Similarly, Maghrib cannot be prayed as nafl because it is three rak'ats.
This is based on the hadith forbidding prayer after Fajr and Asr.
4
Understand the scope
This ruling applies to someone who has already performed the fard prayer individually or in another congregation and then comes across another congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الجَمَاعَة 19 وَمَنْ اقْتَدَى بِإِمَامٍ ثُمَّ عَلِمَ أَنَّهُ عَلَى غَيْرِ طَهَارَةٍ أَعَادَ الصَّلَاةَ وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَيُصَلِّي الْمُتَنَفِّلُ خَلْفَ الْمُفْتَرِضِ انَهَى عَنِ الصَّلَاةِ بَعْدَ الصُّبْحِ حَتَّى تشرق الشَّمْسُ وَبَعْدَ الْعَصْرِ حَتَّى تَغْرُبَ»، صحيح البخاري بَابُ الصَّلَاةِ بَعْدَ الْفَجْرِ حَتَّى تَرْتَفِعَ الشَّمْسُ ، رقم (581) واوجه : (۱)الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ اقْتَدَى بِإِمَامٍ ثُمَّ عَلِمَ أَنَّهُ عَلَى غَيْرِ طَهَارَةِ أَعَادَ الصَّلَاةَ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: «أُقِيمَتِ الصَّلَاةُ، فَسَوَّى النَّاسُ صُفُوفَهُمْ، فَخَرَجَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَتَقَدَّمَ، وَهُوَ جُنُبِّ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: عَلَى مَكَانِكُمْ. فَرَجَعَ فَاغْتَسَلَ ثُمَّ خَرَجَ وَرَأْسُهُ يَقْطُرُ مَاءً فَصَلَّى بِهِمْ.» (صحيح البخاري، بابٌ : إِذَا قَالَ الْإِمَامُ مَكَانَكُمْ حَتَّى رَجَعَ انْتَظَرُوهُ، رقم (640) وجه (۲)قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ اقْتَدَى بِإِمَامٍ ثُمَّ عَلِمَ أَنَّهُ عَلَى غَيْرِ طَهَارَةٍ أَعَادَ الصَّلَاةَ \ عَنْ عَلِيّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنَّهُ " صَلَّى بِالْقَوْمِ وَهُوَ جُنُبٌ فَأَعَادَ ثُمَّ أَمَرَهُمْ فَأَعَادُوا "(السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ إِمَامَةِ الْجُنُبِ ، رقم 4078\ سنن دارقطني، بَابُ ذِكْرِ مَا يَخْرُجُ مِنَ الصَّلَاةِ بِهِ وَكَيْفِيَّةِ التَسْلِيم، رقم 1355) وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ اقْتَدَى بِإِمَامٍ ثُمَّ عَلِمَ أَنَّهُ عَلَى غَيْرِ طَهَارَةِ أَعَادَ الصَّلَاةَ \ عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ الْمُسَيِّبِ ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم صَلَّى بِالنَّاسِ وَهُوَ جُنُبٌ فَأَعَادَ وَأَعَادُوا»،»،(سنن دارقطني بابُ صَلَاةِ الْإِمَامِ وَهُوَ جُنُبٌ أَوْ مُحْدِثُ، رقم (1369) (۴) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ اقْتَدَى بِإِمَامٍ ثُمَّ عَلِمَ أَنَّهُ عَلَى غَيْرِ طَهَارَةِ أَعَادَ الصَّلَاةَ \ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «أَيُّمَا إِمَامٍ سَهَى فَصَلَّى بِالْقَوْمِ وَهُوَ جُنُبْ فَقَدْ مَضَتْ صَلَاتُهُمْ ، ثُمَّ لِيَغْتَسِلْ هُوَ ثُمَّ لِيَعُدْ صَلَاتَهُ ، وَإِنْ صَلَّى بِغَيْرِ وُضُوءٍ فَمِثْلُ ذَلِكَ»»»»، سنن دارقطني، بَابُ صَلَاةِ الْإِمَامِ وَهُوَ جُنُبٌ أَوْ مُحْدِثٌ ، رقم 1368) اصول : احناف : فجر ، عصر اور مغرب کی فرض پڑھ چکا ہو تو دوبارہ نفل کی نیت سے امام کے ساتھ شامل نہ ہو، کیونکہ فجر اور عصر کے بعد کوئی نفل نہیں ہے ، اور تین رکعت نفل نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اصول : اقتداء کرنے والے کی نماز اصلاح و فساد میں امام کی نماز کو متضمن ہوتی ہے، لہذا العام کے فساد سے مقتدی کی نماز بھی متاثر ہو گی۔
Chapter on Congregational Prayer. 19. Whoever follows an imam and then learns that he was not in a state of purity must repeat the prayer. Wajh (1): Hadith to prove that one performing supererogatory prayer may pray behind one performing obligatory prayer: He forbade prayer after Fajr until the sun rises and after Asr until the sun sets. (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter: Prayer after Fajr until the sun rises, no. 581) And wajh (1): Hadith to prove that whoever follows an imam and then learns he was not in a state of purity must repeat the prayer: from Abu Huraira who said: 'The prayer was established, and the people straightened their rows. Then the Messenger of Allah came out and stepped forward while he was in a state of major impurity. Then he said: 'Stay in your places.' So he returned and bathed, then came out with his head dripping water and led them in prayer.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter: When the imam says 'Stay in your places' until he returns, they wait, no. 640) Wajh (2): Saying of the Companion to prove that whoever follows an imam and then learns he was not in a state of purity must repeat the prayer: from Ali that he led the people while he was in a state of major impurity, so he repeated and commanded them to repeat. (Al-Sunan al-Kubra lil-Bayhaqi, Chapter: Imamate of a person in major impurity, no. 4078; Sunan al-Daraqutni, Chapter: Mention of what invalidates prayer and how to say the taslim, no. 1355) Wajh (3): Hadith to prove that whoever follows an imam and then learns he was not in a state of purity must repeat the prayer: from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib that the Messenger of Allah led the people while he was in major impurity, so he repeated and they repeated. (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Chapter: The imam's prayer while he is in major impurity or minor impurity, no. 1369) (4) Hadith to prove that whoever follows an imam and then learns he was not in a state of purity must repeat the prayer: from the Prophet who said: 'Any imam who forgets and leads the people while he is in major impurity, then their prayer is valid, but he must bathe and repeat his prayer; and if he prays without ablution, it is the same.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Chapter: The imam's prayer while he is in major impurity or minor impurity, no. 1368) Principle (Hanafis): If one has already prayed the fard of Fajr, Asr, or Maghrib, he should not join the congregation again intending nafl, because there is no nafl after Fajr and Asr, and three rak'ats cannot be nafl. Principle: The follower's prayer, in terms of validity and corruption, is contingent upon the imam's prayer; therefore, if the imam's prayer is corrupted, the follower's prayer is also affected.
Source pages p. 110

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's matn states that if a follower discovers after the prayer that his imam was without purity (either lacking wudu or in a state of janabah), he must repeat his prayer. The commentator provides several proofs: the hadith of Abu Hurairah where the Prophet, while junub, went to lead but then stopped, bathed, and led; the act of Ali who repeated with his followers after leading in janabah; and a hadith from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib. Notably, hadith (4) from al-Daraqutni says the followers' prayer is valid but the imam repeats, but the Hanafi position—based on the other stronger evidences—requires the followers to repeat as well if they discover the impurity later. The first usul note (in Urdu) adds a separate ruling: if one has already prayed the fard of Fajr, Asr, or Maghrib, he should not rejoin the congregation intending nafl because there is no nafl after Fajr and Asr, and Maghrib is three rak'ats which cannot be nafl. The second usul principle explains the underlying reason: the follower's prayer is contingent on the imam's prayer; if the imam's prayer is invalid (due to impurity), the follower's is also invalid, thus requiring repetition.

Key Terms
جُنُب (junub): A state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl
طَهَارَة (taharah): Ritual purity, both from minor (wudu) and major (ghusl) impurities
اقْتَدَى (iqtada): To follow an imam in congregational prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling regarding a person who has already prayed Fajr and then joins a Fajr congregation intending nafl?
A) Permissible
B) Not permissible because nafl after Fajr is prohibited
C) Permissible if he intends to repeat the fard
D) Makruh tanzih

Key Takeaway
The follower's prayer is tied to the imam's, and nafl after Fajr and Asr is prohibited; Maghrib cannot be prayed as nafl.

Disliked Acts in Prayer: The Rulings and Their Hadith Proofs
Listing disliked actions in prayer with their Hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on six disliked acts in prayer and identify the Hadith evidence for each.

Core Idea
The Prophet ﷺ forbade specific postures and distractions in prayer to maintain humility; these prohibitions indicate dislike (karahah).

This lesson explores the detailed list of makruhat (disliked acts) from the Hanafi matn of Al-Quduri, each supported by authentic Hadith. Understanding these rulings helps you perfect your prayer by avoiding actions that diminish its reward or invalidate it.

Guided Path
1
Identify each act and ruling
For each of the listed actions (sadl, aqs al-sha'r, etc.), note whether it is makruh tanzih or tahrimi. The text generally treats them as makruh, but turning the face is specifically makruh tahrimi.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the Hadith cited for each act. Most are from the major collections (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawood, Tirmidhi, Bayhaqi).
Some acts like cracking fingers and placing hands on hips lack explicit Hadith proof in this passage.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does each Hadith indicate karahah? Prohibitions (nahy) generally imply dislike in Hanafi usul, not absolute prohibition unless specified.
The imperative 'amartu' in the Hadith of Ibn Abbas indicates command, so folding garment is contrary to that command.
4
Distinguish degrees of turning
The Usul paragraph clarifies: turning eyes is makruh tanzih, turning face is makruh tahrimi, turning chest invalidates the prayer.
This is a key practical distinction.
5
Apply the ruling
Determine the practical consequence: does the act require sujud al-sahw or invalidate? For turning chest, the prayer is invalid.
For other makruhat, the prayer is valid but reward is diminished.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل مايكره في الصلوة
ولا يسدل ثوبه ولا يعقص شعره ولا يكف ثوبه ولا يلتفت ولا يقعي ولا يفرقع أصابعه ولا يتخصر. 
وجه: (١) الحديث لثبوت ولا يسدل ثوبه عن أبي هريرة أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى عن السدل في الصلاة وأن يغطي الرجل فاه (سنن أبي داود). 
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت ولا يعقص شعره عن أبي رافع أنه رأى حسن بن علي يصلي قائما وقد غرز ضفره في قفاه فحلها أبو رافع وقال سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: ذلك كفل الشيطان (سنن أبي داود، سنن الترمذي). 
وجه: (٣) الحديث لثبوت ولا يكف ثوبه عن ابن عباس عن النبي قال: أمرت أن أسجد على سبعة لا أكف شعرا ولا ثوبا (البخاري، مسلم). 
وجه: (٤) الحديث لثبوت ولا يلتفت عن عائشة قالت سألت رسول الله عن الالتفات في الصلاة فقال: هو اختلاس يختلسه الشيطان من صلاة العبد (البخاري، سنن أبي داود). 
وجه: (٥) الحديث لثبوت ولا يقعي عن سمرة بن جندب قال: نهى رسول الله عن الإقعاء في الصلاة (السنن الكبرى للبيهقي). 
وجه: (٦) قول التابعي لثبوت ولا يقعي سمع طاوسا يقول قلنا لابن عباس في الإقعاء على القدمين فقال: هي السنة. فقلنا له إنا لنراه جفاء بالرجل. فقال ابن عباس: بل هي سنة نبيك (مسلم). 
أصول: مصلي ادھر ادھر نظر پھیرے تو مکروہ، چہرہ پھر جائے تو مکروہ تحریمی، اور سینہ پھر جائے تو نماز فاسد۔
و ولا يرد السلام بلسانه ولا بيده. 
وجه: (١) الحديث لثبوت ولا يرد السلام بلسانه ولا بيده عن زيد بن أرقم قال كنا نتكلم في الصلاة حتى نزلت {وقوموا لله قانتين} فأمرنا بالسكوت ونهينا عن الكلام (مسلم، سنن الترمذي، سنن أبي داود). 
وجه: (٢) (دليل الشافعي) الحديث لثبوت ولا يرد السلام بلسانه ولا بيده عن عبد الله قال صلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فلما سلم قيل له أحدث في الصلاة شيء؟ قال: وما ذاك؟ قالوا صليت كذا وكذا، فثنى رجليه واستقبل القبلة فسجد سجدتين ثم سلم ثم قال: إنه لو حدث في الصلاة شيء أنبأتكم به، ولكن إنما أنا بشر أنسى كما تنسون، فإذا نسيت فذكروني، وإذا شك أحدكم في صلاته فليتحر الصواب ثم ليسجد سجدتين (مسلم، سنن الترمذي). 
وجه: (٣) الحديث لثبوت ولا يرد السلام بلسانه ولا بيده عن جابر بن سمرة قال كنا إذا صلينا مع رسول الله قلنا السلام عليكم ورحمة الله السلام عليكم ورحمة الله وأشار بيده إلى الجانبين فقال رسول الله: علام تومئون بأيديكم كأنها أذناب خيل شمس؟ إنما يكفي أحدكم أن يضع يده على فخذه ثم يسلم على أخيه من على يمينه وشماله (مسلم، سنن أبي داود). 
أصول: نماز میں کلام کرنا جائز نہیں، اور احناف کے نزدیک اگر بھول سے بھی بات کر لیا تو بھی نماز فاسد ہو گئی۔
Chapter on what is disliked in prayer. He does not let his garment hang down, nor does he twist his hair, nor does he fold his garment, nor does he turn away, nor does he sit on his heels, nor does he crack his fingers, nor does he put his hands on his hips. Evidence: (1) The hadith for not letting the garment hang down: from Abu Huraira that the Messenger of Allah forbade letting the garment hang down in prayer and covering the mouth. (2) The hadith for not twisting the hair: from Abu Rafi that he saw Hasan ibn Ali praying standing while he had inserted his braid at the back of his neck, so Abu Rafi undid it and said he heard the Prophet say: that is the portion of Satan. (3) The hadith for not folding the garment: from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet said: I have been commanded to prostrate on seven parts, not to fold hair or garment. (4) The hadith for not turning away: from Aisha who asked the Prophet about turning in prayer and he said: it is a snatch that Satan snatches from the prayer of the servant. (5) The hadith for not sitting on the heels: from Samura ibn Jundub that the Prophet forbade iq'a in prayer. (6) The statement of a follower: he heard Tawus say that they asked Ibn Abbas about iq'a on the feet and he said it is the Sunnah. They said we consider it harsh on the foot. Ibn Abbas said: rather it is the Sunnah of your Prophet. Principles: If the praying person turns his eyes here and there it is disliked, if he turns his face it is prohibitively disliked, and if he turns his chest the prayer becomes invalid. And he does not return the greeting with his tongue nor with his hand. Evidence: (1) The hadith for not returning the greeting with tongue or hand: from Zaid ibn Arqam who said we used to speak during prayer until the verse 'And stand before Allah in devout obedience' was revealed, so we were commanded to be silent and forbidden to speak. (2) (Shafi'i's proof) The hadith for not returning the greeting with tongue or hand: from Abdullah that the Prophet prayed and when he said salam he was asked if something had occurred in the prayer. He said: what is that? They said you prayed such and such. So he turned his legs and faced the qibla and prostrated two prostrations then said salam and said: if something had occurred in the prayer I would have informed you, but I am a human who forgets as you forget; so if I forget then remind me, and if any of you doubts his prayer let him seek what is correct and complete it then prostrate two prostrations. (3) The hadith for not returning the greeting with tongue or hand: from Jabir ibn Samura who said when we prayed with the Prophet we would say 'peace be upon you and mercy of Allah' and gesture with our hands, so the Prophet said: why do you gesture with your hands like the tails of wild horses? It is enough for one to place his hand on his thigh then greet his brother on the right and left. Principles: Speaking in prayer is not permissible, and according to the Hanafis if one speaks even out of forgetfulness the prayer becomes invalid.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a section on disliked acts (makruhat) in prayer from the Hanafi matn of Al-Quduri, expanded with hadith proofs. The text lists several specific actions that are makruh: letting the garment hang loosely (sadl), twisting or tying the hair, folding or tucking the garment, turning the face or body away from the qibla, sitting on the heels (iqa'), cracking the fingers, placing hands on hips (takhtsur), and returning the greeting of salam during prayer. Each ruling is supported by authentic hadith, mostly from the six major hadith collections. The commentary also includes a practical note (Usul) that distinguishes the degree of turning: merely turning the eyes is considered makruh tanzih (slightly disliked), turning the face is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), and turning the whole chest invalidates the prayer. The passage also addresses returning salam: the Hanafi position is that one should not respond to salam during prayer, neither with tongue nor with hand, based on the prohibition of speech in prayer and the command to be silent. Shafi'is argue for permissibility based on the hadith of the Prophet's forgetfulness and the hadith of Jabir about gesturing, but the Hanafi response emphasizes that those hadith are either abrogated or not evidence for responding to a greeting. The final principle (Usul) reaffirms that speaking in prayer, even forgetfully, invalidates it according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
سدل (sadl): Letting the garment hang down loosely without wrapping or securing it.
عقص الشعر (aqs al-sha'r): Twisting or tying the hair back during prayer.
إقعاء (iqa'): Sitting on the heels with the buttocks touching the ground, a posture between prostration and sitting.
اختلاس (ikhtilas): Snatching or snatching away; used to describe the action of Satan in taking away the reward of prayer through turning.
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): Prohibitively disliked; an action that is close to haram but not exactly, based on a zanni dalil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a person who cracks his fingers during prayer?
A) It invalidates the prayer.
B) It is makruh tanzih.
C) It is makruh tahrimi.
D) It is permissible.

Key Takeaway
Six specific acts are disliked in prayer, each supported by hadith, and turning the chest invalidates the prayer entirely.

Returning Salam During Prayer: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Dispute about returning salam during prayer with proofs from both sides

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on returning salam in prayer, identify the Shafi'i counter-argument, and apply the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Speaking or returning the greeting during prayer invalidates it; the Hanafi school maintains this even for forgetfulness, differing from Shafi'is.

This lesson focuses on a major point of ikhtilaf: returning the salam while in prayer. The Hanafi school rules that it is not permissible and if one speaks, the prayer is invalid, even if done forgetfully. The Shafi'is allow responding with gestures and even words under certain conditions. We will examine the proofs and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Returning salam is prohibited; speaking invalidates the prayer.
2
Identify the Hanafi dalil
Quran 2:238 and hadith of Zaid ibn Arqam on silence.
The verse commands standing in devout obedience, implying silence.
3
Identify the Shafi'i dalil
Hadith of the Prophet responding after forgetfulness and hadith of Jabir on gesturing.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The forgetfulness hadith is specific to the Prophet and not general; the gesture hadith is abrogated by the command to be silent.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafi says prayer invalid even if forgetful; Shafi'i says valid if forgetful.
This affects the need to repeat the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل مايكره في الصلوة
ولا يسدل ثوبه ولا يعقص شعره ولا يكف ثوبه ولا يلتفت ولا يقعي ولا يفرقع أصابعه ولا يتخصر. 
وجه: (١) الحديث لثبوت ولا يسدل ثوبه عن أبي هريرة أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى عن السدل في الصلاة وأن يغطي الرجل فاه (سنن أبي داود). 
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت ولا يعقص شعره عن أبي رافع أنه رأى حسن بن علي يصلي قائما وقد غرز ضفره في قفاه فحلها أبو رافع وقال سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: ذلك كفل الشيطان (سنن أبي داود، سنن الترمذي). 
وجه: (٣) الحديث لثبوت ولا يكف ثوبه عن ابن عباس عن النبي قال: أمرت أن أسجد على سبعة لا أكف شعرا ولا ثوبا (البخاري، مسلم). 
وجه: (٤) الحديث لثبوت ولا يلتفت عن عائشة قالت سألت رسول الله عن الالتفات في الصلاة فقال: هو اختلاس يختلسه الشيطان من صلاة العبد (البخاري، سنن أبي داود). 
وجه: (٥) الحديث لثبوت ولا يقعي عن سمرة بن جندب قال: نهى رسول الله عن الإقعاء في الصلاة (السنن الكبرى للبيهقي). 
وجه: (٦) قول التابعي لثبوت ولا يقعي سمع طاوسا يقول قلنا لابن عباس في الإقعاء على القدمين فقال: هي السنة. فقلنا له إنا لنراه جفاء بالرجل. فقال ابن عباس: بل هي سنة نبيك (مسلم). 
أصول: مصلي ادھر ادھر نظر پھیرے تو مکروہ، چہرہ پھر جائے تو مکروہ تحریمی، اور سینہ پھر جائے تو نماز فاسد۔
و ولا يرد السلام بلسانه ولا بيده. 
وجه: (١) الحديث لثبوت ولا يرد السلام بلسانه ولا بيده عن زيد بن أرقم قال كنا نتكلم في الصلاة حتى نزلت {وقوموا لله قانتين} فأمرنا بالسكوت ونهينا عن الكلام (مسلم، سنن الترمذي، سنن أبي داود). 
وجه: (٢) (دليل الشافعي) الحديث لثبوت ولا يرد السلام بلسانه ولا بيده عن عبد الله قال صلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فلما سلم قيل له أحدث في الصلاة شيء؟ قال: وما ذاك؟ قالوا صليت كذا وكذا، فثنى رجليه واستقبل القبلة فسجد سجدتين ثم سلم ثم قال: إنه لو حدث في الصلاة شيء أنبأتكم به، ولكن إنما أنا بشر أنسى كما تنسون، فإذا نسيت فذكروني، وإذا شك أحدكم في صلاته فليتحر الصواب ثم ليسجد سجدتين (مسلم، سنن الترمذي). 
وجه: (٣) الحديث لثبوت ولا يرد السلام بلسانه ولا بيده عن جابر بن سمرة قال كنا إذا صلينا مع رسول الله قلنا السلام عليكم ورحمة الله السلام عليكم ورحمة الله وأشار بيده إلى الجانبين فقال رسول الله: علام تومئون بأيديكم كأنها أذناب خيل شمس؟ إنما يكفي أحدكم أن يضع يده على فخذه ثم يسلم على أخيه من على يمينه وشماله (مسلم، سنن أبي داود). 
أصول: نماز میں کلام کرنا جائز نہیں، اور احناف کے نزدیک اگر بھول سے بھی بات کر لیا تو بھی نماز فاسد ہو گئی۔
Chapter on what is disliked in prayer. He does not let his garment hang down, nor does he twist his hair, nor does he fold his garment, nor does he turn away, nor does he sit on his heels, nor does he crack his fingers, nor does he put his hands on his hips. Evidence: (1) The hadith for not letting the garment hang down: from Abu Huraira that the Messenger of Allah forbade letting the garment hang down in prayer and covering the mouth. (2) The hadith for not twisting the hair: from Abu Rafi that he saw Hasan ibn Ali praying standing while he had inserted his braid at the back of his neck, so Abu Rafi undid it and said he heard the Prophet say: that is the portion of Satan. (3) The hadith for not folding the garment: from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet said: I have been commanded to prostrate on seven parts, not to fold hair or garment. (4) The hadith for not turning away: from Aisha who asked the Prophet about turning in prayer and he said: it is a snatch that Satan snatches from the prayer of the servant. (5) The hadith for not sitting on the heels: from Samura ibn Jundub that the Prophet forbade iq'a in prayer. (6) The statement of a follower: he heard Tawus say that they asked Ibn Abbas about iq'a on the feet and he said it is the Sunnah. They said we consider it harsh on the foot. Ibn Abbas said: rather it is the Sunnah of your Prophet. Principles: If the praying person turns his eyes here and there it is disliked, if he turns his face it is prohibitively disliked, and if he turns his chest the prayer becomes invalid. And he does not return the greeting with his tongue nor with his hand. Evidence: (1) The hadith for not returning the greeting with tongue or hand: from Zaid ibn Arqam who said we used to speak during prayer until the verse 'And stand before Allah in devout obedience' was revealed, so we were commanded to be silent and forbidden to speak. (2) (Shafi'i's proof) The hadith for not returning the greeting with tongue or hand: from Abdullah that the Prophet prayed and when he said salam he was asked if something had occurred in the prayer. He said: what is that? They said you prayed such and such. So he turned his legs and faced the qibla and prostrated two prostrations then said salam and said: if something had occurred in the prayer I would have informed you, but I am a human who forgets as you forget; so if I forget then remind me, and if any of you doubts his prayer let him seek what is correct and complete it then prostrate two prostrations. (3) The hadith for not returning the greeting with tongue or hand: from Jabir ibn Samura who said when we prayed with the Prophet we would say 'peace be upon you and mercy of Allah' and gesture with our hands, so the Prophet said: why do you gesture with your hands like the tails of wild horses? It is enough for one to place his hand on his thigh then greet his brother on the right and left. Principles: Speaking in prayer is not permissible, and according to the Hanafis if one speaks even out of forgetfulness the prayer becomes invalid.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a section on disliked acts (makruhat) in prayer from the Hanafi matn of Al-Quduri, expanded with hadith proofs. The text lists several specific actions that are makruh: letting the garment hang loosely (sadl), twisting or tying the hair, folding or tucking the garment, turning the face or body away from the qibla, sitting on the heels (iqa'), cracking the fingers, placing hands on hips (takhtsur), and returning the greeting of salam during prayer. Each ruling is supported by authentic hadith, mostly from the six major hadith collections. The commentary also includes a practical note (Usul) that distinguishes the degree of turning: merely turning the eyes is considered makruh tanzih (slightly disliked), turning the face is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked), and turning the whole chest invalidates the prayer. The passage also addresses returning salam: the Hanafi position is that one should not respond to salam during prayer, neither with tongue nor with hand, based on the prohibition of speech in prayer and the command to be silent. Shafi'is argue for permissibility based on the hadith of the Prophet's forgetfulness and the hadith of Jabir about gesturing, but the Hanafi response emphasizes that those hadith are either abrogated or not evidence for responding to a greeting. The final principle (Usul) reaffirms that speaking in prayer, even forgetfully, invalidates it according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
سدل (sadl): Letting the garment hang down loosely without wrapping or securing it.
عقص الشعر (aqs al-sha'r): Twisting or tying the hair back during prayer.
إقعاء (iqa'): Sitting on the heels with the buttocks touching the ground, a posture between prostration and sitting.
اختلاس (ikhtilas): Snatching or snatching away; used to describe the action of Satan in taking away the reward of prayer through turning.
مکروہ تحریمی (makruh tahrimi): Prohibitively disliked; an action that is close to haram but not exactly, based on a zanni dalil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if a person speaks during prayer to return a greeting, even if he does so forgetfully?
A) The prayer is valid but requires sujud al-sahw.
B) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
C) The prayer is valid because he forgot.
D) The prayer is valid if he gestures instead of speaking.

Key Takeaway
Returning the greeting during prayer, whether by speech or gesture, is prohibited; speaking invalidates the prayer completely.

Salah — Prayer

Nullifiers of Prayer: Speech and Events after Tashahhud
States rulings on talking, istinaf, and events after tashahhud with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on talking and events that nullify or complete prayer, and identify the respective proofs.

Core Idea
Talking invalidates prayer; after tashahhud, an intentional event completes it, but an unintentional event requires wudu and taslim.

This passage from Al-Quduri presents key rulings on what invalidates prayer and what does not. It distinguishes between major nullifiers requiring istinaf, speech invalidating the prayer, and the unique status of events after tashahhud. The proofs from Quran and Sunnah solidify the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the major nullifiers requiring istinaf
Look at the list: sleep with janabah, looking with ejaculation, insanity, fainting, and laughing out loud. These require renewing both wudu and prayer.
Istinaf means starting completely over.
2
Understand the ruling on talking in prayer
The text states that talking intentionally or forgetfully invalidates the prayer. Note the universal scope.
Shafi'is differ on forgetful talking.
3
Analyze the proof for prohibition of speech
The hadith 'This prayer does not contain any speech of people' and the verse 'Qumoo lillahi qaniteen' are cited. The command 'qaniteen' implies silence.
The proof is clear and binding.
4
Distinguish between intentional and unintentional events after tashahhud
If an event occurs unintentionally after tashahhud, renew wudu and say taslim; the prayer is not invalidated. If intentional, the prayer is complete and valid.
The hadith from Abdullah ibn Amr supports this.
5
Note the consequence when the prayer is complete
After tashahhud, the essential parts of prayer are done. Intentional nullifiers like speech or hadath do not break it.
This is a specific Hanafi ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالِاسْتِتْنَافُ أَفْضَلُ فَإِنْ نَامَ فَاحْتَلَمَ أَوْ نَظَرَ إِلَى امْرَأَةٍ فَأَنْزَلَ أَوْ جُنَّ أَوْ أُغْمِيَ عَلَيْهِ أَوْ قَهْقَهَ اسْتَأَنَفَ الْوُضُوءَ وَالصَّلَاةَ جَمِيعًا ١٣ فَإِنْ تَكَلَّمَ فِي صَلَاتِهِ عَامِدًا أَوْ سَاهِيًا بَطَلَتْ صَلَاتُهُ ١٢ وَإِنْ سَبَقَهُ الْحَدَثُ بَعْدَ التَّشَهُدِ تَوَضَّأَ وَسَلَّمَ ١٥ وَإِنْ تَعَمَّدَ الْحَدَثَ فِي هَذِهِ الْحَالَةِ أَوْ تَكَلَّمَ أَوْ عَمِلَ عَمَلًا يُنَا فِي الصَّلَاةَ تَمَّتْ صَلَاتُهُ أَلَا تُحَدِّثِينِي عَنْ مَرَضِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَكَانَ أَبُو بَكْرٍ يُصَلِّي وَهُوَ قَائِمٌ بِصَلَاةِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَالنَّاسُ يُصَلُّونَ بِصَلَاةِ أَبي بَكْرٍ وَالنَّبِيُّ صَلَّى الله عليه السلام قَاعِدٌ (مسلم شریف، باب اسْتِخْلَافِ الإِمَامِ إِذَا عَرَضَ لَهُ عُذْرٌ مِنْ مَرَضِ وَسَفَرٍ وَغَيْرِهِمَا مَنْ يُصَلِّي بِالنَّاسِ، وَأَنَّ مَنْ صَلَّى خَلْفَ إِمَامٍ جَالِسِ لِعَجْزِهِ عَنِ الْقِيَامِ لَزِمَهُ الْقِيَامُ إِذَا قَدَرَ عَلَيْهِ، وَنَسْخُ الْقُعُودِ خَلْفَ الْقَاعِدِ فِي حَقِّ مَنْ قَدَرَ عَلَى الْقِيَامِ 418\ صحيح البخاري بَابٌ : إِنَّمَا جُعِلَ الْإِمَامُ لِيُؤْتَمَّ بِهِ، رقم ، 687) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ تَكَلَّمَ فِي صَلَاتِهِ عَامِدًا \ عَنْ زَيْدِ بْنِ أَرْقَمَ؛ قَالَ كُنَّا نَتَكَلَّمُ فِي الصَّلَاةِ. يُكَلِّمُ الرَّجُلُ صَاحِبَهُ وَهُوَ إِلَى جَنْبِهِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ. حَتَّى نَزَلَتْ: {وَقُومُوا لِلَّهِ قَانِتِينَ} [2/ البقرة الآية 238] فأمرنا بالسكوت، ونهينا عن الكلام (مسلم شریف، بَاب تَحْرِيمِ الْكَلَامِ في الصَّلَاةِ، وَنَسْخِ مَا كان من إباحة، 539/سنن ترمذي، بَابٌ فِي نَسْخِ الكَلَامِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ، 405) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَرُدُّ السَّلَامَ بِلِسَانِهِ عَنْ مُعَاوِيَةَ بْنِ الْحَكَمِ السُّلَمِيِّ؛ قَالَ بَيْنَا أَنَا أُصَلِّي مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ . قَالَ إِنَّ هَذِهِ الصَّلَاةَ لَا يَصْلُحُ فِيهَا شَيْءٌ مِنْ كَلَامِ النَّاسِ. إِنَّمَا هُوَ التَّسْبِيحُ وَالتَّكْبِيرُ وَقِرَاءَةُ الْقُرْآنِ مسلم شریف ، بَاب تَحْرِيمِ الْكَلَامِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ، وَنَسْحَ مَا كان من إباحة، نمبر 537) أَنَّ ها وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ تَعَمَّدَ الْحَدَثَ فِي هَذِهِ الْحَالَةِ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرِو، رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إِذَا قَضَى الْإِمَامُ الصَّلَاةَ وَقَعَدَ فَأَحْدَثَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَتَكَلَّمَ، فَقَدْ تَمَّتْ صَلَاتُهُ، وَمَنْ كَانَ خَلْفَهُ مِمَّنْ أَتَمَّ الصَّلَاةَ ، ( سنن ابوداود، بَابُ الْإِمَامِ يُحْدِثُ بَعْدَ مَا يَرْفَعُ رَأْسَهُ مِنْ آخِرِ الرَّكْعَةِ، نمبر 617\ سنن دارقطني، بَابُ مَنْ أَحْدَثَ قَبْلَ التَسْلِيمِ فِي آخِرِ صَلَاتِهِ أَوْ أَحْدَثَ قَبْلَ تَسْلِيمِ الْإِمَامِ فَقَدْ تَمَّتْ صَلَاتُهُ، رقم (1407) اصول: امام کو نماز میں حدث لاحق ہو جائے تو مقتدی میں سے کسی کو خلیفہ بنائے اور اصلی امام وضوء کر نماز کی بناء کرے گا۔
And renewing (istinaf) is better. So if he sleeps and has a wet dream, or looks at a woman and emits, or becomes insane, or becomes unconscious, or laughs out loud, he renews both wudu and prayer. If he speaks in his prayer intentionally or forgetfully, his prayer is invalidated. If an event (hadath) overtakes him after the tashahhud, he performs wudu and says taslim. If he intentionally causes an event in this state, or speaks, or does an action that contradicts the prayer, his prayer is complete. ... Hadith evidence for each ruling.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with hadith proofs. It addresses key nullifiers of prayer. First, the author mentions situations that require renewing both wudu and prayer (istinaf): sleep with janabah, looking with ejaculation, insanity, fainting, and laughing. These invalidate both wudu and prayer. Then the main ruling: talking intentionally or forgetfully nullifies prayer. The hadith from Zaid ibn Arqam and Muawiya ibn Hakam prove that speech is forbidden in prayer. Next, if a person has a hadath (like passing wind) after tashahhud but before taslim, he must renew wudu and then say taslim - the prayer is not invalidated. The hadith from Abdullah ibn Amr supports this. Finally, if someone intentionally has a hadath, speaks, or does a contradictory action after tashahhud, the prayer is complete (valid) because the essential parts are done. The Urdu note at the end explains that if the imam has a hadath, someone from the congregation should be made deputy (khalifa) and the original imam should renew wudu and build upon the prayer.

Key Terms
استئناف (istinaf): Renewing both wudu and prayer from the beginning.
حدث (hadath): Any ritual impurity that breaks wudu (e.g., passing wind).
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony recited while sitting in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone intentionally speaks after tashahhud but before taslim, what is the ruling?
A) Prayer is invalidated.
B) Prayer is complete and valid.
C) Prayer requires sujud al-sahw.
D) He must repeat both wudu and prayer.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, speech invalidates prayer unless it occurs after tashahhud, where intentional nullifiers do not break the prayer.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Tayammum and Seeing Water After Tashahhud
Rules on tayammum seeing water and various cases; ends with Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule of tayammum invalidation upon seeing water and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding seeing water after sitting for tashahhud.

Core Idea
Seeing water during tayammum prayer invalidates it, but after tashahhud the Sahibayn deem it valid.

This lesson examines a series of rulings where a person performing tayammum sees water during prayer, along with related scenarios. The passage culminates in an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two illustrious students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, on whether seeing water after the tashahhud invalidates the prayer. Understanding this difference is crucial for knowing when a prayer must be repeated and when it is considered complete.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Take note of the opening ruling: if a mutayammim sees water at any point during prayer, it invalidates the prayer entirely.
This is based on the statement of Hasan al-Basri and is the default position.
2
Recognize the Exception Scenario
Observe the specific scenario: 'if he sees it after sitting for the measure of tashahhud'. This is where the ikhtilaf arises.
Tashahhud is recited while sitting; the measure of tashahhud is a specific posture.
3
State Abu Hanifa's Position
Abu Hanifa holds that even after tashahhud, the prayer remains incomplete because taslim is still wajib. Seeing water therefore invalidates it.
His principle: the prayer is not over until taslim is pronounced.
4
State the Sahibayn's Position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani argue that since all faraid (rukn) are complete, the prayer is valid, albeit with a deficiency (naqs). The taslim is not a rukn.
They cite the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'When you have said this (tashahhud), you have completed your prayer.'
5
Analyze the Practical Consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: under Abu Hanifa, the mutayammim must restart the prayer; under the Sahibayn, he may complete the taslim and the prayer is valid.
Later Hanafi fatwa practice may lean towards the Sahibayn for ease, but the text does not give a tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا رَأَى الْمُتَيَمَّمُ الْمَاءَ فِي صَلَاتِهِ بَطَلَتْ كل فَإِنْ رَآهُ بَعْدَمَا قَعَدَ قَدْرَ التَّشَهُدِ أَوْ كَانَ مَاسِحًا فَانْقَضَتْ مُدَّةُ مَسْحِهِ إِلَى آخِرِهِ أَوْ كَانَ مَاسِحًا فَانْقَضَتْ مُدَّةُ مَسْحِهِ أَوْ خَلَعَ خُفَّيْهِ بِعَمَلِ رَفِيقِ أَوْ كَانَ أُمِّيًّا فَتَعَلَّمَ سُورَةً أَوْ عُرْيَانًا فَوَجَدَ ثَوْبًا أَوْ تَذَكَّرَ أَنَّ عَلَيْهِ صَلَاةً فَائِتَةً قَبْلَ هَذِهِ أَوْ أَحْدَثَ الْإِمَامُ الْقَارِئُ فَاسْتَخْلَفَ أُمِيًّا : (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ تَعَمَّدَ الْحَدَثَ فِي هَذِهِ الْحَالَةِ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إِذَا جَلَسَ الْإِمَامُ فِي آخِرِ رَكْعَةٍ ثُمَّ أَحْدَثَ رَجُلٌ مِنْ خَلْفِهِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يُسَلَّمَ الْإِمَامُ فَقَدْ تَمَّتْ صَلَاتُهُ ) سنن دارقطني ، بَابُ مَنْ أَحْدَثَ قَبْلَ التَّسْلِيمِ فِي آخِرِ صَلَاتِهِ أَوْ أَحْدَثَ قَبْلَ تَسْلِيمِ الْإِمَامِ فَقَدْ تَمتْ صَلَاتُهُ، رقم (1407) وجه: (3) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ تَعَمَّدَ الْحَدَثَ فِي هَذِهِ الْحَالَةِ \ عَنْ عَلِيَّ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «مِفْتَاحُ الصَّلَاةِ الطُّهُورُ، وَتَحْرِيمُهَا التَّكْبِيرُ ، وَتَحْلِيلُها التَّسْلِيمُ ، ( سنن الترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ أَنَّ مِفْتَاحَ الصَّلَاةِ الطُّهُورُ، نمبر 3\ سنن ابوداود بَابُ الْإِمَامِ يُحْدِثُ بَعْدَ مَا يَرْفَعُ رَأْسَهُ مِنْ آخِرِ الرَّكْعَةِ، نمبر (618) وجه: (ا)قول التابعي لثبوت وَإِذَا رَأَى الْمُتَيَمَّمُ الْمَاءَ فِي صَلَاتِهِ بَطَلَتْ \ عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، أَنَّهُ قَالَ فِي مُتَيَمِمٍ مَرَّ بِمَاءٍ غَيْرَ مُحْتَاجِ إِلَى الْوُضُوءِ فَجَاوَزَهُ، فَحَضَرْتِ الصَّلَاةُ وَلَيْسَ مَعَهُ مَاءٌ، قَالَ: يُعِيدُ التَّيَمُّمَ، لِأَنَّ قُدْرَتَهُ عَلَى الْمَاءِ تُنْقِصُ تَيَمُّمَهُ الْأَوَّلَ ، مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، فِي مُتَيَمِّمٍ مَرَّ بِمَاءٍ فَجَاوَزَهُ ، نمبر 2026) ا وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ رَآهُ بَعْدَمَا قَعَدَ قَدْرَ التَّشَهُدِ \ أَنَّ عَبْدَ اللَّهِ بْنَ مَسْعُودٍ، أَخَذَ بِيَدِهِ، وَأَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَخَذَ بِيَدِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، فَعَلَّمَهُ التَّشَهدَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ، فَذَكَرَ مِثْلَ دُعَاءِ حَدِيثِ الْأَعْمَشِ: «إِذَا قُلْتَ هَذَا أَوْ قَضَيْتَ هَذَا فَقَدْ قَضَيْتَ صَلَاتَكَ، إِنْ شِئْتَ أَنْ تَقُومَ فَقُمْ، وَإِنْ اصول : امام ابو حنیفہ : تشہد کے بعد نماز میں خلیفہ کے بجائے اصل پر قدرت ہو گئی تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی کیونکہ ابھی نماز باقی ہے۔ اصول : صاحبین: تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد نماز میں خلیفہ کے بجائے اصل پر قدرت ہو گئی تو پوری ہو جائے کی کمی کیساتھ ، کیونکہ تمام فرائض پورے ہو چکے۔
And if the one who performs tayammum sees water during his prayer, it invalidates it all. If he sees it after sitting for the measure of tashahhud, or if he was wiping (masah) and the period of his wiping expired, or he removes his khuffs with gentle action, or he was unlettered and learns a surah, or he was naked and finds clothing, or he remembers that he has a missed prayer before this, or the imam who is qari has a hadath and appoints an unlettered deputy… Hadith evidence. Then the dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa says if after tashahhud he is able to perform the original (i.e., without the deputy), the prayer becomes invalid because there remains some of the prayer. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say if after sitting for the measure of tashahhud he is able to perform the original, it is complete, albeit with deficiency, because all the faraid have been completed.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings that cause invalidation (butlan) of prayer, along with hadith proofs, and ends with an intra-Hanafi dispute. The first ruling: if a person performing tayammum sees water during prayer, his prayer is invalidated. This is proven by a statement of Hasan al-Basri. Then various other scenarios: if after sitting for tashahhud he sees water (or similar), or if his masah period expires, or he removes khuffs, or an ummi learns a surah, a naked person finds clothing, remembers a missed prayer, or the qari imam has a hadath and appoints an ummi deputy — in all these cases the prayer is invalidated. The hadith from Ibn Mas'ud about tashahhud indicates that after reciting the tashahhud, the prayer is considered complete. The dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that if after sitting for tashahhud the original (i.e., the imam or oneself) becomes able to perform without deputy, the prayer becomes invalid because there is still some part of prayer remaining (i.e., salutation). The Sahibayn hold that since all faraid (obligatory pillars) are complete, the prayer is valid, albeit with a deficiency (naqs).

Key Terms
متيمم (mutayammim): One who performs dry ablution (tayammum) due to lack of water.
قعد قدر التشهد (qa'ada qadr al-tashahhud): Sitting for the duration necessary to recite the tashahhud.
أمّي (ummi): Someone who cannot recite Quran properly (unlettered).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when a mutayammim sees water after sitting for the measure of tashahhud?
A) The prayer is invalid according to all Hanafis.
B) Abu Hanifa says invalid; Sahibayn say valid with deficiency.
C) The prayer is valid and complete.
D) The prayer is invalid only if water was available earlier.

Key Takeaway
Seeing water after tashahhud incurs an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa declares invalidity, Sahibayn see completion.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Prayer Invalidated by Availability of Original: The Hanafi Principle
A set of rulings establishing that when the original becomes available during prayer, the substitute is invalid and the prayer is void.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that prayer becomes invalid when the original becomes available during prayer, and cite the hadith proof used by Imam Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
The prayer is only concluded by salam — until then, availability of the original invalidates the substitute.

When a person uses a substitute in prayer (like tayammum for water, wiping over khuffs, etc.) due to necessity, the substitute is valid only as long as the original is unavailable. If the original becomes available during the prayer, the substitute loses its validity. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the prayer becomes invalid in such cases because the prayer is still ongoing until the final salam, based on the hadith that 'the key of prayer is purification, its forbiddance is takbir, and its release is salam.' This lesson explores that ruling and its application to several scenarios.

Guided Path
1
List the scenarios
Identify the cases given in the text: mutayammim sees water, wiping period expires, khuffs removed, illiterate learns a surah, naked finds clothing, remembers missed prayer, imam's hadath, etc.
Each scenario involves a substitute (tayammum, wiping, etc.) and the original (water, garment, etc.) becoming available.
2
Understand the principle
The substitute is valid only as long as the original is absent. When the original becomes accessible, the substitute's ruling ends retroactively.
This is based on the idea that the substitute is granted because of necessity; when necessity ends, the substitute ends.
3
Identify Abu Hanifa's proof
The hadith: 'مفتاح الصلاة الطهور، وتحريمها التكبير، وتحليلها التسليم' (The key of prayer is purification, its forbiddance is takbir, its release is salam).
Since the prayer is only released by salam, it is still ongoing until that point. Therefore, if the original becomes available, the substitute is invalid and the prayer breaks.
4
Apply to each scenario
For each case, the original became available before salam, so prayer is invalid according to Abu Hanifa.
This is the view of Imam Abu Hanifa; his students (Sahibayn) differ for cases after tashahhud, which will be covered in the next lesson.

فصل مايكره في الصلوة وَإِذَا رَأَى الْمُتَيَمَّمُ الْمَاءَ فِي صَلَاتِهِ بَطَلَتْ كل فَإِنْ رَآهُ بَعْدَمَا قَعَدَ قَدْرَ التَّشَهُدِ أَوْ كَانَ مَاسِحًا فَانْقَضَتْ مُدَّةُ مَسْحِهِ إِلَى آخِرِهِ أَوْ كَانَ مَاسِحًا فَانْقَضَتْ مُدَّةُ مَسْحِهِ أَوْ خَلَعَ خُفَّيْهِ بِعَمَلِ رَفِيقِ أَوْ كَانَ أُمِّيَّا فَتَعَلَّمَ سُورَةً أَوْ عُرْيَانًا فَوَجَدَ ثَوْبًا أَوْ تَذَكَّرَ أَنَّ عَلَيْهِ صَلَاةً فَائِتَةً قَبْلَ هَذِهِ أَوْ أَحْدَثَ الْإِمَامُ الْقَارِئُ فَاسْتَخْلَفَ أُمِيًّا : (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ تَعَمَّدَ الْحَدَثَ فِي هَذِهِ الْحَالَةِ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو ، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إِذَا جَلَسَ الْإِمَامُ فِي آخِرِ رَكْعَةٍ ثُمَّ أَحْدَثَ رَجُلٌ مِنْ خَلْفِهِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يُسَلَّمَ الْإِمَامُ فَقَدْ تَمَّتْ صَلَاتُهُ ) سنن دارقطني ، بَابُ مَنْ أَحْدَثَ قَبْلَ التَّسْلِيمِ فِي آخِرِ صَلَاتِهِ أَوْ أَحْدَثَ قَبْلَ تَسْلِيمِ الْإِمَامِ فَقَدْ تَمتْ صَلَاتُهُ، رقم (1407) وجه: (3) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ تَعَمَّدَ الْحَدَثَ فِي هَذِهِ الْحَالَةِ \ عَنْ عَلِيَّ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «مِفْتَاحُ الصَّلَاةِ الطُّهُورُ، وَتَحْرِيمُهَا التَّكْبِيرُ ، وَتَحْلِيلُها التَّسْلِيمُ ، ( سنن الترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ أَنَّ مِفْتَاحَ الصَّلَاةِ الطُّهُورُ، نمبر 3\ سنن ابوداود بَابُ الْإِمَامِ يُحْدِثُ بَعْدَ مَا يَرْفَعُ رَأْسَهُ مِنْ آخِرِ الرَّكْعَةِ، نمبر (618) وجه: (ا)قول التابعي لثبوت وَإِذَا رَأَى الْمُتَيَمَّمُ الْمَاءَ فِي صَلَاتِهِ بَطَلَتْ \ عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، أَنَّهُ قَالَ فِي مُتَيَمِمٍ مَرَّ بِمَاءٍ غَيْرَ مُحْتَاجِ إِلَى الْوُضُوءِ فَجَاوَزَهُ، فَحَضَرْتِ الصَّلَاةُ وَلَيْسَ مَعَهُ مَاءٌ، قَالَ: يُعِيدُ التَّيَمُّمَ، لِأَنَّ قُدْرَتَهُ عَلَى الْمَاءِ تُنْقِصُ تَيَمُّمَهُ الْأَوَّلَ ، مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، فِي مُتَيَمِّمٍ مَرَّ بِمَاءٍ فَجَاوَزَهُ ، نمبر 2026) ا وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ رَآهُ بَعْدَمَا قَعَدَ قَدْرَ التَّشَهُدِ \ أَنَّ عَبْدَ اللَّهِ بْنَ مَسْعُودٍ، أَخَذَ بِيَدِهِ، وَأَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَخَذَ بِيَدِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، فَعَلَّمَهُ التَّشَهدَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ، فَذَكَرَ مِثْلَ دُعَاءِ حَدِيثِ الْأَعْمَشِ: «إِذَا قُلْتَ هَذَا أَوْ قَضَيْتَ هَذَا فَقَدْ قَضَيْتَ صَلَاتَكَ، إِنْ شِئْتَ أَنْ تَقُومَ فَقُمْ، وَإِنْ اصول : امام ابو حنیفہ : تشہد کے بعد نماز میں خلیفہ کے بجائے اصل پر قدرت ہو گئی تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی کیونکہ ابھی نماز باقی ہے۔ اصول : صاحبین: تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنے کے بعد نماز میں خلیفہ کے بجائے اصل پر قدرت ہو گئی تو پوری ہو جائے کی کمی کیساتھ ، کیونکہ تمام فرائض پورے ہو چکے۔ أَوْ طَلَعَتْ الشَّمْسُ وَهُوَ فِي صَلَاةِ الْفَجْرِ أَوْ دَخَلَ وَقْتُ الْعَصْرِ وَهُوَ فِي صَلَاةِ الجُمُعَةِ أَوْ كَانَ مَاسِحًا عَلَى الْخَبِيرَةِ فَسَقَطَتْ عَنْ بُرْءٍ بَطَلَتْ صَلَاتُهُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ تَمَّتْ صَلَاتُهُ شِئْتَ أَنْ تَقْعُدَ فَاقْعُدْ، سنن ابوداود بَابُ التَّشَهدِ، نمبر 970) وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت أَوْ طَلَعَتْ الشَّمْسُ وَهُوَ فِي صَلَاةِ الْفَجْرِ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: «نَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ صَلَاتَيْنِ بَعْدَ الْفَجْرِ حَتَّى تَطْلُعَ الشَّمْسُ، وَبَعْدَ الْعَصْرِ حَتَّى تَغْرُبَ الشَّمْسُ ، ( صحيح البخاري، بَابٌ : لَا يَتَحَرَّى الصَّلَاةُ قَبْلَ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ، نمبر 1588) وجه : (٢) الحديث لثبوت أَوْ طَلَعَتْ الشَّمْسُ وَهُوَ فِي صَلَاةِ الْفَجْرِ \ أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ أَبَا سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيَّ يَقُولُ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ: «لا صَلَاةَ بَعْدَ الصُّبْحِ حَتَّى تَرْتَفِعَ الشَّمْسُ وَلَا صَلَاةَ بَعْدَ الْعَصْرِ حَتَّى تَغِيبَ الشَّمْسُ، صحيح البخاري، بَابٌ: لَا يَتَحَرَّى الصَّلَاةُ قَبْلَ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ، نمبر 586\مسلم شريف ، بَابُ الْأَوْقَاتِ الَّتِي هِيَ عَنِ الصَّلَاةِ فِيهَا، رقم 827) « لغات : فَانْقَضَتْ : ختم ہونا، خَلَعَ : اتارنا، أُمَيَّا : ان پڑھ جو ایک آیت بھی نہ جانتا ہو، عُریانا : ننگا، صَلَاةَ فَائِتَةً : متروکہ نمازیں، چھوٹی نمازیں، أَحْدَثَ : حدث لاحق ہونا، اسْتَخْلَفَ : خلیفہ بنانا، نائب بنانا، طَلَعَتْ الشَّمْسُ : سورج لكلنا الجبيرة : کھچی، سَقَطَتْ : گرنا، بُرء : ٹھیک ہوتا، بطلتْ : باطل ہونا ۔
Chapter on what is disliked in prayer. And when the one who performs tayammum sees water during his prayer, it becomes invalid. But if he sees it after he has sat to the extent of the tashahhud, or if he was wiping (over khuffs) and the period of his wiping expired to its end, or if he was wiping and the period of his wiping expired, or if he removed his khuffs with gentle action, or if he was illiterate and then learned a surah, or if he was naked and then found a garment, or if he remembered that he has a missed prayer before this one, or if the reciting imam had an event (hadath) and appointed an illiterate person as substitute: (2) The hadith for the ruling: And if he deliberately committed hadath in this situation, from Abdullah ibn Amr that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When the imam sits in the last rak'ah and then a man behind him has an event before the imam says salam, his prayer is complete.' (Sunan Darqutni, chapter on one who has an event before salam in his last prayer or has an event before the imam's salam, his prayer is complete, no. 1407) Evidence: (3) The hadith for the ruling: And if he deliberately committed hadath in this situation, from Ali, from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The key of prayer is purification, its forbiddance is the takbir, and its release is the salam.' (Sunan Tirmidhi, chapter on that the key of prayer is purification, no. 3; Sunan Abu Dawud, chapter on the imam having an event after raising his head from the last rak'ah, no. 618) Evidence: (a) The saying of the tabi'i for the ruling: And when the mutayammim sees water during his prayer, it becomes invalid. From Hasan that he said about a mutayammim who passed by water without needing wudu and bypassed it, then the prayer time came and he had no water, he said: He should repeat the tayammum because his ability to access water reduces his first tayammum. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, on a mutayammim who passed by water and bypassed it, no. 2026) And evidence: (1) The hadith for the ruling: Then if he sees it after he has sat the extent of tashahhud. That Abdullah ibn Mas'ud took his hand, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) took Abdullah's hand and taught him the tashahhud in prayer, and he mentioned a similar supplication to the hadith of al-A'mash: 'When you say this or you complete this, you have completed your prayer. If you wish to stand, then stand, and if you wish to sit, then sit.' (Sunan Abu Dawud, chapter on tashahhud, no. 970) Principle: Imam Abu Hanifa: After tashahhud, if one gains ability over the original (i.e., water, clothing, etc.) instead of the substitute, the prayer becomes invalid because the prayer is still remaining. Principle: The Sahibayn: After sitting the extent of tashahhud, if one gains ability over the original instead of the substitute, the prayer is complete with deficiency because all obligations have been fulfilled. Or if the sun rises while he is in the Fajr prayer, or if the time of Asr enters while he is in the Friday prayer, or if he was wiping over the splint and it fell off due to healing, his prayer becomes invalid according to Abu Hanifa, and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: His prayer is complete. (Hadith evidence for sunrise: from Abu Hurairah said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade two prayers: after Fajr until the sun rises, and after Asr until the sun sets.' (Sahih Bukhari, chapter on not seeking prayer before sunset, no. 1588) Evidence: (2) The hadith for the ruling: Or if the sun rises while he is in Fajr prayer. That he heard Abu Sa'id al-Khudri say: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'No prayer after dawn until the sun rises, and no prayer after Asr until the sun sets.' (Sahih Bukhari, chapter on not seeking prayer before sunset, no. 586; Sahih Muslim, chapter on times when prayer is forbidden, no. 827) Glossary: فَانْقَضَتْ: ended; خَلَعَ: removed; أُمَيَّا: illiterate (one who does not know even one verse); عُریانا: naked; صَلَاةَ فَائِتَةً: missed prayers; أَحْدَثَ: to have an event (hadath); اسْتَخْلَفَ: to appoint a substitute; طَلَعَتْ الشَّمْسُ: the sun rises; الجبيرة: splint; سَقَطَتْ: fell; بُرء: healing; بطلت: becomes invalid.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage is a series of rulings from the matn of al-Quduri regarding conditions that either invalidate the prayer or render it complete, followed by hadith proofs and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The first ruling: if a person performing tayammum sees water during prayer, the prayer becomes invalid because the substitute (tayammum) is no longer valid when the original (water) is available. However, if he sees it after sitting for the extent of tashahhud, the prayer is considered complete according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), based on the hadith from Ibn Mas'ud that after completing tashahhud, the prayer is complete. Imam Abu Hanifa disagrees, holding that since the final salam has not been said, the prayer is still ongoing and seeing water invalidates it. The hadith of the key of prayer (from Ali) supports that release is only by salam, so until salam, the prayer continues. Similarly, if the period of wiping over khuffs expires, or if he removes khuffs gently, or if an illiterate person learns a surah, or a naked person finds clothing, or remembers a missed prayer, or if the imam has an event and appoints an illiterate follower – in all these cases, the original becomes available and the substitute is invalid, thus prayer becomes invalid (according to Abu Hanifa) or complete (Sahibayn). The text then presents a second set: sunrise during Fajr, entering Asr time during Jumu'ah, or a splint falling off after healing – Abu Hanifa says prayer becomes invalid because the time for that prayer has ended or the excuse (splint) is gone; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say prayer is complete as obligations were fulfilled. The hadith evidence for sunrise prohibition is cited from Bukhari and Muslim.

Key Terms
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited while sitting in the last rak'ah of prayer.
المتيمم (al-mutayammim): One who performs dry ablution (tayammum) due to lack of water or inability to use it.
الحديث (al-hadith): The prophetic tradition; here cited as evidence for the rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith 'مفتاح الصلاة الطهور، وتحريمها التكبير، وتحليلها التسليم', what does 'تحليلها' (its release) refer to?
A) The tashahhud
B) The salam
C) The takbir
D) The purification

Key Takeaway
The prayer is considered ongoing until the final salam; any event that ends the necessity for a substitute invalidates the prayer if it occurs before salam.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
10 min
The Sahibayn's Exception: Prayer Completion After Tashahhud
Intra-Hanafi dispute over whether prayer is complete after sitting for tashahhud when the original becomes available.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Sahibayn's view that prayer is complete after sitting for tashahhud, and evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf with Abu Hanifa's position.

Core Idea
After the tashahhud, the essential obligations are fulfilled — the prayer is considered complete despite the original becoming available before salam.

While Imam Abu Hanifa holds that prayer is invalid until the final salam, his two main students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), carve out an exception: if the original (water, clothing, etc.) becomes available after the person has sat for the duration of the tashahhud, the prayer is considered complete. Their proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that upon completing the tashahhud, one has completed his prayer. This lesson explores this intra-Hanafi dispute and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Recall the general rule
Abu Hanifa says prayer invalid if original becomes available before salam.
2
Understand the Sahibayn's exception
They make an exception for when the original becomes available after sitting for the duration of tashahhud.
The key phrase: 'بعدما قعد قدر التشهد' (after sitting the extent of tashahhud).
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'إذَا قُلْتَ هَذَا أَوْ قَضَيْتَ هَذَا فَقَدْ قَضَيْتَ صَلَاتَكَ' – when you say this (tashahhud) or complete this, you have completed your prayer.
This indicates completion after tashahhud, not at salam.
4
Examine Abu Hanifa's rebuttal
He interprets the hadith as meaning completion in terms of obligations, not termination of the prayer state. The key of prayer hadith shows that only salam releases.
Thus, Abu Hanifa sees no conflict; both hadiths are reconciled by distinguishing between fulfillment of actions and ending the prayer.
5
Apply to all scenarios
For all the same scenarios (mutayammim sees water, wiping expires, illiterate learns surah, etc.), if the original appears after tashahhud, the Sahibayn say prayer is complete; if before, invalid. The same dispute applies to sunrise during Fajr, Asr time entering during Jumu'ah, and splint falling off.
The threshold of tashahhud is consistent across all cases.

Chapter on what is disliked in prayer. And when the one who performs tayammum sees water during his prayer, it becomes invalid. But if he sees it after he has sat to the extent of the tashahhud, or if he was wiping (over khuffs) and the period of his wiping expired to its end, or if he was wiping and the period of his wiping expired, or if he removed his khuffs with gentle action, or if he was illiterate and then learned a surah, or if he was naked and then found a garment, or if he remembered that he has a missed prayer before this one, or if the reciting imam had an event (hadath) and appointed an illiterate person as substitute: (2) The hadith for the ruling: And if he deliberately committed hadath in this situation, from Abdullah ibn Amr that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'When the imam sits in the last rak'ah and then a man behind him has an event before the imam says salam, his prayer is complete.' (Sunan Darqutni, chapter on one who has an event before salam in his last prayer or has an event before the imam's salam, his prayer is complete, no. 1407) Evidence: (3) The hadith for the ruling: And if he deliberately committed hadath in this situation, from Ali, from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The key of prayer is purification, its forbiddance is the takbir, and its release is the salam.' (Sunan Tirmidhi, chapter on that the key of prayer is purification, no. 3; Sunan Abu Dawud, chapter on the imam having an event after raising his head from the last rak'ah, no. 618) Evidence: (a) The saying of the tabi'i for the ruling: And when the mutayammim sees water during his prayer, it becomes invalid. From Hasan that he said about a mutayammim who passed by water without needing wudu and bypassed it, then the prayer time came and he had no water, he said: He should repeat the tayammum because his ability to access water reduces his first tayammum. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, on a mutayammim who passed by water and bypassed it, no. 2026) And evidence: (1) The hadith for the ruling: Then if he sees it after he has sat the extent of tashahhud. That Abdullah ibn Mas'ud took his hand, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) took Abdullah's hand and taught him the tashahhud in prayer, and he mentioned a similar supplication to the hadith of al-A'mash: 'When you say this or you complete this, you have completed your prayer. If you wish to stand, then stand, and if you wish to sit, then sit.' (Sunan Abu Dawud, chapter on tashahhud, no. 970) Principle: Imam Abu Hanifa: After tashahhud, if one gains ability over the original (i.e., water, clothing, etc.) instead of the substitute, the prayer becomes invalid because the prayer is still remaining. Principle: The Sahibayn: After sitting the extent of tashahhud, if one gains ability over the original instead of the substitute, the prayer is complete with deficiency because all obligations have been fulfilled. Or if the sun rises while he is in the Fajr prayer, or if the time of Asr enters while he is in the Friday prayer, or if he was wiping over the splint and it fell off due to healing, his prayer becomes invalid according to Abu Hanifa, and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: His prayer is complete. (Hadith evidence for sunrise: from Abu Hurairah said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade two prayers: after Fajr until the sun rises, and after Asr until the sun sets.' (Sahih Bukhari, chapter on not seeking prayer before sunset, no. 1588) Evidence: (2) The hadith for the ruling: Or if the sun rises while he is in Fajr prayer. That he heard Abu Sa'id al-Khudri say: I heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'No prayer after dawn until the sun rises, and no prayer after Asr until the sun sets.' (Sahih Bukhari, chapter on not seeking prayer before sunset, no. 586; Sahih Muslim, chapter on times when prayer is forbidden, no. 827) Glossary: فَانْقَضَتْ: ended; خَلَعَ: removed; أُمَيَّا: illiterate (one who does not know even one verse); عُریانا: naked; صَلَاةَ فَائِتَةً: missed prayers; أَحْدَثَ: to have an event (hadath); اسْتَخْلَفَ: to appoint a substitute; طَلَعَتْ الشَّمْسُ: the sun rises; الجبيرة: splint; سَقَطَتْ: fell; بُرء: healing; بطلت: becomes invalid.
