Commentary
This passage is a series of rulings from the matn of al-Quduri regarding conditions that either invalidate the prayer or render it complete, followed by hadith proofs and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The first ruling: if a person performing tayammum sees water during prayer, the prayer becomes invalid because the substitute (tayammum) is no longer valid when the original (water) is available. However, if he sees it after sitting for the extent of tashahhud, the prayer is considered complete according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), based on the hadith from Ibn Mas'ud that after completing tashahhud, the prayer is complete. Imam Abu Hanifa disagrees, holding that since the final salam has not been said, the prayer is still ongoing and seeing water invalidates it. The hadith of the key of prayer (from Ali) supports that release is only by salam, so until salam, the prayer continues. Similarly, if the period of wiping over khuffs expires, or if he removes khuffs gently, or if an illiterate person learns a surah, or a naked person finds clothing, or remembers a missed prayer, or if the imam has an event and appoints an illiterate follower – in all these cases, the original becomes available and the substitute is invalid, thus prayer becomes invalid (according to Abu Hanifa) or complete (Sahibayn). The text then presents a second set: sunrise during Fajr, entering Asr time during Jumu'ah, or a splint falling off after healing – Abu Hanifa says prayer becomes invalid because the time for that prayer has ended or the excuse (splint) is gone; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say prayer is complete as obligations were fulfilled. The hadith evidence for sunrise prohibition is cited from Bukhari and Muslim.

Key Terms
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited while sitting in the last rak'ah of prayer.
الصاحبين (al-Sahibayn): The two main students of Imam Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
تمام (tamam): Completion; here meaning the prayer is considered validly concluded despite minor deficiency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, if a mutayammim sees water after sitting for tashahhud, what is the ruling on his prayer?
A) The prayer becomes invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is complete and valid.
C) The prayer is invalid only if he intended to break it.
D) The prayer becomes makruh but valid.

Key Takeaway
The Sahibayn's exception after tashahhud provides a practical concession in the Hanafi school, reflecting the idea that the essential acts of prayer are complete with tashahhud.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
When Prayer Becomes Invalid: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Presents rule on makruh in prayer and three cases where prayer becomes invalid according to Abu Hanifa but not Sahibayn.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios where Abu Hanifa rules prayer invalid but Sahibayn rule it valid, and explain the basis of their disagreement.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa applies hadith prohibitions broadly; Sahibayn restrict them to initiation.

This passage from al-Quduri presents a classic intra-Hanafi difference. It addresses three specific situations during prayer: sunrise during Fajr, the entry of Asr time during Jumu'ah, and a bandage falling off due to healing. Abu Hanifa holds the prayer becomes invalid (batil), while his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold it remains complete (tammat). Understanding the legal reasoning behind each position sharpens your grasp of how hadith are interpreted within the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
List the three events that occur during prayer: sunrise during Fajr, entry of Asr time during Jumu'ah, and a bandage (jabirah) falling off due to healing while wiping over it.
2
State the ruling of each Imam
For each scenario, note that Abu Hanifa says 'batilat salatuhu' (his prayer is invalid) and the Sahibayn say 'tammat salatuhu' (his prayer is complete).
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf among the three founding imams.
3
Analyze the dalil for the first two scenarios
Both positions rely on the same hadith forbidding prayer at sunrise and sunset. Abu Hanifa interprets the nahy as general, covering even an ongoing prayer. The Sahibayn restrict it to initiating new prayers.
See the dalil_block for the exact hadith text.
4
Analyze the third scenario
For the bandage case, Abu Hanifa argues that when the bandage falls off due to healing, the condition for wiping (covering a wound) no longer exists, so the wudu is broken, invalidating the prayer. The Sahibayn consider the prayer complete because the wiping was valid when performed.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence: a follower of Abu Hanifa's view would repeat the prayer, while a follower of the Sahibayn would not. Note that later fatwa often favors the Sahibayn to avoid hardship.
The mufta bihi is not specified in the matn, but later authorities prefer the Sahibayn's position for the first two cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل مايكره في الصلوة أَوْ طَلَعَتْ الشَّمْسُ وَهُوَ فِي صَلَاةِ الْفَجْرِ أَوْ دَخَلَ وَقْتُ الْعَصْرِ وَهُوَ فِي صَلَاةِ الجُمُعَةِ أَوْ كَانَ مَاسِحًا عَلَى الْخَبِيرَةِ فَسَقَطَتْ عَنْ بُرْءٍ بَطَلَتْ صَلَاتُهُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ تَمَّتْ صَلَاتُهُ

وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت أَوْ طَلَعَتْ الشَّمْسُ وَهُوَ فِي صَلَاةِ الْفَجْرِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: «نَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ صَلَاتَيْنِ بَعْدَ الْفَجْرِ حَتَّى تَطْلُعَ الشَّمْسُ، وَبَعْدَ الْعَصْرِ حَتَّى تَغْرُبَ الشَّمْسُ، ( صحيح البخاري، بَابٌ : لَا يَتَحَرَّى الصَّلَاةُ قَبْلَ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ، نمبر 1588) وجه : (٢) الحديث لثبوت أَوْ طَلَعَتْ الشَّمْسُ وَهُوَ فِي صَلَاةِ الْفَجْرِ أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ أَبَا سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيَّ يَقُولُ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ: «لا صَلَاةَ بَعْدَ الصُّبْحِ حَتَّى تَرْتَفِعَ الشَّمْسُ وَلَا صَلَاةَ بَعْدَ الْعَصْرِ حَتَّى تَغِيبَ الشَّمْسُ، صحيح البخاري، بَابٌ: لَا يَتَحَرَّى الصَّلَاةُ قَبْلَ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ، نمبر 586\مسلم شريف ، بَابُ الْأَوْقَاتِ الَّتِي هِيَ عَنِ الصَّلَاةِ فِيهَا، رقم 827)

لغات : فَانْقَضَتْ : ختم ہونا، خَلَعَ : اتارنا، أُمَيَّا : ان پڑھ جو ایک آیت بھی نہ جانتا ہو، عُريانا : ننگا، صَلَاةَ فَائِتَةً : متروکہ نمازیں، چھوٹی نمازیں، أَحْدَثَ : حدث لاحق ہونا، اسْتَخْلَفَ : خلیفہ بنانا، نائب بنانا، طَلَعَتْ الشَّمْسُ : سورج لكلنا الجبيرة : کھچی، سَقَطَتْ : گرنا، بُرء : ٹھیک ہوتا، بطلتْ : باطل ہونا ۔
Section of what is disliked in prayer: If the sun rises while he is in the Fajr prayer, or the time of Asr enters while he is in the Jumu'ah prayer, or he is wiping over a bandage and it falls off due to healing, his prayer becomes invalid according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: his prayer is complete. Evidence: (1) The hadith to confirm: 'If the sun rises while he is in the Fajr prayer' from Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah forbade two prayers: after Fajr until sunrise, and after Asr until sunset. (Sahih Bukhari, chapter: no prayer before sunset, no. 1588) Evidence (2) The hadith to confirm: 'If the sun rises while he is in the Fajr prayer' that he heard Abu Sa'id al-Khudri say: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'No prayer after Fajr until the sun rises high, and no prayer after Asr until the sun sets.' (Sahih Bukhari, chapter: no prayer before sunset, no. 586; Muslim, chapter of times in which prayer is prohibited, no. 827) Vocabulary: fa-nqadat: completed; khala'a: took off; ummayya: illiterate who does not know even one verse; 'uryana: naked; salatan fa'itah: missed prayers; ahdatha: hadath occurred; istakhlafa: appointed a deputy; tal'a al-shams: the sun rose; al-jabirah: bandage; saqatat: fell; bur': healing; batilat: invalid.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute embedded in the matn of al-Quduri. The text presents three scenarios where an external event occurs during prayer: (1) sunrise during Fajr, (2) Asr time entering during Jumu'ah, and (3) a bandage (jabirah) falling off due to healing while one is wiping over it. According to Abu Hanifa, in all three cases the prayer becomes batil (invalid). According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), the prayer is complete (tammat) and valid. The disagreement centers on the interpretation of the hadiths prohibiting prayer at sunrise and sunset: Abu Hanifa takes the prohibition as covering even a prayer already in progress, thus invalidating it; the Sahibayn understand the prohibition as only for initiating new prayer, so the ongoing prayer is not affected. For the third case, Abu Hanifa considers the wiping invalidated by the fall, breaking wudu, while the Sahibayn consider the prayer complete because the condition of wiping was valid at the start. The Urdu glossary explains key terms from the chapter, including 'jabirah' (bandage) and 'bur'' (healing). The hadiths provided from Bukhari and Muslim support the prohibition of prayer during those times, which is the basis for the ruling. The lesson emphasizes that the madhhab has internal differences, and the mufta bihi position (relied upon for fatwa) may vary; typically, for the first two cases, the view of the Sahibayn is preferred to avoid hardship.

Key Terms
الخبيرة (al-jabirah): A bandage or splint applied to a wound or fracture over which one may wipe during wudu.
بُرء (bur'): Healing of the wound such that the bandage is no longer needed, causing it to fall off.
بطلت (batilat): The prayer becomes invalid (batil) meaning it must be repeated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a person is praying Fajr and the sun rises before he finishes, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer becomes invalid (batil).
B) The prayer remains valid (tammat).
C) The prayer is valid but makruh.
D) The person must stop and repeat after sunrise.

Key Takeaway
Intra-Hanafi differences exist on key rulings, and the mufta bihi may favor the Sahibayn's more lenient view.

Making Up Missed Prayers and the Requirement of Order (Tartib)
Inter-madhhab dispute on order of making up missed prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada' and precedence, explain the hadith proofs, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument on tartib.

Core Idea
A missed prayer must be made up immediately and given precedence over the current prayer, unless the current prayer's time is about to be lost.

This lesson addresses a practical daily scenario: you miss an obligatory prayer. When do you make it up? Must you pray it before the next prayer? The Hanafi school requires order (tartib) based on the command to pray upon remembrance, but the Shafi'i school disagrees. Understanding this difference is essential for proper qada'.

Guided Path
1
State the rule
The matn states: whoever misses a prayer makes it up when he remembers it, giving it precedence over the current time prayer unless he fears missing the current prayer.
The exception is crucial: if the current prayer's time is about to end, pray that first.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof
The primary proof is the hadith: 'Whoever forgets a prayer, let him pray when he remembers it.' The imperative 'falyusalli' indicates obligation (wujub) and immediacy, supporting precedence.
This hadith is found in Bukhari and Abu Dawud.
3
Examine the supporting story of Umar
Umar prayed Asr after sunset before Maghrib, demonstrating that the Companions observed order between missed and current prayers.
The story is from Jabir in Bukhari.
4
Consider the Shafi'i objection
The Shafi'i school cites a hadith where the Prophet prayed Asr between Maghrib and Isha (i.e., after Maghrib), arguing that order is not required.
The Hanafi response interprets this as a special case of necessity, not abrogating the general rule.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: if you remember a missed Zuhr during Asr time, Hanafi requires praying Zuhr first unless Asr time is about to end; Shafi'i allows praying Asr first.
This difference affects daily planning of prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ قَضَاءِ الْفَوَائِتِ
ل وَمَنْ فَاتَتْهُ صَلَاةٌ قَضَاهَا إِذَا ذَكَرَهَا . وَقَدَّمَهَا عَلَى صَلَاةِ الْوَقْتِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَخَافَ فَوْتَ صَلَاةِ الْوَقْتِ عَلَى الْفَائِتَةِ ثُمَّ يَقْضِيهَا إِلَّا أَنْ يَخَافَ فَوْتَ صَلَاةِ الْوَقْتِ فَيُقَدِّمَ صَلَاةَ الْوَقْتِ عَلَى الْفَائِتَةِ

اوجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ فَاتَتْهُ صَلَاةٌ قَضَاهَا إِذَا ذَكَرَهَا \ عَنْ أَنَسٍ : عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «مَنْ نَسِيَ صَلَاةَ، فَلْيُصَلِ إِذَا ذَكَرَهَا، لَا كَفَّارَةَ لَهَا إِلَّا ذَلِكَ: {وَأَقِمِ الصَّلَاةَ لِذِكْرِي }» قَالَ مُوسَى: قَالَ هَمَّامٌ: سَمِعْتُهُ يَقُولُ بَعْدُ: {وَأَقِمِ الصَّلَاةَ لِلذِّكْرَى} سوره طه، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ مَنْ نَسِيَ صَلَاةَ فَلْيُصَلِ إِذَا ذَكَرَهَا وَلَا يُعِيدُ إِلَّا تِلْكَ الصَّلَاةَ ، نمبر 597/سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي مَنْ نَامَ عَنِ الصَّلَاةِ، أَوْ نَسِيَهَا، نمبر 435) عنهما

وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ فَاتَتْهُ صَلَاةٌ قَضَاهَا إِذَا ذَكَرَهَا \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِي الله أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ : " مَنْ نَسِيَ صَلَاةً فَلَمْ يَذْكُرْهَا، إِلَّا وَهُوَ مَعَ الْإِمَامِ فَلْيُصَلِّ مَعَ الْإِمَامِ، فَإِذَا فَرَغَ مِنَ صَلَاتِهِ فَلْيُعِدِ الصَّلَاةَ الَّتِي نَسِي، ثُمَّ لِيُعِدِ الصَّلاةَ الَّتِي صَلَّى مَعَ الْإِمَامِ، (سنن بيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ ذَكَرَ صَلَاةً وَهُوَ فِي أُخْرَى، نمبر 3193/)

وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ فَاتَتْهُ صَلَاةٌ قَضَاهَا إِذَا ذَكَرَهَا \ عَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: «جَعَلَ عُمَرُ يَوْمَ الْخَنْدَقِ يَسُبُّ كُفَّارَهُمْ، وَقَالَ: مَا كِدْتُ أُصَلِّي الْعَصْرَ حَتَّى غَرَبَتْ، قَالَ: فَنَزَلْنَا يُطْحَانَ، فَصَلَّى بَعْدَ مَا غَرَبَتِ الشَّمْسُ، ثُمَّ صَلَّى الْمَغْرِبَ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ قَضَاءِ الصَّلَوَاتِ الْأُولَى فَالْأُولَى، غمبر 598/سنن ترمذی، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الرَّجُل تَفُوتُهُ الصَّلَوَاتُ بِأَيَّتِهِنَّ يَبْدَأُ ، غبر (179) وجه: (ا) دليل الشافعى الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ فَاتَتْهُ صَلَاةٌ قَضَاهَا إِذَا ذَكَرَهَا \ عَنْ عَلِيِّ بْنِ أَبِي طالب أَنَّهُ قَالَ : شُغِلَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَوْمَ الْأَحْزَابِ عَنْ صَلَاةِ الْعَصْرِ حَتَّى صَلَّى مَا بَيْنَ الْمَغْرِبِ وَالْعِشَاءِ، فَقَالَ: " شَغَلُونَا عَنِ الصَّلَاةِ الْوُسْطَى صَلَاةِ الْعَصْرِ مَلَأَ اللَّهُ قُبُورَهُمْ وَبُيُوتَهُمْ نَارًا، سنن بيهقي، بَابُ مَنْ قَالَ بِتَرْكِ التَّرْتِيبِ في قَضَائِهِنَّ، نمبر 3189)

اصول : جس طرح نماز وقت پر فرض ہے اسی طرح قضاء نمازیں پڑھنا بھی فرض ہے، فرمان رسالت مَنْ نَسِيَ صَلَاةً، فَلْيُصَلِ إِذَا ذَكَرَهَا کی وجہ سے۔
Chapter on making up missed prayers. And whoever misses a prayer makes it up when he remembers it, and gives it precedence over the current time prayer, unless he fears missing the current time prayer over the missed one. Then he makes it up, unless he fears missing the current time prayer, so he gives precedence to the current time prayer over the missed one. Evidences: (1) Hadith to confirm: from Anas that the Prophet said: 'Whoever forgets a prayer, let him pray when he remembers it; there is no expiation for it except that.' (Bukhari no. 597, Abu Dawud no. 435) (2) Hadith to confirm: from Ibn Umar that the Prophet said: 'Whoever forgets a prayer and only remembers while with the imam, let him pray with the imam, and when he finishes his prayer, let him repeat the prayer he forgot, then repeat the prayer he prayed with the imam.' (Bayhaqi no. 3193) (3) Hadith to confirm: from Jabir: 'Umar on the day of the trench was cursing the disbelievers and said: I almost did not pray Asr until the sun set. He said: So we descended to Buthan, and he prayed after the sun set, then he prayed Maghrib.' (Bukhari no. 598, Tirmidhi no. 179) Evidence: (a) Proof of al-Shafi'i: from Ali that he said: The Messenger of Allah was occupied on the day of the Confederates from Asr until he prayed between Maghrib and Isha, and he said: 'They occupied us from the middle prayer, the Asr prayer; may Allah fill their graves and houses with fire.' (Bayhaqi no. 3189) Principle: Just as the prayer at its time is fard, so too making up missed prayers is fard, due to the Prophet's statement: 'Whoever forgets a prayer, let him pray when he remembers it.'
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on making up missed prayers (qada' al-fawa'it). The ruling is clear: a missed obligatory prayer must be made up as soon as one remembers it. The default rule is that the missed prayer (faa'itah) takes precedence over the current time prayer (ada'). However, if one fears the current prayer's time will end if he prays the missed one first, then he should pray the current prayer first and then make up the missed one. This is the Hanafi position (after considering the hadith proofs). The first proof is the well-known hadith from Anas: 'Whoever forgets a prayer, let him pray when he remembers it.' The second proof from Ibn Umar addresses the case of remembering while already in another prayer: one should complete the current prayer with the imam, then repeat the forgotten one, and then repeat the one he prayed with the imam. The third proof from the story of Umar at the Battle of the Trench shows that the Prophet (or Umar) prayed Asr after sunset, before Maghrib, indicating order. Then the text presents the evidence used by Imam al-Shafi'i: a hadith from Ali that the Prophet prayed Asr between Maghrib and Isha (i.e., after Maghrib) without order. The Shafi'i school uses this to say that order (tartib) is not required in making up prayers. The Hanafi school, however, adheres to the order based on the stronger evidence and the practice of the Companions. The Urdu usul note affirms that qada is just as obligatory (fard) as ada due to the clear command. This lesson highlights a practical inter-madhhab difference with significant implications for one's daily prayer schedule.

Key Terms
الفَوَائِت (al-fawa'it): Missed obligatory prayers that were not performed at their prescribed times.
قَضَاء (qada'): Performing an obligatory act of worship after its designated time has passed.
التَّرْتِيب (al-tartib): Order of precedence: praying missed prayers in the order they were missed, and before current time prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone remembers a missed Fajr prayer during Zuhr time and fears Zuhr time will end shortly, what should he do?
A) He must pray the missed Fajr first even if Zuhr time ends.
B) He should pray Zuhr first, then make up Fajr.
C) He may choose either order.
D) He should combine both in one prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school mandates immediate qada with order (tartib) based on the Prophet's command, but allows delaying the missed prayer if the current prayer would otherwise be lost.

Making Up Missed Prayers (Qada al-Fawa'it): Obligation and Priority
Ruling with supporting hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up missed prayers and apply the priority rule when a current prayer is at risk.

Core Idea
A missed fard prayer must be made up immediately upon remembrance, given precedence over the current prayer unless the current prayer would be missed.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on qada al-fawa'it (making up missed prayers). The matn from al-Quduri clearly states that if a person misses a prayer, he must make it up when he remembers it, and he must give it precedence over the current time prayer. However, an exception exists: if performing the missed prayer would cause him to miss the current prayer, then he performs the current prayer first. This ruling is firmly grounded in multiple hadith, especially the hadith of Anas. We will analyze the legal reasoning and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi position: whoever misses a prayer must make it up upon remembrance and give it precedence over the current time prayer, unless he fears missing the current prayer.
The ruling is based on the matn and the hadith.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Identify the hadith of Anas: 'Whoever forgets a prayer, let him pray when he remembers it, there is no expiation for it except that.'
The imperative 'falyusalli' is key.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) indicates obligation (wujub). The phrase 'no expiation except that' confirms immediate qada is the only way to fulfill the obligation.
This establishes that qada is fard immediately.
4
Understand the exception
If performing the missed prayer now would cause the current time prayer to be missed entirely, then the current prayer takes precedence. The missed prayer is made up afterwards.
The exception prevents a greater loss: missing a current obligatory prayer.
5
Review additional proofs
The hadith of Ibn Umar provides guidance for one who remembers a missed prayer while in congregation: complete with the imam, then make up the missed one, then repeat that prayer. The incidents of Umar and Ali show that the Prophet and Companions made up missed prayers in order after the current time had passed, confirming the ruling.
These proofs reinforce the obligation and illustrate the priority rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ قَضَاءِ الْفَوَائِتِ
وَمَنْ فَاتَتْهُ صَلَاةٌ قَضَاهَا إِذَا ذَكَرَهَا . وَقَدَّمَهَا عَلَى صَلَاةِ الْوَقْتِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَخَافَ فَوْتَ صَلَاةِ الْوَقْتِ عَلَى الْفَائِتَةِ ثُمَّ يَقْضِيهَا إِلَّا أَنْ يَخَافَ فَوْتَ صَلَاةِ الْوَقْتِ فَيُقَدِّمَ صَلَاةَ الْوَقْتِ عَلَى الْفَائِتَةِ
عَنْ أَنَسٍ : عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «مَنْ نَسِيَ صَلَاةَ، فَلْيُصَلِ إِذَا ذَكَرَهَا، لَا كَفَّارَةَ لَهَا إِلَّا ذَلِكَ: {وَأَقِمِ الصَّلَاةَ لِذِكْرِي }» (بخاري، نمبر 597/سنن ابوداود، نمبر 435)
عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِي الله أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ : " مَنْ نَسِيَ صَلَاةً فَلَمْ يَذْكُرْهَا، إِلَّا وَهُوَ مَعَ الْإِمَامِ فَلْيُصَلِّ مَعَ الْإِمَامِ، فَإِذَا فَرَغَ مِنَ صَلَاتِهِ فَلْيُعِدِ الصَّلَاةَ الَّتِي نَسِي، ثُمَّ لِيُعِدِ الصَّلاةَ الَّتِي صَلَّى مَعَ الْإِمَامِ، (سنن بيهقي، نمبر 3193)
عَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: «جَعَلَ عُمَرُ يَوْمَ الْخَنْدَقِ يَسُبُّ كُفَّارَهُمْ، وَقَالَ: مَا كِدْتُ أُصَلِّي الْعَصْرَ حَتَّى غَرَبَتْ، قَالَ: فَنَزَلْنَا يُطْحَانَ، فَصَلَّى بَعْدَ مَا غَرَبَتِ الشَّمْسُ، ثُمَّ صَلَّى الْمَغْرِبَ، (بخاري، نمبر 598/سنن ترمذی، غبر (179)
عَنْ عَلِيِّ بْنِ أَبِي طالب أَنَّهُ قَالَ : شُغِلَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَوْمَ الْأَحْزَابِ عَنْ صَلَاةِ الْعَصْرِ حَتَّى صَلَّى مَا بَيْنَ الْمَغْرِبِ وَالْعِشَاءِ، فَقَالَ: " شَغَلُونَا عَنِ الصَّلَاةِ الْوُسْطَى صَلَاةِ الْعَصْرِ مَلَأَ اللَّهُ قُبُورَهُمْ وَبُيُوتَهُمْ نَارًا، (سنن بيهقي، نمبر 3189)
اصول : جس طرح نماز وقت پر فرض ہے اسی طرح قضاء نمازیں پڑھنا بھی فرض ہے، فرمان رسالت مَنْ نَسِيَ صَلَاةً، فَلْيُصَلِ إِذَا ذَكَرَهَا کی وجہ سے۔
Chapter of Making Up Missed Prayers. Whoever misses a prayer makes it up when he remembers it, and gives it precedence over the current time prayer unless he fears missing the current time prayer over the missed one. Then he makes it up, unless he fears missing the current time prayer, then he gives precedence to the current time prayer over the missed one. From Anas from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever forgets a prayer, let him pray when he remembers it, there is no expiation for it except that: {And establish prayer for My remembrance}.' From Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever forgets a prayer and only remembers it while with the imam, let him pray with the imam, and when he finishes his prayer, let him repeat the prayer he forgot, then let him repeat the prayer he prayed with the imam.' From Jabir said: 'Umar on the day of the Trench was cursing their disbelievers, and said: I almost did not pray Asr until the sun set. He said: so we descended to Bathan, and he prayed after the sun set, then he prayed Maghrib.' From Ali ibn Abi Talib that he said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was occupied on the day of the Confederates from Asr prayer until he prayed between Maghrib and Isha, and said: They occupied us from the middle prayer, the Asr prayer, may Allah fill their graves and houses with fire.' Principle: Just as prayer at its time is obligatory, similarly making up missed prayers is obligatory, due to the command of the Prophet: 'Whoever forgets a prayer, let him pray when he remembers it.'
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on making up missed prayers (qada al-fawa'it). The matn from al-Quduri states that if a person misses a prayer, he must make it up immediately upon remembering it, and he must give it precedence over the current time prayer. However, there is an exception: if he fears that performing the missed prayer now will cause him to miss the current time prayer, then he should pray the current time prayer first, and then make up the missed one afterward. This ruling is supported by several hadith. The primary proof is the hadith of Anas: 'Whoever forgets a prayer, let him pray when he remembers it, there is no expiation for it except that.' The imperative 'falyusalli' indicates obligation in Hanafi usul. The hadith of Ibn Umar provides guidance for one who remembers a missed prayer while already in congregation: he should complete his current prayer with the imam, then repeat the missed one, and then repeat the one he prayed with the imam (this is a special case for following the imam). The incident of Umar on the day of the Khandaq shows that when a prayer is missed due to war, the Prophet and the Companions made up the prayers in order after the sun set, indicating the obligation of qada. The hadith of Ali also shows that the Prophet made up Asr between Maghrib and Isha, proving that qada is performed after remembering. The final Urdu principle summarizes: just as prayer at its time is fard, so is making up missed prayers fard, due to the hadith.

Key Terms
قضاء الفوائت (qada' al-fawa'it): Making up missed obligatory prayers after their prescribed time has passed.
الفوائت (al-fawa'it): The missed prayers (plural of فائتة).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a person remembers a missed fard prayer while it is still the time for another current fard prayer, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) He should first perform the missed prayer, even if meaning the current prayer will be missed.
B) He should perform the missed prayer, unless he fears missing the current time prayer, in which case he performs the current prayer first.
C) He should perform the current prayer first, and delay the missed prayer to a later time.
D) He is excused from making up the missed prayer if the current prayer time is about to end.

Key Takeaway
Making up missed prayers is obligatory immediately, and they take priority over the current prayer unless the current prayer would be missed.

Sequence in Making Up Missed Prayers and When It Drops
Ruling with proof and exceptions for tartib in qada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sequence (tartib) in qada, identify when the obligation of sequence drops (kathirah, time constriction, forgetfulness), and apply the ruling to scenarios involving multiple missed prayers and fear of missing the current prayer.

Core Idea
Sequence in qada is wajib unless you have six or more missed prayers or fear missing the current time.

When you have missed several prayers, should you make them up in the order they were obligated? The Hanafi school says yes — sequence is required — but this obligation is not absolute. In this lesson, we examine the ruling from al-Quduri and the proof from the Prophet's practice on the day of Khandaq, along with the conditions that cause the obligation of sequence to drop.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on making up multiple missed prayers. State the general hukm: sequence (tartib) is wajib. Find the phrase 'رتبها في القضاء كما وجبت في الأصل'.
Sequence means following the original order of obligation (e.g., Zuhr before Asr).
2
Find the exception for kathirah
Locate the exception: 'إلا أن تزيد الفوائت على ست صلوات'. If missed prayers exceed six, sequence is no longer wajib. Note the definition of kathirah: six prayers (one day and night).
The Urdu principle clarifies 'كثير' means six prayers.
3
Identify other exceptions
The passage also mentions 'إلا أن يخاف فوت صلاة الوقت' — if one fears missing the current time prayer, he starts with that prayer first. Additionally, forgetfulness and unconsciousness (from the narrations) also drop sequence.
These are supported by the narrations of Ibrahim and al-Hasan.
4
Analyze the dalil
The hadith of Abdullah (Ibn Mas'ud) about the day of Khandaq shows the Prophet made up four prayers in order. Identify the wajh al-dalalah: his act demonstrates that sequence is required. Note the thubut (zanni) and dalala (zanni).
The proof is from practice (fi'l), not explicit command.
5
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school does not require sequence in qada except for the same day's prayers. The Hanafi position is based on this hadith and the practice of the Companions.
The practical difference (thamarah) is whether one must redo prayers if done out of order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ فَاتَتْهُ صَلَوَاتٌ رَتَّبَهَا فِي الْقَضَاءِ كَمَا وَجَبَتْ فِي الْأَصْلِ إِلَّا أَنْ تَزِيدَ الْفَوَائِتُ عَلَى سِتِّ صَلَوَاتِ
ثُمَّ يَقْضِيهَا إِلَّا أَنْ يَخَافَ فَوْتَ صَلَاةِ الْوَقْتِ
قَالَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ: «إِنَّ الْمُشْرِكِينَ شَغَلُوا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ أَرْبَعِ صَلَوَاتٍ يَوْمَ الْخَنْدَقِ، حَتَّى ذَهَبَ مِنَ اللَّيْلِ مَا شَاءَ اللَّهُ، فَأَمَرَ بِلَالًا فَأَذَّنَ، ثُمَّ أَقَامَ فَصَلَّى الظُّهْرَ، ثُمَّ أَقَامَ فَصَلَّى العَصْرَ ، ثُمَّ أَقَامَ فَصَلَّى الْمَغْرِبَ، ثُمَّ أَقَامَ فَصَلَّى العِشَاءَ،(سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الرَّجُلِ تَفُوتُهُ الصَّلَوَاتُ بِأَيَّتِهِنَّ يَبْدَأُ ، غبر (179)
عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، قَالَ: كَانَ يَقُولُ فِي الْمُغْمَى عَلَيْهِ إِذَا أُغْمِيَ عَلَيْهِ يَوْمٌ وَلَيْلَةٌ: «أَعَادَ وَإِذَا كَانَ أَكْثَرَ مِنْ ذَلِكَ لَمْ يُعِد،(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَا يُعِيدُ الْمُغْمَى عَلَيْهِ مِنَ الصَّلَاةِ، نمبر6592)
عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، قَالَ: إِذَا نَسِيَ الصَّلَوَاتِ فَلْيَبْدَأْ بِالْأُولَى فَالْأُولَى فَإِنْ خَافَ الْفَوْتَ يَبْدَأُ بِالَّتِي يَخَافُ فَوْتَهَا،(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، فِي الرَّجُلِ يَنْسَى الصَّلَوَاتِ جَمِيعًا، نمبر 4725)
عَنْ مُغِيرَةَ، عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، قَالَا: إِذَا كُنْتَ فِي صَلَاةِ الْعَصْرِ فَذَكَرْتَ أَنَّكَ لَمْ تُصَلِ الظُّهْرَ فَانْصَرِفْ فَصَلَ الظُّهْرَ ثُمَّ صَلِ الْعَصْرَ، (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه الرَّجُلُ يَذْكُرُ صَلَاةً عَلَيْهِ وَهُوَ فِي أُخْرَى،نمبر 4757)
اصول : جس کی گزشتہ کوئی قضاء نماز باقی نہ ہو ایسے نمازی کو صاحب ترتیب کہتے ہیں، اور صاحب ترتیب کی قضاء نمازیں چار سے کم ہوں تو فائتہ نمازوں میں ترتیب واجب ہے، اور ادائیگی میں فائتہ کو وقتیہ پر رکھے۔ اصول : تین شرطوں سے ترتیب ساقط ہو جاتی ہے اوقت کی تنگی ۲ بھول ۳ فائتہ نمازیں کثیر ہو جائیں۔ اصول : فائتہ نمازیں اگر کثیر ہو جائیں تو جو سی نماز پڑھے گا وہ جائز ہو گی کیونکہ ترتیب ساقط ہو چکی ہے ، اور کثیر سے مراد ایک دن ایک رات کی نماز یعنی چھ نمازیں قضاء ہو گئی تو کثیر ہو گی۔
If he missed prayers, he arranges them in making up as they were obligated originally, unless the missed prayers exceed six prayers. Then he makes them up unless he fears missing the current time prayer. Abdullah said: 'The polytheists occupied the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) from four prayers on the day of the Khandaq until part of the night passed as Allah willed, so he ordered Bilal to give the adhan, then iqamah, and he prayed Zuhr, then iqamah and prayed Asr, then iqamah and prayed Maghrib, then iqamah and prayed Isha.' From Ibrahim, he said: 'He used to say concerning the unconscious person: if he is unconscious for a day and night, he repeats his prayers; if more than that, he does not repeat.' From al-Hasan, he said: 'If one forgets prayers, he should start with the first then the first; if he fears missing (the current prayer), he starts with the one he fears missing.' From Mughirah, from Ibrahim, they said: 'If you are in Asr prayer and remember that you did not pray Zuhr, then break off and pray Zuhr, then pray Asr.' Principle: A person who has no previous missed prayer remaining is called sahib tartib. And for a sahib tartib, if his missed prayers are less than four, sequence in the missed prayers is wajib, and in performance, the missed prayer is placed before the current time prayer. Principle: Sequence drops under three conditions: (1) constriction of time, (2) forgetfulness, (3) the missed prayers become many (kathirah). Principle: If missed prayers become many, whichever he prays first is valid because sequence has dropped. And 'many' means prayers of one day and one night, i.e., six prayers become missed, then it is many.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on making up missed prayers, now dealing with multiple missed prayers. The matn states that if one has missed several prayers, he must make them up in the order they were obligated (e.g., Zuhr before Asr, Asr before Maghrib, etc.), unless the number of missed prayers exceeds six. The hadith of Abdullah (Ibn Mas'ud or similar) about the day of the Khandaq shows that the Prophet made up four missed prayers in order (Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha), establishing the obligation of sequence (tartib). The hadith is from Tirmidhi. Then proof is given from the sayings of the tabi'un: Ibrahim al-Nakha'i says that if a person is unconscious for a day and night, he must repeat his prayers (indicating a limit of five prayers? Actually it's about unconsciousness but used here to support the six-prayer limit). Al-Hasan al-Basri says: start with the first missed prayer, but if you fear missing the current prayer, start with that. This supports the exception for fear of missing current prayer. Mughirah and Ibrahim give a ruling: if you are in Asr and remember you missed Zuhr, break the Asr and pray Zuhr first, then Asr. This shows that sequence is required even if it means breaking a current prayer (unless fear of missing current time). The Urdu principles clarify: a person who has no previous missed prayers is called 'sahib tartib' (one subject to sequence). If his missed prayers are less than four (or actually the text says 'less than four' but then later says six is 'kathirah'? There is some inconsistency: the matn says 'exceed six', the Urdu principle says 'less than four' for wajib sequence? Actually the Urdu says 'چار سے کم ہوں' meaning less than four, but then later says 'چھ نمازیں قضاء ہو گئی تو کثیر ہو گی' meaning six is many. This might be a difference in wording. The standard Hanafi position is that if missed prayers are less than six (i.e., five or fewer), sequence is wajib; if six or more, sequence drops. The Urdu principle might be stating that for a sahib tartib (who has no prior missed prayers), if his missed prayers are less than four? That seems off. To stay faithful to the text, we note that the text says 'إلا أن تزيد الفوائت على ست صلوات' and the Urdu principle says 'فائتہ نمازیں اگر کثیر ہو جائیں... کثیر سے مراد ایک دن ایک رات کی نماز یعنی چھ نمازیں' so 'kathirah' is defined as six prayers. The earlier mention of 'چار سے کم' might be a separate note about sahib tartib? Actually the Urdu: 'صاحب ترتیب کی قضاء نمازیں چار سے کم ہوں تو فائتہ نمازوں میں ترتیب واجب ہے' — this might be a different condition: if the missed prayers are less than four? But the matn says six. Possibly the text has an error or it's from another source. We will comment as per the text: the ruling is from al-Quduri: sequence is required unless missed prayers exceed six. The Urdu principle adds that sequence drops under three conditions: time constriction, forgetfulness, and when missed prayers become many (six or more).

Key Terms
صاحب ترتیب (sahib tartib): A person who has no prior missed prayers (i.e., he is not already in a state of having missed prayers). For such a person, sequence in qada is wajib unless the number becomes kathirah.
ترتیب (tartib): Sequence in performing missed prayers according to the original order of obligation (e.g., Zuhr before Asr).
کثیر (kathirah): Many missed prayers; defined in this text as six or more (i.e., prayers of one full day and night).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when does the obligation of sequence (tartib) in making up missed prayers drop?
A) When the missed prayers are less than four.
B) When the missed prayers exceed six (i.e., become kathirah).
C) Only when one fears missing the current time prayer.
D) When the person is unconscious for more than a day.

Key Takeaway
Sequence in making up missed prayers is wajib for sahib tartib unless the missed prayers reach six or more (kathirah), or when one fears missing the current time prayer — then the current prayer takes precedence.

Qada' al-Fawa'it: The Obligation of Order and When It Falls
Ruling on order of qada prayers and conditions for it to fall away

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on order in missed prayers, identify the three conditions that cause order to fall away, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Order in qada is wajib only until the missed prayers become many (six or more); then it falls.

This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar presents the Hanafi ruling on making up missed prayers: order (tarteeb) is required unless the number of missed prayers exceeds six. The commentary expands with proofs from hadith and sayings of the Salaf, and contrasts the Shafi'i position that order is always required. You will learn the precise conditions that trigger the obligation and the exceptions that lift it.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling in the matn: missed prayers must be made up in order as they were obligated, unless they exceed six. This is the starting point.
The matn uses 'exceed six' (تزيد على ست صلوات).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The commentator cites Imam al-Shafi'i who holds that order is always required, quoting a general hadith and his own statement about completing a current prayer before making up a missed one.
Al-Shafi'i's proof is from a general command: 'Whoever misses a prayer, let him pray it when he remembers it.'
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand al-Shafi'i's dalil: if one remembers a missed prayer while in another, he finishes the current and then prays the missed, implying order is always to be observed.
The Shafi'i view does not recognize a threshold for many missed prayers.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the general hadith applies when missed prayers are few; when they become many (six or more), order is dropped due to hardship, as supported by the hadith of Khandaq (Prophet made up four in order, not more) and the athar of Ibrahim (unconscious for more than a day does not repeat).
The principle of ease (رفع الحرج) is invoked.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi allows a person with six or more missed prayers to pray them in any order; Shafi'i requires chronological order always.
This affects how a person with accumulated qada plans their prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ قَضَاءِ الْفَوَائِتِ فَإِنْ فَاتَتْهُ صَلَوَاتٌ رَتَّبَهَا فِي الْقَضَاءِ كَمَا وَجَبَتْ فِي الْأَصْلِ إِلَّا أَنْ تَزِيدَ الْفَوَائِتُ عَلَى سِتِ صَلَوَاتِ وجه (۲) دليل الشافعى قول الشافعى لثبوت وَمَنْ فَاتَتْهُ صَلَاةٌ قَضَاهَا إِذَا ذَكَرَهَا اقال الشافعي: من فاتته الصلاة فذكرها وقد دخل في صلاة غيرها ---- ولم تفسد عليه إماما كان أو مأموما فإذا فرغ من صلاته صلى الصلاة الفائتة، الام) للشافعي وقت الصلاة في السفر، نمبر 97) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت ثُمَّ يَقْضِيهَا إِلَّا أَنْ يَخَافَ فَوْتَ صَلَاةِ الْوَقْتِ \ قَالَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ: «إِنَّ الْمُشْرِكِينَ شَغَلُوا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ أَرْبَعِ صَلَوَاتٍ يَوْمَ الْخَنْدَقِ، حَتَّى ذَهَبَ مِنَ اللَّيْلِ مَا شَاءَ اللَّهُ، فَأَمَرَ بِلَالًا فَأَذَّنَ، ثُمَّ أَقَامَ فَصَلَّى الظُّهْرَ، ثُمَّ أَقَامَ فَصَلَّى العَصْرَ ، ثُمَّ أَقَامَ فَصَلَّى الْمَغْرِبَ، ثُمَّ أَقَامَ فَصَلَّى العِشَاءَ،(سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الرَّجُلِ تَفُوتُهُ الصَّلَوَاتُ بِأَيَّتِهِنَّ يَبْدَأُ ، غبر (179) وجه: (٢) قول التابعي لثبوت ثُمَّ يَقْضِيهَا إِلَّا أَنْ يَخَافَ فَوْتَ صَلَاةِ الْوَقْتِ \ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، قَالَ: كَانَ يَقُولُ فِي الْمُغْمَى عَلَيْهِ إِذَا أُغْمِيَ عَلَيْهِ يَوْمٌ وَلَيْلَةٌ: «أَعَادَ وَإِذَا كَانَ أَكْثَرَ مِنْ ذَلِكَ لَمْ يُعِد،(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَا يُعِيدُ الْمُغْمَى عَلَيْهِ مِنَ الصَّلَاةِ، نمبر6592/) وجه (۳) قول التابعي لثبوت ثُمَّ يَقْضِيهَا إِلَّا أَنْ يَخَافَ فَوْتَ صَلَاةِ الْوَقْتِ \ عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، قَالَ: إِذَا نَسِيَ الصَّلَوَاتِ فَلْيَبْدَأْ بِالْأُولَى فَالْأُولَى فَإِنْ خَافَ الْفَوْتَ يَبْدَأُ بِالَّتِي يَخَافُ فَوْتَهَا،(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، فِي الرَّجُلِ يَنْسَى الصَّلَوَاتِ جَمِيعًا، نمبر 4725) وجه : (۴) قول التابعي لثبوت ثُمَّ يَقْضِيهَا إِلَّا أَنْ يَخَافَ فَوْتَ صَلَاةِ الْوَقْتِ \ عَامِرٍ، وَعَنْ مُغِيرَةَ، عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، قَالَا: إِذَا كُنْتَ فِي صَلَاةِ الْعَصْرِ فَذَكَرْتَ أَنَّكَ لَمْ تُصَلِ الظُّهْرَ فَانْصَرِفْ فَصَلَ الظُّهْرَ ثُمَّ صَلِ الْعَصْرَ، (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه الرَّجُلُ يَذْكُرُ صَلَاةً عَلَيْهِ وَهُوَ فِي أُخْرَى،نمبر 4757) اصول : جس کی گزشتہ کوئی قضاء نماز باقی نہ ہو ایسے نمازی کو صاحب ترتیب کہتے ہیں، اور صاحب ترتیب کی قضاء نمازیں چار سے کم ہوں تو فائتہ نمازوں میں ترتیب واجب ہے، اور ادائیگی میں فائتہ کو وقتیہ پر رکھے۔ اصول : تین شرطوں سے ترتیب ساقط ہو جاتی ہے اوقت کی تنگی ۲ بھول ۳ فائتہ نمازیں کثیر ہو جائیں۔ اصول : فائتہ نمازیں اگر کثیر ہو جائیں تو جو سی نماز پڑھے گا وہ جائز ہو گی کیونکہ ترتیب ساقط ہو چکی ہے ، اور کثیر سے مراد ایک دن ایک رات کی نماز یعنی چھ نمازیں قضاء ہو گئی تو کثیر ہو گی۔
Chapter of Making up Missed Prayers. If he misses prayers, he should make them up in order as they were obligatory originally, unless the missed prayers exceed six prayers. Aspect (2): Evidence of al-Shafi'i: the statement of al-Shafi'i for establishing: 'Whoever misses a prayer, he makes it up when he remembers it.' Al-Shafi'i said: 'Whoever misses a prayer and remembers it while he has entered into another prayer... it does not invalidate for him whether he is imam or follower; when he finishes his prayer, he prays the missed prayer.' (Al-Umm, al-Shafi'i, chapter on prayer time in travel, no. 97). Aspect (1): Hadith for establishing: then he prays it except if he fears losing the prayer of the current time. 'Abdullah said: 'The polytheists occupied the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) from four prayers on the day of the trench, until as much of the night passed as Allah willed. So he commanded Bilal to give the adhan, then iqama, and he prayed Zuhr; then iqama and prayed Asr; then iqama and prayed Maghrib; then iqama and prayed Isha.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on the man who misses prayers with which one he begins, no. 179). Aspect (2): Saying of the Tabi'i for establishing: then he prays them except if he fears losing the current prayer. From Ibrahim: He used to say about the unconscious person: if he is unconscious for a day and night, he repeats; if it is more than that, he does not repeat. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 6592). Aspect (3): Saying of the Tabi'i for establishing: then he prays them except if he fears losing the current prayer. From al-Hasan: If he forgets prayers, let him begin with the first, then the first; and if he fears losing (the current prayer), he begins with the one he fears losing. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 4725). Aspect (4): Saying of the Tabi'i for establishing: then he prays them except if he fears losing the current prayer. From 'Amir and from Mughira, from Ibrahim: They said: If you are in Asr prayer and you remember that you did not pray Zuhr, then leave and pray Zuhr, then pray Asr. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 4757). Principles: The one who has no previous qada prayers remaining is called 'Sahib al-Tarteeb'. And if the qada prayers of a Sahib al-Tarteeb are less than four, then order is wajib among the missed prayers, and in performance he should place the missed before the current. Principles: Order falls away by three conditions: (1) tightness of time, (2) forgetfulness, (3) when missed prayers become many. Principles: If missed prayers become many, then whichever prayer he prays, it will be valid, because order has fallen away. And 'many' means the prayers of one day and one night, i.e., if six prayers become qada, then it is many.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the obligation of order (tarteeb) in making up missed prayers. The matn of al-Quduri states the Hanafi ruling: missed prayers must be made up in the order they were originally obligated, unless they exceed six. The commentator expands by providing proofs and then presents the Shafi'i position. The Hanafi proofs include the hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ) making up four prayers in order after the Battle of the Trench, indicating order is required when the number is few. Additionally, sayings of Tabi'un (ibrahim al-Nakha'i, al-Hasan al-Basri, etc.) support that if one fears losing the current prayer, he prays it first, showing that order can be overridden by time constraint. The Shafi'i position, quoted from al-Shafi'i himself, holds that if one remembers a missed prayer while in another prayer, he completes the current prayer and then makes up the missed one, implying order is always required. The Hanafi response is that this applies only when missed prayers are few; when they become many (six or more), order falls away due to hardship. The Urdu principles clarify: a person with no missed prayers is called 'sahib al-tarteeb'; if his missed prayers are less than four (or six?), order is wajib; it falls away due to time tightness, forgetfulness, or when missed prayers become many (defined as six – a day and night's worth of prayers).

Key Terms
صاحب ترتیب (sahib al-tarteeb): In this text, a person who has no previous missed prayers; but more commonly, one who has a manageable number of missed prayers requiring order. The Urdu definition is ambiguous.
ترتیب (tarteeb): The obligation to make up missed prayers in the same order they were originally obligated (e.g., Fajr before Zuhr, etc.).
كثير (kathir): Many missed prayers; defined here as six or more (a day and night's prayers).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following causes the obligation of order (tarteeb) in making up missed prayers to fall away?
A) The person is an imam
B) The missed prayers are five
C) The person forgets the order
D) The person is in a state of janabah

Key Takeaway
Order in making up missed prayers is wajib only when the missed prayers are less than six; it falls away due to time pressure, forgetfulness, or when the number reaches six or more.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
The Three Forbidden Times for Prayer
Ruling on three prohibited prayer times with multiple hadith proofs and an exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three times when prayer is prohibited, distinguish between voluntary and obligatory prayers at those times, and cite the key hadith proofs from the Hanafi source.

Core Idea
Prayer at sunrise, zenith, and sunset is forbidden for voluntary acts; only the current 'Asr is an exception with dislike.

The Hanafi school, following the primary texts, identifies three specific times when performing salah is severely disliked (makruh tahrimi) or impermissible for voluntary prayers. This lesson unpacks the key ruling from al-Quduri's matn and the supporting hadith evidence, clarifying the exception for obligatory prayers, especially the 'Asr of the same day.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the three times mentioned: sunrise (tulu' al-shams), zenith (qiyam al-shams fi al-zahirah), and sunset (ghurub al-shams). The ruling is 'la tajuz' – not permissible – which for voluntary prayers means the prayer is invalid (batil), while for obligatory prayers it is valid but disliked.
2
Examine the primary hadith proof
Read the hadith of 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir listing three hours: when the sun rises, when it stands at zenith, and when it inclines for sunset. Note the explicit prohibition (yanhana).
3
Analyze the additional hadith for reason and scope
Study the hadith of 'Amr ibn 'Abasah, which explains the reason (e.g., sun rising between the horns of Shaytan) and confirms the prohibition extends to all prayers during these times. Also note the hadith of Ibn 'Umar forbidding deliberate prayer at sunrise and sunset.
4
Identify the exception for 'Asr
The Urdu principles state that the 'Asr prayer of the same day is valid with dislike (karahah). This is the only deliberate prayer allowed at sunset, though it remains makruh.
5
Distinguish voluntary vs. obligatory
Voluntary (nafl) prayers are completely invalid at these times. Obligatory (fard/wajib) prayers, including qada, are valid but disliked if performed during these times, except for the current 'Asr which is permissible with dislike.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْأَوْقَاتِ الَّتِي تُكْرَهُ فِيهَا الصَّلَاةُ لَا تَجُوزُ الصَّلَاةُ عِنْدَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ وَلَا عِنْدَ قِيَامِهَا فِي الظَّهِيرَةِ وَلَا عِنْدَ غُرُوبِهَا عِنْدَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ وجه ه: (۱) الحديث لثبوت لا تَجُوزُ الصَّلَاةُ عِنْدَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ اسَمِعْتُ عُقْبَةَ بْنَ عَامِرٍ الْجُهَنِيَّ يَقُولُ ثَلَاثُ سَاعَاتِ كَانَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَنْهَانَا أَنْ نُصَلِّيَ فِيهِنَّ أَوْ أَنْ نَقْبُرَ فِيهِنَّ مَوْتَانَا حِينَ تَطْلُعُ الشَّمْسُ بَازِغَةً حَتَّى تَرْتَفِعَ وَحِينَ يَقُومُ قَائِمُ الظَّهِيرَةِ حَتَّى تَمِيلَ الشَّمْسُ وَحِينَ تَضَيَّفُ الشَّمْسُ للغروب حتى تغرب (مسلم شريف، بَاب الأَوْقَاتِ الَّتِي هِيَ عَنِ الصَّلَاةِ فِيهَا ،نمبر 831/(سنن ابوداود، بَابُ الدَّفْنِ عِنْدَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ وَعِنْدَ غُرُوبِهَا ، نمبر 3192/،(سنن ترمذى، مَا جَاءَ فِي كَرَاهِيَةِ الصَّلَاةِ عَلَى الجَنَازَةِ عِنْدَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ وَعِنْدَ غُرُوبِهَا وَتَحْلِيلِهَا،1030) وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت لا تَجُوزُ الصَّلَاةُ عِنْدَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ اقَالَ عَمْرُو بْنُ عَبَسَةَ السُّلَمِيُّ يَا نَبِيَّ اللَّهِ !.... أَخْبِرْنِي عَمَّا عَلَّمَكَ اللَّهُ وَأَجْهَلُهُ. أَخْبِرْنِي عَنِ الصَّلَاةِ؟ قَالَ صَلِّ صَلَاةَ الصُّبْحِ ثُمَّ أَقْصِرْ عَنِ الصَّلَاةِ حَتَّى تَطْلُعَ الشَّمْسُ حَتَّى تَرْتَفِعَ فَإِنَّهَا تَطْلُعُ حِينَ تَطْلُعُ بَيْنَ قَرْيَ شَيْطَانٍ. وَحِينَئِذٍ يَسْجُدُ لَهَا الْكُفَّارُ ثُمَّ صَلِ. فَإِنَّ الصَّلَاةَ مَشْهُودَةٌ مَحْضُورَةٌ. حَتَّى يَسْتَقِلَ الظَّلُ بِالرُّمْحِ. ثُمَّ أَقْصِرْ عَن الصَّلَاةِ. فَإِنَّ حِينَئِذٍ تُسْجَرُ جَهَنَّمُ. فَإِذَا أَقْبَلَ الْفَيْءُ فَصَلَ فَإِنَّ الصَّلَاةَ مَشْهُودَةٌ مَحْضُورَةٌ. حَقَّ تُصَلِّيَ الْعَصْرَ. ثُمَّ أَقْصِرْ عَن الصَّلَاةِ. حَتَّى تَغْرُبَ الشَّمْسُ فَإِنَّهَا تَغْرُبُ بَيْنَ قَرْيَ شَيْطَانٍ وَحِينَئِذٍ يَسْجُدُ لَهَا الْكُفَّارُ"، (مسلم) شريف بَاب إِسْلَام عَمْرو بن عَبَسَةَ، غمبر 832/سنن نسائي، النَّهْيُ عَنِ الصَّلَاةِ بَعْدَ الْعَصْرِ، نمبر 567) وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت لَا تَجُوزُ الصَّلَاةُ عِنْدَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ وَلَا عِنْدَ غُرُوبِمَا أَخْبَرَنِي ابْنُ عُمَرَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لَا تَحَرَّوْا بِصَلَاتِكُمْ طُلُوعَ الشَّمْسِ وَلَا غُرُوبَهَا، ،(بخاري شريف، بَابُ الصَّلَاةِ بَعْدَ الْفَجْرِ حَتَّى تَرْتَفِعَ الشَّمْسُ ، نمبر 582/، (سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِيمَنْ أَدْرَكَ رَكْعَةً مِنَ العَصْرِ قَبْلَ أَنْ تَغْرُبَ الشَّمْسُ، نمبر 186) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت لا تَجُوزُ الصَّلَاةُ عِنْدَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ اعَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اصول : تین اوقات میں نماز نہیں ادا کرنا چاہئے اسورج طلوع ہونے وقت ۲ زوال کے وقت ۳ غروب کے وقت یہاں تک غروب ہو جائے البتہ اسی دن کی عصر کی نماز کراہت کیساتھ درست ہو گی۔
Chapter of the times in which prayer is disliked. Prayer is not permissible at sunrise, nor at its zenith in the middle of the day, nor at its sunset at sunrise. Aspect (1): Hadith for establishing that prayer is not permissible at sunrise: I heard 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir al-Juhani say: Three hours that the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) forbade us to pray in or to bury our dead in: when the sun rises until it rises high, when the sun stands at its zenith until it declines, and when the sun inclines towards setting until it sets. (Muslim, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). Aspect (2): Hadith for establishing: 'Amr ibn 'Abasah al-Sulami said: O Prophet of Allah... The Prophet said: Pray the morning prayer, then refrain from prayer until the sun rises and becomes high, for it rises between the horns of Shaytan, and then the disbelievers prostrate to it. Then pray, for prayer is witnessed and attended, until the shadow becomes level with the spear. Then refrain from prayer, for then Hell is stoked. Then when the shadow turns, pray, for prayer is witnessed and attended, until you pray 'Asr. Then refrain from prayer until the sun sets, for it sets between the horns of Shaytan, and then the disbelievers prostrate to it. (Muslim, al-Nasa'i). Aspect (1): Hadith for establishing that prayer is not permissible at sunrise nor at its sunset: Ibn 'Umar said: The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) said: 'Do not deliberately seek to pray at sunrise or sunset.' (Bukhari, Tirmidhi). Aspect (2): Hadith for establishing... Principles: Prayer should not be performed at three times: (1) at sunrise, (2) at the time of zenith, (3) at sunset until it has completely set. However, the 'Asr prayer of that same day is valid with dislike.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the three times when prayer is prohibited (makruh tahrimi / la tajuz). The matn of al-Quduri states that prayer is not permissible at sunrise, at the zenith (when the sun is at its highest, i.e., midday), and at sunset. The commentator provides multiple hadith proofs: the famous hadith of 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir listing three hours; the detailed hadith of 'Amr ibn 'Abasah explaining the reasons; and the hadith of Ibn 'Umar forbidding deliberate prayer at sunrise and sunset. The Urdu principles clarify that these three times are prohibited, but an exception is made for the 'Asr prayer of the same day if one has not yet prayed it; however, it is still disliked (karahah) to delay it until sunset, but the prayer itself is valid. The Hanafi position is that the prohibition is at the specific moments: when the sun is rising until it has fully risen (approx 15-20 min), at zenith until the sun declines (midday when shadow is shortest), and at sunset until the sun has completely set. Voluntary prayers are strictly prohibited at these times; obligatory prayers that are missed (qada) can be performed at these times with dislike, except for the current 'Asr which is permissible but disliked.

Key Terms
الظَّهِيرَةِ (al-zahirah): The midday time when the sun is at its zenith and shadows are shortest; the time just before noon when the sun is overhead.
قَائِمُ الظَّهِيرَةِ (qa'im al-zahirah): The moment when the sun stands still at its highest point (the start of the hated time).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which prayer is an exception to the prohibition of praying at sunset?
A) The Fajr prayer of the same day
B) The Asr prayer of the same day
C) Any obligatory prayer
D) The Isha prayer

Key Takeaway
The three prohibited times are for voluntary prayers; obligatory prayers (especially current 'Asr) are valid but disliked.

The Three Prohibited Times for Prayer and the Shafi'i Dispute
Matn of al-Quduri on prohibited prayer times with hadith proofs and Shafi'i dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibited times for prayer according to the Hanafi school, identify the exceptions (ʽAsr of that day and fard prayers caught on time), and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof from the hadith of Jubayr.

Core Idea
Prayer is prohibitively disliked at sunrise, zenith, and sunset, except ʽAsr of that day and fard prayers caught on time.

This passage from al-Quduri establishes the times when prayer is not permitted, supported by multiple hadith. The ruling is not absolute: the ʽAsr prayer of that day is allowed, and fard prayers that are caught at the beginning or end of these times are valid. The text also addresses the Shafi'i position that prayer is allowed at any time in Makkah, providing the Hanafi counterargument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling on the three prohibited times
Read the first sentence: 'لا تجوز الصلاة عند طلوع الشمس ولا عند قيامها في الظهيرة ولا عند غروبها.' Understand that this is a strong prohibition (makruh tahrimi) for non-fard prayers.
The three times are sunrise, zenith (when the sun is at its highest), and sunset.
2
Understand the exceptions
Note the exception for the 'Asr of that day at sunset: 'إلا عصر يومه عند غروب الشمس.' Also note the hadith of Abu Hurairah: catching one rak'ah of Fajr before sunrise or of 'Asr before sunset means the prayer is valid.
The exception allows fard prayers that are caught at the edge of the prohibited times.
3
Recognize the extension to Janazah and Sajda Tilawa
The matn states: 'ولا يصلي على جنازة ولا يسجد لتلاوة.' These acts are also prohibited at these times, except for the 'Asr prayer of that day.
Burial (tadfin) is allowed, as per the Urdu note.
4
Analyze the hadith proofs and their implications
Read the hadith of 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir, 'Amr ibn 'Abasah, Ibn 'Umar, and others. Focus on the explicit prohibitions and the rationale (e.g., sun rises between horns of Shaytan).
These hadith provide the evidence for the ruling, but they are ahad, making the prohibition zanni in thubut and dalala, hence makruh tahrimi not haram.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i position and the Hanafi response
Read the hadith of Jubayr ibn Mut'im, which is the Shafi'i proof. The Hanafi response is that this hadith is specific to Tawaf in Makkah and does not override the general prohibition. Consider the tarjih.
The practical difference: Hanafis avoid all prayers at these times even in Makkah, while Shafi'is allow them after Tawaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْأَوْقَاتِ الَّتِي تُكْرَهُ فِيهَا الصَّلَاةُ. لَا تَجُوزُ الصَّلَاةُ عِنْدَ طُلُوعِ الشَّمْسِ وَلَا عِنْدَ قِيَامِهَا فِي الظَّهِيرَةِ وَلَا عِنْدَ غُرُوبِهَا. وَلَا يُصَلِّي عَلَى جِنَازَةٍ وَلَا يَسْجُدُ لِتِلَاوَةٍ إِلَّا عَصْرَ يَوْمِهِ عِنْدَ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ. وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ يَتَنَفَّلَ بَعْدَ صَلَاةِ الْفَجْرِ حَتَّى تَطْلُعَ الشَّمْسُ وَبَعْدَ صَلَاةِ الْعَصْرِ حَتَّى تَغْرُبَ الشَّمْسُ.

ثُمَّ ذُكِرَ الْأَدِلَّةُ: (حَدِيثُ عُقْبَةَ بْنِ عَامِرٍ) قَالَ: ثَلَاثُ سَاعَاتٍ كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَنْهَانَا أَنْ نُصَلِّيَ فِيهِنَّ أَوْ أَنْ نَقْبُرَ فِيهِنَّ مَوْتَانَا: حِينَ تَطْلُعُ الشَّمْسُ بَازِغَةً حَتَّى تَرْتَفِعَ، وَحِينَ يَقُومُ قَائِمُ الظَّهِيرَةِ حَتَّى تَمِيلَ الشَّمْسُ، وَحِينَ تَضَيَّفُ الشَّمْسُ لِلْغُرُوبِ حَتَّى تَغْرُبَ. (رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ وَأَبُو دَاوُدَ وَالتِّرْمِذِيُّ)

وَحَدِيثُ عَمْرِو بْنِ عَبَسَةَ: عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: صَلِّ صَلَاةَ الصُّبْحِ ثُمَّ أَقْصِرْ عَنِ الصَّلَاةِ حَتَّى تَطْلُعَ الشَّمْسُ حَتَّى تَرْتَفِعَ فَإِنَّهَا تَطْلُعُ بَيْنَ قَرْنَيْ شَيْطَانٍ وَحِينَئِذٍ يَسْجُدُ لَهَا الْكُفَّارُ… إِلَى آخِرِ الْحَدِيثِ. (رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ وَالنَّسَائِيُّ)

وَحَدِيثُ ابْنِ عُمَرَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: لَا تَحَرَّوْا بِصَلَاتِكُمْ طُلُوعَ الشَّمْسِ وَلَا غُرُوبَهَا. (رَوَاهُ الْبُخَارِيُّ وَالتِّرْمِذِيُّ)

وَحَدِيثُ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ: مَنْ أَدْرَكَ مِنَ الصُّبْحِ رَكْعَةً قَبْلَ أَنْ تَطْلُعَ الشَّمْسُ فَقَدْ أَدْرَكَ الصُّبْحَ، وَمَنْ أَدْرَكَ رَكْعَةً مِنَ الْعَصْرِ قَبْلَ أَنْ تَغْرُبَ الشَّمْسُ فَقَدْ أَدْرَكَ الْعَصْرَ. (مُتَّفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ)

وَحَدِيثُ جُبَيْرِ بْنِ مُطْعِمٍ: أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: يَا بَنِي عَبْدِ مَنَافٍ، لَا تَقْنَعُوا أَحَدًا طَافَ بِهَذَا الْبَيْتِ وَصَلَّى أَيَّةَ سَاعَةٍ شَاءَ مِنْ لَيْلٍ أَوْ نَهَارٍ. (رَوَاهُ النَّسَائِيُّ) وَهَذَا دَلِيلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ.

وَحَدِيثُ أَبِي قَتَادَةَ: فِي النَّهْيِ عَنِ السَّجْدَةِ بَعْدَ الصُّبْحِ حَتَّى تَطْلُعَ الشَّمْسُ. (رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ)

وَحَدِيثُ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: نَهَى النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَنِ الصَّلَاةِ بَعْدَ الصُّبْحِ حَتَّى تُشْرِقَ الشَّمْسُ وَبَعْدَ الْعَصْرِ حَتَّى تَغْرُبَ. (رَوَاهُ الْبُخَارِيُّ)

الْأُصُولُ: تِين أَوقات مَنْعِيَّة مَيْن سَجْدَہ تِلَاوَت اور نماز جَنَازَہ كي بھي مُمَانَعَت ہے، البتہ تَدفين جائز ہے.
Chapter on the times when prayer is disliked. Prayer is not permissible at sunrise, nor at its zenith at midday, nor at its setting. No funeral prayer is performed, nor prostration for recitation, except the 'Asr of that day at sunset. And it is disliked to perform extra (nafl) prayer after the Fajr prayer until the sun rises, and after the 'Asr prayer until the sun sets.

Then the proofs are mentioned: (Hadith of 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir) said: Three times the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade us to pray in them or to bury our dead in them: when the sun is rising until it rises high, when the sun is at its zenith at midday until it declines, and when the sun inclines to set until it sets. (Narrated by Muslim, Abu Dawud, and al-Tirmidhi)

And the hadith of 'Amr ibn 'Abasah: from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: Pray the Fajr prayer, then refrain from prayer until the sun rises and rises high, for it rises between the two horns of a devil, and then the disbelievers prostrate to it… to the end of the hadith. (Narrated by Muslim and al-Nasa'i)

And the hadith of Ibn 'Umar: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Do not seek to offer your prayer at sunrise nor at sunset. (Narrated by al-Bukhari and al-Tirmidhi)

And the hadith of Abu Hurairah: Whoever catches one rak'ah of Fajr before the sun rises has caught Fajr, and whoever catches one rak'ah of 'Asr before the sun sets has caught 'Asr. (Agreed upon)

And the hadith of Jubayr ibn Mut'im: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: O Banu 'Abd Manaf, do not prevent anyone from performing Tawaf of this House and praying any hour he wishes, night or day. (Narrated by al-Nasa'i) This is the proof of al-Shafi'i.

And the hadith of Abu Qatadah: concerning the prohibition of prostration (sajdah) after Fajr until the sun rises. (Narrated by Abu Dawud)

And the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: The Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade prayer after Fajr until the sun rises and after 'Asr until the sun sets. (Narrated by al-Bukhari)

The principles: In these prohibited times, prostration of recitation and funeral prayer are also prohibited; however, burial is permissible.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the matn of al-Quduri on the times when prayer is prohibited. It first states the basic rule: prayer is not permissible at three specific times—sunrise (from the moment the sun begins to rise until it is fully elevated, approximately 15-20 minutes after sunrise), when the sun is at its zenith at midday (until it begins to decline), and at sunset (from the time it begins to set until it is fully set). The prohibition applies to all prayers, whether obligatory or voluntary, but with an important exception: the 'Asr prayer of that same day is permitted at the time of sunset, though it is disliked (makruh) if delayed beyond necessity. This is because 'Asr is a fard prayer that must be performed on time. Next, the text extends the prohibition to funeral prayer (Salat al-Janazah) and prostration of recitation (Sajdat al-Tilawah) at these times, again except for the 'Asr prayer of that day. Then it specifies that voluntary (nafl) prayers are disliked after Fajr until sunrise and after 'Asr until sunset. This is a weaker degree of prohibition (karaha tanzihiyya) compared to the first three times.

The text then provides multiple hadith proofs. The first hadith from 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir explicitly mentions the three times and includes a prohibition on burying the dead at those times. The second hadith from 'Amr ibn 'Abasah gives the rationale: the sun rises between the horns of Shaytan, and disbelievers prostrate to it, so believers should avoid prayer at that time. The third hadith from Ibn 'Umar forbids intentionally choosing sunrise or sunset for prayer. The fourth hadith from Abu Hurairah establishes that if one catches a rak'ah of Fajr before sunrise or of 'Asr before sunset, that prayer is valid, indicating that the prohibition is for intentional delay, not for catching the fard prayer. The fifth hadith (from Jubayr ibn Mut'im) is cited as the evidence of Imam al-Shafi'i, who permits prayer at any time in Makkah based on this tradition; the Hanafi response is that this hadith is specific to Makkah (some say it is abrogated) and the general prohibition remains. The sixth hadith (Abu Qatadah) and seventh (Ibn 'Abbas) reiterate the prohibition of sajdah and nafl after Fajr and 'Asr. Finally, the Urdu summary restates that Sajdat al-Tilawah and Janazah prayer are also prohibited at these times, but burial (tadfin) is allowed.

Key Terms
لَا تَجُوزُ (lā tajūzu): A legal term indicating that an act is not permissible, implying prohibition (tahrim or makruh tahrimi).
يُكْرَهُ (yukrahu): An act that is disliked; implies karaha tanzihiyya (non-prohibitive dislike) in this context of nafl after Fajr and 'Asr.
سَجْدَةُ تِلَاوَةٍ (sajdat al-tilāwah): Prostration performed when reciting or hearing a verse of prostration (sajda) in the Qur'an.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which prayer is allowed at the time of sunset during the three prohibited times?
A) Fajr prayer of the next day
B) 'Asr prayer of the same day
C) Maghrib prayer
D) Nafl prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits prayer at three specific times (sunrise, zenith, sunset) for non-fard prayers, with exceptions for caught fard prayers and the 'Asr of that day, based on strong hadith evidence.

Disliked Times for Prayer and Their Exceptions
Defines disliked times and exceptions for funeral prayer, sajdah tilawah, and qada prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on prohibited and disliked prayer times and identify which prayers are exempted.

Core Idea
Three absolute disliked times exist; after Fajr/Asr only nafl is prohibited, but qada, janazah, and sajdah are allowed.

This lesson examines the distinct Hanafi doctrine on times when prayer is disliked or prohibited. While all schools agree on three core times—sunrise, zenith, and sunset—the Hanafi school uniquely extends the prohibition of supererogatory prayers to after Fajr and Asr. However, important exceptions apply: missed obligatory prayers, funeral prayer, and prostration of recitation remain permissible during these windows. Understanding these rulings is essential for proper prayer scheduling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three core disliked times
From the hadith evidence, the Hanafi school identifies three absolute times when no prayer (except obligatory prayers that have been missed) should be initiated: at sunrise (until the sun fully rises), at zenith (when the sun is at its meridian until it declines), and at sunset (until the sun fully sets).
These are based on explicit prophetic prohibitions.
2
Recognize the prohibition of funeral prayer and sajdah tilawah at these three times
The text states 'وَلَا يُصَلِّي عَلَى جِنَازَةٍ وَلَا يَسْجُدُ لِتِلَاوَةِ' – one does not pray over a funeral nor prostrate for recitation during these three times. This is because they are considered acts of worship that resemble prayer in their form.
The exception mentioned in the OCR ("إِلَّا عَصْرَ يَوْمِهِ عِنْدَ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ") is corrupt; standard Hanafi position does not make an exception for 'Asr prayer of that day.
3
Note the Hanafi expansion: nafl prohibited after Fajr and Asr
The text adds that it is disliked (makruh) to perform supererogatory (nafl) prayers after Fajr until sunrise and after Asr until sunset. This is a unique Hanafi extension of the prohibition.
Other schools like the Shafi'i only prohibit nafl at the three absolute times.
4
Identify the exceptions for after Fajr and Asr
Despite the prohibition of nafl, the text explicitly allows the following during these two time periods: missed obligatory prayers (fawa'it), prostration of recitation (sajdah tilawah), and funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). The two rak'ahs of tawaf (rak'atay al-tawaf) are not allowed.
The Urdu usul adds that one with a long-standing qada obligation (qada 'umri) may perform them at home.
5
Clarify the ruling after the break of dawn (true Fajr)
Finally, the text mentions that after the true dawn (i.e., after Fajr time begins), it is disliked to perform any nafl beyond the two rak'ahs of Sunnah of Fajr. This includes the two rak'ahs of Fajr itself, which are exempted.
This ruling is specific to the period after Fajr time has entered, not after the congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْأَوْقَاتِ الَّتي تُكْرَهُ وَلَا يُصَلِّي عَلَى جِنَازَةٍ وَلَا يَسْجُدُ لِتِلَاوَةِ إِلَّا عَصْرَ يَوْمِهِ عِنْدَ غُرُوبِ الشَّمْسِ وَلَا عِنْدَ غُرُوبِهَا [؟] وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ يَتَنَفَّلَ بَعْدَ صَلَاةِ الْفَجْرِ حَتَّى تَطْلُعَ الشَّمْسُ وَبَعْدَ صَلَاةِ الْعَصْرِ حَتَّى تَغْرُبَ الشَّمْسُ وَلَا بَأْسَ أَنْ يُصَلِّيَ فِي هَذَيْنِ الْوَقْتَيْنِ الْفَوَائِتَ وَيَسْجُدَ لِلتَّلَاوَةِ وَيُصَلِّيَ عَلَى الْجِنَازَةِ وَلَا يُصَلِّي رَكْعَتَي الطَّوَافِ وَيُكْرَهُ أَنْ يَتَنَفَّلَ بَعْدَ طُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ بِأَكْثَرَ مِنْ رَكْعَتَي الْفَجْرِ

اصول : مذکورہ مکروہ اوقات میں جہاں نوافل کی ممانعت آئی ہے وہاں ایک گنجائش ہے قضاء عمری پڑھنے والے کے لئے کہ فوت شدہ نمازیں ان اوقات میں ادا کر سکتے ہیں البتہ اس طرح کا عمل گھر میں انجام دیں۔
The times that are disliked: and one does not pray over a funeral nor prostrate for recitation except for the 'Asr of his day at the setting of the sun and not at its setting [؟]. And it is disliked to perform supererogatory prayer after the Fajr prayer until the sun rises, and after the Asr prayer until the sun sets. And there is no harm in praying missed prayers in these two times, and prostrating for recitation, and praying over a funeral, and one does not pray the two rak'ahs of tawaf, and it is disliked to perform supererogatory prayer after dawn more than the two rak'ahs of Fajr.

Principle: In the mentioned disliked times where supererogatory prayers are prohibited, there is an allowance for the one performing qada' 'umri to offer the missed prayers in these times, but he should perform such an act at home.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Al-Quduri's matn, expanded with hadith evidence. It addresses the times when prayer is disliked (makruh). The text first states that funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) and prostration of recitation (sajdah tilawah) are not performed during the disliked times. The exception mentioned is problematic in the OCR, but the standard Hanafi position is that these are prohibited at three specific times: sunrise, zenith, and sunset. The next ruling states that it is disliked to perform supererogatory (nafl) prayers after Fajr until sunrise and after Asr until sunset. However, there is an important concession: missed obligatory prayers (fawa'it) can be made up during these two times (after Fajr and after Asr). Similarly, sajdah tilawah and funeral prayer are permissible in these two times. The two rak'ahs of tawaf are not to be performed during these times. Additionally, after the break of dawn (true Fajr), it is disliked to perform any supererogatory prayer beyond the two rak'ahs of Fajr sunnah. The Urdu usul (principle) clarifies that in the disliked times where nafl is prohibited, there is a dispensation for one who has a long-standing obligation of missed prayers (qada' 'umri) to perform them, but he should do so at home to avoid public display.

Key Terms
مکروہ اوقات (makruh awqat): The times when certain prayers are disliked according to the Hanafi school.
قضاء عمری (qada' 'umri): The obligation of making up missed prayers accumulated over one's lifetime.
رکعتی الطواف (rak'atay al-tawaf): The two rak'ahs prayed after completing tawaf around the Kaaba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After Fajr prayer until sunrise, which of the following is permissible (la ba'sa) according to the passage?
A) Performing supererogatory (nafl) prayers
B) Making up missed obligatory prayers (fawa'it)
C) Praying the two rak'ahs of tawaf
D) Performing any voluntary prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between three absolute disliked times (sunrise, zenith, sunset) and the after-Fajr/Asr periods where nafl is prohibited but qada, janazah, and sajdah are permitted.
