8 min
Flexibility of Nafl: Sitting Without Excuse and Praying on a Mount
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute on nafl flexibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sitting without excuse in nafl after beginning standing, explain the evidence and the intra-Hanafi dispute, and describe the permissibility of nafl on a mount with gestures (imā').

Core Idea
Nafl prayers allow flexibility: sitting without excuse and praying on a mount are permitted by Abu Hanifa, based on prophetic practice.

This passage from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar addresses two scenarios that highlight the relative ease of voluntary prayers. The first is whether one may sit after beginning standing without excuse; the second is praying on a mount while traveling. Both rulings are supported by hadith and involve an important intra-Hanafi ikhtilāf on the first issue. Understanding these rulings helps clarify the school's approach to supererogatory acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings in the matn
Read the first sentence: it states two permissions: (1) if one begins nafl standing and then sits without excuse, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa; (2) a person outside the city may perform nafl on his mount, gesturing towards any direction.
The matn uses 'jāza' for the first ruling, implying permissibility.
2
Locate the hadith proofs
The commentary provides several hadith: the hadith of Aisha showing the Prophet alternating sitting and standing in nafl; and the hadith of Ibn Umar and Amir ibn Rabi'ah showing prayer on a mount with gestures.
These hadith are from Bukhari and Muslim, indicating strong authentication.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on sitting
Abu Hanifa allows sitting without excuse, citing the hadith and the general ease of nafl. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) disallow it, drawing an analogy (qiyas) to a vowed prayer (nadhr).
The Urdu note explains the usul: Sahibayn preferred qiyas over the specific hadith.
4
Understand the Sahibayn's qiyas
Just as a person who vows to pray standing must complete it standing, so too should one who begins nafl standing be bound to remain standing. Abu Hanifa responds that nafl is more flexible than a vow.
This highlights a tension between following apparent sunna and strict analogy.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi fatwa holds that sitting without excuse is valid but makruh tanzihan (moderately disliked). The safer view follows Sahibayn, but Abu Hanifa's position remains within the school.
The ruling on the mount is universally accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَصل فِي الْقِرَاءَةِ ل وَإِنْ افْتَتَحَهَا قَائِمًا ثُمَّ قَعَدَ مِنْ غَيْرِ عُذْرٍ جَازَ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَمَنْ كَانَ خَارِجَ الْمِصْرِ يَتَنَفَّلُ عَلَى دَابَّتِهِ إِلَى أَي جِهَةٍ تَوَجَّهَتْ بِهِ يُومِنُ إِيمَاءً إِلَى أَيِّ جِهَةٍ تَوَجَّهَتْ بِهِ

وجه (۲)الحديث لثبوت وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ يَقْضِي أَرْبَعًا \ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ أُمِّ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ : أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم «كَانَ يُصَلِّي جَالِسًا، فَيَقْرَأُ وَهُوَ جَالِسٌ، فَإِذَا بَقِيَ مِنْ قِرَاءَتِهِ نَحْوَ مِنْ ثَلَاثِينَ أَوْ أَرْبَعِينَ آيَةً، قَامَ فَقَرَأَهَا وَهُوَ قَائِمٌ، ثُمَّ يَرْكَعُ، ثُمَّ سَجَدَ، يَفْعَلُ فِي الرَّكْعَةِ الثَّانِيَةِ مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ،(بخاري بَابٌ : إِذَا صَلَّى قَاعِدًا ثُمَّ صَحَ أَوْ وَجَدَ خِفَّةً تَمَّمَ مَا بَقِيَ ، نمبر 1119/مسلم شريف، بَاب جَوَازِ النَّافِلَةِ قَائِمًا وَقَاعِدًا، وَفِعْلِ بَعْضِ الرَّكْعَةِ قَائِمًا وَبَعْضِهَا قَاعِدًا ، نمبر 731/سنن ترمذي، بَابٌ فِيمَنْ يَتَطَوَّعُ جَالِسًا ، نمبر 374)

(۳) الحديث لثبوت وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ يَقْضِي أَرْبَعًا \ سَأَلْتُ عَائِشَةَ عَنْ صلاة رسول الله عَنْ تَطَوُّعِهِ.... فَيُصَلِّي رَكْعَتَيْنِ وَيُصَلِّي بِالنَّاسِ الْعِشَاءَ، وَيَدْخُلُ بَيْتِي فَيُصَلِّي رَكْعَتَيْنِ، (مسلم) شريف، بَاب جَوَازِ النَّافِلَةِ قَائِمًا وَقَاعِدًا، وَفِعْلِ بَعْضِ الرَّكْعَةِ قَائِمًا وَبَعْضِهَا قَاعِدًا ، نمبر 730) وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ افْتَتَحَهَا قَائِمًا ثُمَّ قَعَدَ مِنْ غَيْرِ عُذْرٍ \ كَانَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ عُمَرَ الله عنهما يُصَلِّي فِي السَّفَرِ عَلَى رَاحِلَتِهِ أَيْنَمَا تَوَجَّهَتْ، يُومِيُّ. وَذَكَرَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ: أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ كَانَ يَفْعَلُهُ ، بخاري شريف ، بَابُ الْإِيمَاءِ عَلَى الدَّابَّةِ ، نمبر 1096/ مسلم شريف، بَاب جَوَازِ صَلَاةِ النَّافِلَةِ عَلَى الدَّابَّةِ فِي السَّفَرِ حَيْثُ تَوَجَّهَتْ ، غمبر (700)

رضي

وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ افْتَتَحَهَا قَائِمًا ثُمَّ قَعَدَ مِنْ غَيْرِ عُذْرِ \ أَنَّ عَامِرَ بْنَ رَبِيعَةَ أَخْبَرَهُ قَالَ: «رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَهُوَ عَلَى الرَّاحِلَةِ يُسَبِّحُ، يُومِنُ بِرَأْسِهِ قِبَلَ أَي وَجْهِ تَوَجَّهَ، وَلَمْ يَكُنْ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَصْنَعُ ذَلِكَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ الْمَكْتُوبَةِ، ، (بخاري شريف ، بَابٌ : يَنْزِلُ لِلْمَكْتُوبَةِ، غبر 1097) اصول : کھڑے ہو کر نفل پڑھنے والا بغیر عذر کے بیٹھ جائے تو کوئی حرج نہیں ہے امام صاحب نزدیک۔ اصول : صاحبین کے نزدیک کھڑے ہو کر نفل پڑھنے والا کا بغیر عذر کے بیٹھنا جائز نہیں ہے، قیاس کرتے ہوئے نذر والے حکم پر۔
Section on recitation: And if one opens it (the prayer) standing, then sits without an excuse, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa. And whoever is outside the city and performs voluntary prayer on his mount, facing whatever direction it faces, he gestures with his head (imaa) towards whatever direction it faces.

Proof (2): Hadith for proof, and Abu Yusuf said: he must make up four [?]. From Aisha, Mother of the Believers: that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to pray sitting, and he would recite while sitting, and when about thirty or forty verses remained of his recitation, he would stand and recite them standing, then bow, then prostrate. He would do likewise in the second rak'ah. (Bukhari, Muslim, Tirmidhi)

Proof (3): Hadith for proof, and Abu Yusuf said: he must make up four [?]. I asked Aisha about the voluntary prayer of the Messenger of Allah... He would pray two rak'ahs and lead the people in Isha, then enter my house and pray two rak'ahs. (Muslim)

Proof (a): Hadith for proof: 'And if one opens it standing then sits without an excuse' - Abdullah ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) used to pray on his mount while traveling, wherever it faced, gesturing. And Abdullah mentioned that the Prophet used to do it. (Bukhari, Muslim)

Proof (2): Hadith for proof: 'And if one opens it standing then sits without an excuse' - That Amir ibn Rabi'ah informed him: He said, 'I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) on a mount performing supererogatory prayer, gesturing with his head to whichever direction he faced, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did not do that in the obligatory prayer.' (Bukhari)

Principles: According to Imam Abu Hanifa, one who begins voluntary prayer standing and then sits without an excuse, there is no harm. According to the Sahibayn, it is not permissible for one who begins voluntary prayer standing to sit without an excuse, drawing analogy to the ruling of a vow.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Al-Quduri's matn, expanded with hadith evidence and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states two rulings: (1) If one begins a voluntary prayer standing and then sits without an excuse, it is permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa. (2) A person outside the city (i.e., traveling) may perform voluntary prayer on his mount, gesturing (imaa') instead of bowing and prostrating, facing any direction the mount goes. The commentator then provides hadith proofs. The hadith from Aisha shows the Prophet alternating between sitting and standing in nafl. The hadith from Ibn Umar and Amir ibn Rabi'ah support praying on a mount with gestures. Then an Urdu note clarifies the intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa allows sitting in nafl without excuse, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disallow it, analogizing it to the strict ruling of a vowed prayer (which must be performed as intended). This is a usul point: the Sahibayn prefer qiyas (analogy) here, while Abu Hanifa relies on the general permissibility of nafl. The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) in the Hanafi school is that sitting without excuse in nafl is valid but makruh tanzihan, while many later scholars follow the Sahibayn's view as more precautionary.

Key Terms
نَفْل (nafl): Voluntary prayer, supererogatory prayer beyond the obligatory ones.
إِيمَاء (imā'): Gesturing with the head or body to indicate bowing (ruku') and prostration (sajdah) when unable to perform the full movements, e.g., on a mount or due to illness.
قَعَدَ (qa'ada): To sit (in prayer). In this context, sitting in the posture of qa'dah (sitting position) during voluntary prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on sitting without a valid excuse after beginning a voluntary prayer standing?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but makruh tanzihan (moderately disliked).
C) The prayer is perfectly valid and recommended.
D) The prayer is valid only if the person intends to sit from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
Nafl prayers permit postural flexibility: sitting without excuse is valid but disliked, and praying on a mount with gestures is fully allowed.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Sujud al-Sahw: Definition, Causes, and Evidence
Definition and evidence for Sujud al-Sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define Sujud al-Sahw, state its wajib nature, identify its causes, and explain the Hanafi position on timing (after salam for increase, before salam for decrease) with evidence.

Core Idea
Sujud al-Sahw is wajib to compensate for forgetful additions or omissions in prayer.

This passage from Al-Quduri opens the chapter on Sujud al-Sahw, defining its procedure and causes. It provides the primary hadith evidence supporting the Hanafi position and touches on the key inter-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i school regarding the timing of the prostration. Understanding this ruling is essential for correctly performing prayers when forgetfulness occurs.

Guided Path
1
Define Sujud al-Sahw and state its ruling
Identify the term and the hukm level (wajib). Note that it is not fard; omitting it does not invalidate the prayer but requires compensation.
The passage explicitly states the procedure: after salam, two prostrations, tashahhud, then salam again.
2
Identify the two primary causes
Distinguish between ziyadah (addition of an act of the same type not originally in prayer) and nuqsan (omission of a sunnah act). The passage also mentions four detailed causes: advancing/delaying, repeating, changing manner, omitting a fard or wajib.
The definition of 'fi'lan min jinsiha laysa minha' is key for additions.
3
Analyze the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (extra rak'ah)
The Prophet prayed Zuhr with five rak'ahs, then after being informed, he performed two sajdahs after the salam. This establishes sujud after salam for increase.
Hadith from Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Analyze the hadith of Ibn Buhaynah (missing tashahhud)
The Prophet stood up after two rak'ahs without sitting, then prostrated before the salam. This establishes sujud before salam for deficiency.
Hadith from Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi. This is also the Shafi'i proof for all sujud being before salam.
5
Compare Hanafi and Shafi'i positions
Hanafis harmonize: increase → after salam; decrease → before salam. Shafi'is hold all sujud is before salam. Understand the thamarah al-khilaf in practice.
The Hanafi response is supported by the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn which shows sujud after salam with tashahhud.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ سُجُودِ السَّهْو ل سجود السهو في الزَّيَادَةِ وَالتَّقْصَانِ بَعْدَ السَّلَامِ يَسْجُدُ سَجْدَتَيْنِ ثُمَّ يَتَشَهدُ وَيُسَلِّمُ . وَالسَّهو يَلْزَمُهُ إِذَا زَادَ فِي صَلَاتِهِ فِعْلًا مِنْ جِنْسِهَا لَيْسَ مِنْهَا أَوْ تَرَكَ فِعْلًا مَسْنُونًا

لوجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت سُجُودُ السَّهْوِ فِي الزِّيَادَةِ وَالنُّقْصَانِ بَعْدَ السَّلَامِ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ قَالَ: صَلَّى النَّبِيُّ الله الظُّهْرَ خَمْسًا ، فَقَالُوا: أَزِيدَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ؟ قَالَ: وَمَا ذَاكَ؟ قَالُوا: صَلَّيْتَ خَمْسًا فَتَنَى رِجْلَيْهِ، وَسَجَدَ سَجْدَتَيْنِ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الْقِبْلَةِ وَمَنْ لَمْ يَرَ الْإِعَادَةَ عَلَى مَنْ سَهَا، نمبر 404/مسلم شريف، بَاب السَّهْوِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ وَالسُّجُودِ لَهُ، نمبر 572)

وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت سُجُودُ السَّهْوِ فِي الزِّيَادَةِ وَالنُّقْصَانِ بَعْدَ السَّلَامِ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ ابْنِ بحيْنَةَ، أَنَّهُ قَالَ: «صَلَّى لَنَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ الله ، رَكْعَتَيْنِ، ثُمَّ قَامَ فَلَمْ يَجْلِسْ فَقَامَ النَّاسُ مَعَهُ، فَلَمَّا قَضَى صَلَاتَهُ وَانْتَظَرْنَا التَّسْلِيمَ كَبَّرَ ، فَسَجَدَ سَجْدَتَيْنِ وَهُوَ جَالِسٌ قَبْلَ التَّسْلِيمِ، ثُمَّ سَلَّمَ صلى الله عليه وسلم، سنن ابوداود بَابُ مَنْ قَامَ مِنْ ثِنْتَيْنِ وَلَمْ يَتَشَهَّدْ ، نمبر 1034/سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الإِمَامِ يَنْهَضُ فِي الرَّكْعَتَيْنِ نَاسِيًا، نمبر 364/) وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت سُجُودُ السَّهْو في الزيَادَةِ وَالتَّقْصَانِ بَعْدَ السَّلَامِ \ عَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْن حُصَيْنٍ، «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم صَلَّى بِهِمْ فَسَهَا، فَسَجَدَ سَجْدَتَيْنِ، ثُمَّ تَشَهَّدَ ثُمَّ سَلَّمَ، (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ سَجْدَتَي السَّهْوِ فِيهِمَا تَشَهُدٌ وَتَسْلِيمننمبر 1039/سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي التَّشَهُدِ فِي سَجْدَتي السهو، نمبر 395)

وجه (۱) دليل الشافعى الحديث لثبوت سُجُودُ السَّهْوِ فِي الزِّيَادَةِ وَالنُّقْصَانِ بَعْدَ السَّلَامِ افَسَجَدَ سَجْدَتَيْنِ وَهُوَ جَالِسٌ قَبْلَ التَسْلِيمِ، ثُمَّ سَلَّمَ ، سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَنْ قَامَ مِنْ ثِنْتَيْنِ وَلَمْ يَتَشَهَّد، نمبر 1034/سنن ترمذى، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الإِمَامِ يَنْهَضُ فِي الرَّكْعَتَيْنِ نَاسِيَّا، نمبر 364/سنن نسائي، مَا يَفْعَلُ مَنْ قَامَ مِنَ اثْنَتَيْنِ نَاسِيًا وَلَمْ يَتَشَهَّدْ، نمبر 1223) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت سُجُودُ السَّهْوِ فِي الزِّيَادَةِ وَالنُّقْصَانِ بَعْدَ السَّلَامِ \ قَالَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ : اصول : سجدہ سہو کے اسباب : اکسی فرض یا واجب عمل کو مقدم یا موخر کر دینا۲ فرض یا واجب کو مکرر کر دینا واجب یا فرض کی صفت بدل دینا ہم کسی واجب یا فرض کو سہو ترک کر دینا۔
Chapter of Sujud al-Sahw: Sujud al-Sahw is for increase and decrease; after the salam, he performs two prostrations, then recites tashahhud, and then says salam. And forgetfulness becomes binding (lazim) upon him when he adds to his prayer an act of its type (jins) that is not from it, or when he omits an act that is sunnah.

Proof (1): Hadith for proof: Sujud al-Sahw is for increase and decrease after salam. From Abdullah (ibn Mas'ud) who said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed Zuhr with five rak'ahs. They said: Has there been an increase in the prayer? He said: What is that? They said: You prayed five. So he bent his legs and prostrated two prostrations. (Bukhari, Muslim)

Proof (2): Hadith for proof: Sujud al-Sahw is for increase and decrease after salam. From Abdullah ibn Buhaynah: He said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) led us in prayer for two rak'ahs, then stood up and did not sit. The people stood with him. When he completed his prayer and we expected the taslim, he said takbir and prostrated two prostrations while sitting before the taslim, then said salam. (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi)

Proof (3): Hadith for proof: Sujud al-Sahw is for increase and decrease after salam. From Imran ibn Husayn: That the Prophet (peace be upon him) led them in prayer and forgot, so he prostrated two prostrations, then recited tashahhud, then said salam. (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi)

Proof (1): Evidence of al-Shafi'i: Hadith for proof: Sujud al-Sahw is for increase and decrease after salam: 'then he prostrated two prostrations while sitting before the taslim, then said salam.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i)

Proof (1): Hadith for proof: Sujud al-Sahw is for increase and decrease after salam. Abdullah said: Principles: The causes of Sujud al-Sahw: (1) to bring forward or delay a fard or wajib act, (2) to repeat a fard or wajib act, (3) to change the description (sifah) of a fard or wajib, (4) to omit a fard or wajib due to forgetfulness.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Sujud al-Sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) in Al-Quduri. The matn defines two key elements: (1) the procedure – after the salam of the prayer, one performs two sajdahs, then tashahhud, then salam again; (2) the causes – when a worshipper adds an act from the same genus (jins) of prayer that is not part of the prayer (e.g., an extra rak'ah or extra rukn), or omits a sunnah act (like tashahhud in the first sitting). The commentator then provides three hadith proofs: the first (from Ibn Mas'ud) shows sujud after salam for an extra rak'ah; the second (from Ibn Buhaynah) shows sujud before salam for a missed sitting; the third (from Imran ibn Husayn) shows sujud after salam with tashahhud. Then a note mentions the Shafi'i evidence: using the hadith of Ibn Buhaynah to argue that sujud al-sahw is performed before salam in all cases. This is the point of ikhtilaf: Hanafis hold that sujud al-sahw is generally after salam for increase (ziyadah) and before salam for deficiency (nuqsan), but the matn here says 'after salam' because the chapter focuses on the common case of addition. The Urdu section at the end lists the general causes of sujud al-sahw: (1) advancing or delaying a fard/wajib action, (2) repeating a fard/wajib, (3) changing the manner (sifah) of a fard/wajib, (4) omitting a fard/wajib due to forgetfulness. These are the situations that necessitate sujud al-sahw.

Key Terms
سُجُودُ السَّهْو (sujūd al-sahw): Two extra prostrations performed to compensate for forgetful errors during prayer, either before or after the salam depending on the type of error.
زِيَادَة (ziyādah): Increase: adding an extra element (e.g., extra rak'ah, extra rukn) in prayer due to forgetfulness.
نُقْصَان (nuqsān): Decrease: omitting a required element (e.g., tashahhud in the first sitting) due to forgetfulness.
فِعْلًا مِنْ جِنْسِهَا لَيْسَ مِنْهَا (fi'lan min jinsihā laysa minhā): An act of the same type (jins) as the prayer but not part of it, e.g., an extra bowing or prostration or rak'ah.
تَشَهُّد (tashahhud): The recitation of 'At-tahiyyat lillahi...' in the sitting position of prayer; in sujud al-sahw, it is recited after the two prostrations before the final salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, for which of the following does Sujud al-Sahw become wajib?
A) Adding an extra rak'ah by mistake.
B) Forgetting to recite a surah after Fatihah.
C) Speaking intentionally in prayer.
D) Moving one's hand unnecessarily.

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-Sahw is a wajib compensation for forgetful additions or omissions in prayer, performed after salam for additions and before salam for deficiencies, supported by clear prophetic actions.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Causes of Sujud al-Sahw and the Rule of the Imam's Forgetfulness
Matn and hadith on causes of sujud al-sahw and imam's sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the acts whose omission necessitates sajdah sahw and explain why the imam's forgetfulness obligates the follower.

Core Idea
Omitting a wajib or making a jahr/sirr error is compensated by sajdah sahw; the imam's sahw binds the follower.

This lesson covers the opening portion of Al-Quduri's chapter on Sujud al-Sahw, where the matn specifies the causes that trigger the prostration. We will also examine the fundamental rule that the imam's forgetfulness obligates the follower to prostrate, supported by hadith from the Prophet's own practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts that necessitate sajdah sahw
From the matn, list the specific wajib acts omitted or the error of jahr/sirr that require sajdah sahw.
These are: leaving Fatiha, Qunut, Tashahhud, Takbirat al-Eidain, or imam reciting aloud in silent prayer or silently in aloud prayer.
2
Understand the hukm level of sajdah sahw
In the Hanafi school, sajdah sahw is wajib (not fard). It compensates for forgetfulness without invalidating the prayer.
Wajib is a distinct category between fard and sunnah.
3
Analyze the hadith proof for sajdah sahw
The Prophet (peace be upon him) performed two prostrations after salam due to forgetfulness (increase or decrease). This action establishes the legitimacy and obligation.
The hadith is narrated by Muslim and Abu Dawud; it is zanni al-thubut but sufficient for wajib.
4
Apply the rule of imam's sahw
The matn states that the imam's forgetfulness obligates the follower to prostrate. If the imam does not prostrate, the follower should not.
This is based on the principle that the imam is the guarantor (damin) for the follower's prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ سُجُودِ السَّهْو
القدوري مع احاديثه أَوْ تَرَكَ قِرَاءَةَ فَاتِحَةِ الْكِتَابِ وَالْقُنُوتَ أَوْ التَّشَهدَ أَوْ تَكْبِيرَاتِ الْعِيدَيْنِ أَوْ جَهَرَ الْإِمَامُ فِيمَا يُخَافَتُ فِيهِ أَوْ خَافَتَ فِيمَا يُجْهَرُ فِيهِ ؟ وَسَهْوُ الْإِمَامِ يُوجِبُ عَلَى الْمُؤْتَمَ السُّجُودَ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْجُدْ الْإِمَامُ لَمْ يَسْجُدُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ.
صَلَّى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ إِبْرَاهِيمُ: زَادَ أَوْ نَقَصَ فَلَمَّا سَلَّمَ قِيلَ لَهُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ! أَحَدَثَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ شَيْءٍ؟ قَالَ "وَمَا ذَاكَ ؟ " قَالُوا: صَلَّيْتَ كَذَا وَكَذَا قَالَ فَتَى رِجْلَيْهِ، وَاسْتَقْبَلَ الْقِبْلَةَ، فَسَجَدَ سَجْدَتَيْنِ، ثُمَّ سَلَّمَ. ثُمَّ أَقْبَلَ عَلَيْنَا بِوَجْهِهِ فَقَالَ إِنَّهُ لَوْ حَدَثَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ شَيْءٌ أَنْبَأْتُكُمْ بِهِ وَلَكِنْ إِنَّمَا أَنَا بَشَرٌ أَنْسَى كَمَا تَنْسَوْنَ. فَإِذَا نَسِيتُ فَذَكَّرُونِي. وَإِذَا شَكَّ أَحَدُكُمْ فِي صَلَاتِهِ فَلْيَتَحَرَّ الصَّوَابَ. فَلْيُتِمَّ عَلَيْهِ ثُمَّ لِيَسْجُدْ سَجْدَتَيْنِ (مسلم شریف، بَاب السَّهْوِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ وَالسُّجُودِ لَه، نمبر 572/سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَنْ قَالَ: يُتِمُّ عَلَى أَكْبَرِ ظَنِّهِ، نمبر 1029).
وجه : (۱)قول التابعى لثبوت سُجُودُ السَّهْوِ فِي الرِّيَادَةِ وَالنُّقْصَانِ بَعْدَ السَّلَامِ\nعَنِ الثَّوْرِيِّ قَالَ: «إِذَا قُمْتَ فِيمَا يُجْلَسُ فِيهِ، أَوْ جَلَسْتَ فِيمَا يُقَامُ فِيهِ، أَوْ جَهَرْتَ فِيمَا يُخَافَتُ فِيهِ، أَوْ خَافَتَّ فِيمَا يُجْهَرُ فِيهِ نَاسِيًا سَجَدْتَ سَجْدَتَي السَّهْوِ (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ إِذَا قَامَ فِيمَا يُقْعَدُ فِيهِ أَوْ قَعَدَ فِيمَا يُقَامُ أَوْ سَلَّمَ فِي مَثْى،نمبر 3495/مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَنْ كَانَ إِذَا جَهَرَ فِيمَا يُخَافَتُ فِيهِ سَجَدَ سَجْدَتَي السَّهْوِ،نمبر 3649).
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت سُجُودُ السَّهْوِ فِي الزِيَادَةِ وَالتَّقْصَانِ بَعْدَ السَّلَامِ\nعَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ أَبِي قَتَادَةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ قَالَ: «كَانَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقْرَأُ فِي الرَّكْعَتَيْنِ مِنَ الظُّهْرِ وَالْعَصْرِ بِفَاتِحَةِ الْكِتَابِ وَسُورَةٍ سُورَةٍ، وَيُسْمِعُنَا الْآيَةَ أَحْيَانًا (بخاري بَابُ الْقِرَاءَةِ فِي الْعَصْر ، نمبر 762/ مسلم شریف ، باب الْقِرَاءَةِ فِي الظُّهْرِ وَالْعَصْرِ ، نمبر 451).
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَسَهْوُ الْإِمَامِ يُوجِبُ عَلَى الْمُؤْتَمَ السُّجُودَ\nعَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ بُكَيْنَةَ الْأَسْدِي حَلِيفِ بَنِي عَبْدِ الْمُطَّلِبِ : «أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَامَ فِي صَلَاةِ الظُّهْرِ وَعَلَيْهِ جُلُوسٌ، فَلَمَّا أَتَمَّ صَلَاتَهُ سَجَدَ سَجْدَتَيْنِ، فَكَبَّرَ فِي كُلِّ سَجْدَةٍ وَهُوَ جَالِسٌ قَبْلَ أَنْ يُسَلَّمَ، وَسَجَدَهُمَا النَّاسُ مَعَهُ، مَكَانَ مَا نَسِيَ مِنَ الْجُلُوسِ» تَابَعَهُ ابْنُ جُرَيْجٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ شِهَابٍ فِي التَّكْبِيرِ (بخاري شريف، بَابُ مَنْ يُكَبِرُ فِي سَجْدَتَي السَّهْوِ، نمبر 1230).
أصول: نماز میں فعل واجب یا فاتحہ یا قنوت یا عیدین ترک ہو گئیں تو سجدہ سہو لازم ہو گا.
د. وَإِنْ سَهَا الْمُؤْتَمُّ لَمْ يَلْزَمُ الإِمَامَ وَلَا الْمُؤْتَمَ السُّجُودُ لَهُ. وَمَنْ سَهَا عَنْ الْقَعْدَةِ الْأُولَى ثُمَّ ذَكَرَ وَهُوَ إِلَى حَالِ الْقُعُودِ أَقْرَبُ عَادَ فَقَعَدَ وَتَشَهَّدَ وَإِنْ كَانَ إِلَى حَالِ الْقِيَامِ أَقْرَبَ لَمْ يُعِدْ وَيَسْجُدُ لِلسَّهْوِ. وَإِنْ سَهَا عَنْ الْقَعْدَةِ الْأَخِيرَةِ فَقَامَ إِلَى الْخَامِسَةِ رَجَعَ إِلَى الْقَعْدَةِ مَا لَمْ يَسْجُدْ وَأَلْغَى الْخَامِسَةَ وَيَسْجُدُ لِلسَّهْوِ. وَإِنْ قَيَّدَ الْخَامِسَةَ بِسَجْدَةٍ بَطَلَ فَرْضُهُ وَتَحَوَّلَتْ صَلَاتُهُ نَفْلًا وَكَانَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَضُمَّ إِلَيْهَا رَكْعَةً سَادِسَةً. وَإِنْ قَعَدَ فِي الرَّابِعَةِ قَدْرَ التَّشَهُدِ ثُمَّ قَامَ إِلَى الْخَامِسَةِ وَلَمْ يُسَلَّمْ يَظُنُّهَا الْقَعْدَةَ الْأُولَى عَادَ إِلَى الْقُعُودِ مَا لَمْ يَسْجُدْ فِي الْخَامِسَةِ وَيُسَلِّمُ وَيَسْجُدُ لِلسَّهو.
د. وجه (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ سَهَا الْمُؤْتَمُّ لَمْ يَلْزَمُ الإِمَامَ\nعَنْ عُمَرَ ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لَيْسَ عَلَى مَنْ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ سَهْوٌ ، فَإِنْ سَهَا الْإِمَامُ فَعَلَيْهِ وَعَلَى مَنْ خَلْفَهُ السَّهْوُ ، وَإِنْ سَهَا مَنْ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ فَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ سَهْوٌ وَالْإِمَامُ كَافِيهِ (سنن دارقطنی، بَابُ: لَيْسَ عَلَى الْمُقْتَدِي سَهْوَ وَعَلَيْهِ سَهْوَ الْإِمَامِ ، نمبر 1413).
وجه : (۲)قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ سَهَا الْمُؤْتَمُّ لَمْ يَلْزَمُ الإِمَامَ\nعَنْ حَمَّادٍ قَالَ: «إِذَا سَهَا الْإِمَامُ سَجَدَ مَنْ خَلْفَهُ، وَإِذَا سَهَا مَنْ خَلْفَهُ فَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِمْ حَتَّى لا يَضُرُّهُمْ سَهْوٌ مَعَ الْإِمَامِ (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ هَلْ عَلَى مَنْ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ سَهْوٌ ، نمبر 3509).
د وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت الرجوع إلى القعود إذا لم يستو قائما\nعَنِ الْمُغِيرَةِ بْن شُعْبَةَ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إِذَا قَامَ الْإِمَامُ فِي الرَّكْعَتَيْنِ، فَإِنْ ذَكَرَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَسْتَوِيَ قَائِمًا فَلْيَجْلِسْ، فَإِنِ اسْتَوَى قَائِمًا فَلَا يَجْلِسْ، وَيَسْجُدْ سَجْدَتَيِ السَّهْوِ (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَنْ نَسِيَ أَنْ يَتَشَهَّدَ وَهُوَ جالس،نمبر 1036/سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي سَجْدَتَي السَّهْوِ قَبْلَ السَّلَامِ، نمبر 391).
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت حكم من صلى خمسا ولم يجلس في الرابعة\nعَنْ حَمَّادٍ قَالَ: «إِذَا صَلَّى الرَّجُلُ خَمْسًا وَلَمْ يَجْلِسْ فِي الرَّابِعَةِ، فَإِنَّهُ يَزِيدُ السَّادِسَةَ، ثُمَّ يُسَلِّمُ ثُمَّ يَسْتَأْنِفُ صَلَاتَهُ (مصنف عبد الرازاق، بَابُ الرَّجُلِ يُصَلِّي الظُّهْرَ أَوِ الْعَصْرِ خَمْسًا، نمبر 3461).
أصول: امام سے سہو ہو اتو مقتدی پر بھی سجدہ لازم ہو گا کیونکہ امام ضامن ہے ، اور مقتدی کے سہو سے کچھ نہیں
Chapter on Prostration of Forgetfulness. Al-Quduri with his hadith: Or he left recitation of Fatiha, Qunut, Tashahhud, or Takbirat of the two Eids, or the imam recited aloud where it is silent, or silently where it is aloud. And the imam's forgetfulness obligates the follower to prostrate; if the imam does not prostrate, the follower does not prostrate. ... [After hadith proofs] And if the follower forgets, it does not obligate the imam nor the follower to prostrate for it. Whoever forgets the first sitting then remembers while he is closer to sitting, he returns and sits and recites tashahhud; if he is closer to standing, he does not return and prostrates for forgetfulness. Whoever forgets the last sitting and stands for a fifth, he returns to sitting as long as he has not prostrated, and cancels the fifth and prostrates for forgetfulness. If he ties the fifth with a prostration, his obligatory prayer becomes invalid and his prayer becomes voluntary, and he must add a sixth rak'ah. If he sits in the fourth to the extent of tashahhud then stands for the fifth without having made salam, thinking it is the first sitting, he returns to sitting as long as he has not prostrated in the fifth, and makes salam, and prostrates for forgetfulness. ... Principle: If the imam forgets, the follower must also prostrate because the imam is the guarantor; and from the follower's forgetfulness, nothing [obligates].
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on Sujud al-Sahw (Prostration of Forgetfulness) from Al-Quduri's matn with a commentary that provides hadith proofs. It begins by listing the causes that necessitate sajdah sahw: leaving out a wajib act like reciting Fatiha, Qunut, Tashahhud, or the Takbirat of Eidain, or the imam reciting aloud in a silent prayer or silently in an aloud prayer. Then it states a key rule: the imam's forgetfulness obligates the follower to prostrate along with him; if the imam neglects to do sajdah sahw, the follower should not do it independently. The commentary supports this with several hadith, including the well-known hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who once prayed incorrectly due to forgetfulness and performed two prostrations after the salam, teaching that such prostrations compensate for both increases and decreases in the prayer. Another hadith from Abdullah ibn Bukaynah illustrates that when the Prophet stood up from the second rak'ah without sitting, he performed sajdah sahw before salam, and the people followed him, proving that the follower must follow the imam's sahw. At the end of the page, an Urdu principle summarizes: if a wajib act or recitation of Fatiha, Qunut, or Eid Takbirat is left, sajdah sahw becomes necessary. The next page continues with a new point (marked 'd'): if the follower forgets, neither the imam nor the follower is obligated to prostrate for it. Then it details scenarios regarding forgetting the first sitting: if the person remembers while closer to sitting, he returns and recites tashahhud; if closer to standing, he does not return and does sajdah sahw. Forgetting the last sitting and standing for a fifth rak'ah: if he has not yet performed sajdah in the fifth, he returns to sitting, cancels the fifth, and does sajdah sahw. If he has performed a sajdah in the fifth, the fard prayer becomes invalid (batil) and converts to nafl, requiring a sixth rak'ah to complete the nafl. Another scenario: if he sits in the fourth for the tashahhud and then stands for the fifth thinking it's the first sitting, he returns to sitting if he hasn't prostrated in the fifth, then makes salam and does sajdah sahw. These rulings establish the precise method to rectify various forgetfulness errors. The hadith proofs for the follower's sahw not obligating the imam include a marfu' hadith from Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) stating that there is no sahw upon those behind the imam; a follower's sahw is covered by the imam. A statement of Hammad also confirms that if the imam forgets, the follower prostrates; if the follower forgets, nothing is upon them. Additional hadith from Mughirah ibn Shu'bah supports the ruling on returning to sitting before fully standing. The final Urdu principle reiterates that the imam's sahw obligates the follower to prostrate because the imam is a guarantor (damin), while the follower's sahw does not affect the imam.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness or error during prayer, either before or after salam depending on the situation.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act in prayer whose omission requires compensation via sajdah sahw, but not repetition of the prayer.
الْمُؤْتَم (al-mu'tam): The follower in congregational prayer who prays behind an imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, which of the following omissions does NOT necessitate sujud al-sahw?
A) Leaving recitation of Fatiha
B) Leaving Qunut in Witr
C) Leaving the final Tashahhud
D) Leaving a sunnah dua in sujud

Key Takeaway
Sajdah sahw is a wajib compensation for omitting a wajib act or committing a jahr/sirr error in prayer; the imam's sahw obligates the follower.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Rectifying Forgetfulness in Sitting: Hanafi Rulings
Matn and hadith on forgetting sitting and fifth rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for forgetting the first and last sitting, and determine when sajdah sahw is required.

Core Idea
Forgetting the first sitting: return if closer to sitting; continue if closer to standing. For the last sitting: return if not yet prostrated in the fifth; otherwise the prayer becomes nafl.

This lesson dives into the detailed scenarios from Al-Quduri's matn regarding forgetfulness in sitting during prayer. The text provides precise criteria based on physical proximity to sitting or standing, and outlines the consequences for the prayer's validity. These rules are essential for correctly applying sajdah sahw.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish first sitting from last sitting
The first sitting occurs after the first two rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer; the last sitting is the final tashahhud. Forgetting each has different rules.
The matn treats them separately.
2
Apply the 'closer to' criterion for the first sitting
If one remembers while closer to sitting (i.e., before fully standing), he returns to sit and recites tashahhud. If closer to standing (after standing upright), he does not return and does sajdah sahw.
Physical proximity is determined by the state of the body during the motion of standing.
3
Analyze the case of forgetting the last sitting and standing for a fifth rak'ah
If one stands for a fifth rak'ah without having done the last sitting, he must return to sitting as long as he has not performed sajdah in the fifth. If he has performed sajdah, the prayer becomes invalid as fard and converts to nafl; he must add a sixth rak'ah.
This scenario specifically deals with the last sitting.
4
Apply the scenario of sitting in the fourth then standing for a fifth thinking it's the first sitting
If one sits for tashahhud in the fourth then stands for a fifth, thinking it is the first sitting, he returns if he has not prostrated in the fifth, then makes salam and does sajdah sahw.
This prevents the invalid addition of a rak'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ سُجُودِ السَّهْو
القدوري مع احاديثه أَوْ تَرَكَ قِرَاءَةَ فَاتِحَةِ الْكِتَابِ وَالْقُنُوتَ أَوْ التَّشَهدَ أَوْ تَكْبِيرَاتِ الْعِيدَيْنِ أَوْ جَهَرَ الْإِمَامُ فِيمَا يُخَافَتُ فِيهِ أَوْ خَافَتَ فِيمَا يُجْهَرُ فِيهِ ؟ وَسَهْوُ الْإِمَامِ يُوجِبُ عَلَى الْمُؤْتَمَ السُّجُودَ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَسْجُدْ الْإِمَامُ لَمْ يَسْجُدُ الْمُؤْتَمُّ.
صَلَّى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ إِبْرَاهِيمُ: زَادَ أَوْ نَقَصَ فَلَمَّا سَلَّمَ قِيلَ لَهُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ! أَحَدَثَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ شَيْءٍ؟ قَالَ "وَمَا ذَاكَ ؟ " قَالُوا: صَلَّيْتَ كَذَا وَكَذَا قَالَ فَتَى رِجْلَيْهِ، وَاسْتَقْبَلَ الْقِبْلَةَ، فَسَجَدَ سَجْدَتَيْنِ، ثُمَّ سَلَّمَ. ثُمَّ أَقْبَلَ عَلَيْنَا بِوَجْهِهِ فَقَالَ إِنَّهُ لَوْ حَدَثَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ شَيْءٌ أَنْبَأْتُكُمْ بِهِ وَلَكِنْ إِنَّمَا أَنَا بَشَرٌ أَنْسَى كَمَا تَنْسَوْنَ. فَإِذَا نَسِيتُ فَذَكَّرُونِي. وَإِذَا شَكَّ أَحَدُكُمْ فِي صَلَاتِهِ فَلْيَتَحَرَّ الصَّوَابَ. فَلْيُتِمَّ عَلَيْهِ ثُمَّ لِيَسْجُدْ سَجْدَتَيْنِ (مسلم شریف، بَاب السَّهْوِ فِي الصَّلَاةِ وَالسُّجُودِ لَه، نمبر 572/سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَنْ قَالَ: يُتِمُّ عَلَى أَكْبَرِ ظَنِّهِ، نمبر 1029).
وجه : (۱)قول التابعى لثبوت سُجُودُ السَّهْوِ فِي الرِّيَادَةِ وَالنُّقْصَانِ بَعْدَ السَّلَامِ\nعَنِ الثَّوْرِيِّ قَالَ: «إِذَا قُمْتَ فِيمَا يُجْلَسُ فِيهِ، أَوْ جَلَسْتَ فِيمَا يُقَامُ فِيهِ، أَوْ جَهَرْتَ فِيمَا يُخَافَتُ فِيهِ، أَوْ خَافَتَّ فِيمَا يُجْهَرُ فِيهِ نَاسِيًا سَجَدْتَ سَجْدَتَي السَّهْوِ (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ إِذَا قَامَ فِيمَا يُقْعَدُ فِيهِ أَوْ قَعَدَ فِيمَا يُقَامُ أَوْ سَلَّمَ فِي مَثْى،نمبر 3495/مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَنْ كَانَ إِذَا جَهَرَ فِيمَا يُخَافَتُ فِيهِ سَجَدَ سَجْدَتَي السَّهْوِ،نمبر 3649).
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت سُجُودُ السَّهْوِ فِي الزِيَادَةِ وَالتَّقْصَانِ بَعْدَ السَّلَامِ\nعَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ أَبِي قَتَادَةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ قَالَ: «كَانَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقْرَأُ فِي الرَّكْعَتَيْنِ مِنَ الظُّهْرِ وَالْعَصْرِ بِفَاتِحَةِ الْكِتَابِ وَسُورَةٍ سُورَةٍ، وَيُسْمِعُنَا الْآيَةَ أَحْيَانًا (بخاري بَابُ الْقِرَاءَةِ فِي الْعَصْر ، نمبر 762/ مسلم شریف ، باب الْقِرَاءَةِ فِي الظُّهْرِ وَالْعَصْرِ ، نمبر 451).
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَسَهْوُ الْإِمَامِ يُوجِبُ عَلَى الْمُؤْتَمَ السُّجُودَ\nعَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ بُكَيْنَةَ الْأَسْدِي حَلِيفِ بَنِي عَبْدِ الْمُطَّلِبِ : «أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَامَ فِي صَلَاةِ الظُّهْرِ وَعَلَيْهِ جُلُوسٌ، فَلَمَّا أَتَمَّ صَلَاتَهُ سَجَدَ سَجْدَتَيْنِ، فَكَبَّرَ فِي كُلِّ سَجْدَةٍ وَهُوَ جَالِسٌ قَبْلَ أَنْ يُسَلَّمَ، وَسَجَدَهُمَا النَّاسُ مَعَهُ، مَكَانَ مَا نَسِيَ مِنَ الْجُلُوسِ» تَابَعَهُ ابْنُ جُرَيْجٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ شِهَابٍ فِي التَّكْبِيرِ (بخاري شريف، بَابُ مَنْ يُكَبِرُ فِي سَجْدَتَي السَّهْوِ، نمبر 1230).
أصول: نماز میں فعل واجب یا فاتحہ یا قنوت یا عیدین ترک ہو گئیں تو سجدہ سہو لازم ہو گا.
د. وَإِنْ سَهَا الْمُؤْتَمُّ لَمْ يَلْزَمُ الإِمَامَ وَلَا الْمُؤْتَمَ السُّجُودُ لَهُ. وَمَنْ سَهَا عَنْ الْقَعْدَةِ الْأُولَى ثُمَّ ذَكَرَ وَهُوَ إِلَى حَالِ الْقُعُودِ أَقْرَبُ عَادَ فَقَعَدَ وَتَشَهَّدَ وَإِنْ كَانَ إِلَى حَالِ الْقِيَامِ أَقْرَبَ لَمْ يُعِدْ وَيَسْجُدُ لِلسَّهْوِ. وَإِنْ سَهَا عَنْ الْقَعْدَةِ الْأَخِيرَةِ فَقَامَ إِلَى الْخَامِسَةِ رَجَعَ إِلَى الْقَعْدَةِ مَا لَمْ يَسْجُدْ وَأَلْغَى الْخَامِسَةَ وَيَسْجُدُ لِلسَّهْوِ. وَإِنْ قَيَّدَ الْخَامِسَةَ بِسَجْدَةٍ بَطَلَ فَرْضُهُ وَتَحَوَّلَتْ صَلَاتُهُ نَفْلًا وَكَانَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَضُمَّ إِلَيْهَا رَكْعَةً سَادِسَةً. وَإِنْ قَعَدَ فِي الرَّابِعَةِ قَدْرَ التَّشَهُدِ ثُمَّ قَامَ إِلَى الْخَامِسَةِ وَلَمْ يُسَلَّمْ يَظُنُّهَا الْقَعْدَةَ الْأُولَى عَادَ إِلَى الْقُعُودِ مَا لَمْ يَسْجُدْ فِي الْخَامِسَةِ وَيُسَلِّمُ وَيَسْجُدُ لِلسَّهو.
د. وجه (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ سَهَا الْمُؤْتَمُّ لَمْ يَلْزَمُ الإِمَامَ\nعَنْ عُمَرَ ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لَيْسَ عَلَى مَنْ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ سَهْوٌ ، فَإِنْ سَهَا الْإِمَامُ فَعَلَيْهِ وَعَلَى مَنْ خَلْفَهُ السَّهْوُ ، وَإِنْ سَهَا مَنْ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ فَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ سَهْوٌ وَالْإِمَامُ كَافِيهِ (سنن دارقطنی، بَابُ: لَيْسَ عَلَى الْمُقْتَدِي سَهْوَ وَعَلَيْهِ سَهْوَ الْإِمَامِ ، نمبر 1413).
وجه : (۲)قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ سَهَا الْمُؤْتَمُّ لَمْ يَلْزَمُ الإِمَامَ\nعَنْ حَمَّادٍ قَالَ: «إِذَا سَهَا الْإِمَامُ سَجَدَ مَنْ خَلْفَهُ، وَإِذَا سَهَا مَنْ خَلْفَهُ فَلَيْسَ عَلَيْهِمْ حَتَّى لا يَضُرُّهُمْ سَهْوٌ مَعَ الْإِمَامِ (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ هَلْ عَلَى مَنْ خَلْفَ الْإِمَامِ سَهْوٌ ، نمبر 3509).
د وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت الرجوع إلى القعود إذا لم يستو قائما\nعَنِ الْمُغِيرَةِ بْن شُعْبَةَ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إِذَا قَامَ الْإِمَامُ فِي الرَّكْعَتَيْنِ، فَإِنْ ذَكَرَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَسْتَوِيَ قَائِمًا فَلْيَجْلِسْ، فَإِنِ اسْتَوَى قَائِمًا فَلَا يَجْلِسْ، وَيَسْجُدْ سَجْدَتَيِ السَّهْوِ (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَنْ نَسِيَ أَنْ يَتَشَهَّدَ وَهُوَ جالس،نمبر 1036/سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي سَجْدَتَي السَّهْوِ قَبْلَ السَّلَامِ، نمبر 391).
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت حكم من صلى خمسا ولم يجلس في الرابعة\nعَنْ حَمَّادٍ قَالَ: «إِذَا صَلَّى الرَّجُلُ خَمْسًا وَلَمْ يَجْلِسْ فِي الرَّابِعَةِ، فَإِنَّهُ يَزِيدُ السَّادِسَةَ، ثُمَّ يُسَلِّمُ ثُمَّ يَسْتَأْنِفُ صَلَاتَهُ (مصنف عبد الرازاق، بَابُ الرَّجُلِ يُصَلِّي الظُّهْرَ أَوِ الْعَصْرِ خَمْسًا، نمبر 3461).
أصول: امام سے سہو ہو اتو مقتدی پر بھی سجدہ لازم ہو گا کیونکہ امام ضامن ہے ، اور مقتدی کے سہو سے کچھ نہیں
Chapter on Prostration of Forgetfulness. Al-Quduri with his hadith: Or he left recitation of Fatiha, Qunut, Tashahhud, or Takbirat of the two Eids, or the imam recited aloud where it is silent, or silently where it is aloud. And the imam's forgetfulness obligates the follower to prostrate; if the imam does not prostrate, the follower does not prostrate. ... [After hadith proofs] And if the follower forgets, it does not obligate the imam nor the follower to prostrate for it. Whoever forgets the first sitting then remembers while he is closer to sitting, he returns and sits and recites tashahhud; if he is closer to standing, he does not return and prostrates for forgetfulness. Whoever forgets the last sitting and stands for a fifth, he returns to sitting as long as he has not prostrated, and cancels the fifth and prostrates for forgetfulness. If he ties the fifth with a prostration, his obligatory prayer becomes invalid and his prayer becomes voluntary, and he must add a sixth rak'ah. If he sits in the fourth to the extent of tashahhud then stands for the fifth without having made salam, thinking it is the first sitting, he returns to sitting as long as he has not prostrated in the fifth, and makes salam, and prostrates for forgetfulness. ... Principle: If the imam forgets, the follower must also prostrate because the imam is the guarantor; and from the follower's forgetfulness, nothing [obligates].
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on Sujud al-Sahw (Prostration of Forgetfulness) from Al-Quduri's matn with a commentary that provides hadith proofs. It begins by listing the causes that necessitate sajdah sahw: leaving out a wajib act like reciting Fatiha, Qunut, Tashahhud, or the Takbirat of Eidain, or the imam reciting aloud in a silent prayer or silently in an aloud prayer. Then it states a key rule: the imam's forgetfulness obligates the follower to prostrate along with him; if the imam neglects to do sajdah sahw, the follower should not do it independently. The commentary supports this with several hadith, including the well-known hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who once prayed incorrectly due to forgetfulness and performed two prostrations after the salam, teaching that such prostrations compensate for both increases and decreases in the prayer. Another hadith from Abdullah ibn Bukaynah illustrates that when the Prophet stood up from the second rak'ah without sitting, he performed sajdah sahw before salam, and the people followed him, proving that the follower must follow the imam's sahw. At the end of the page, an Urdu principle summarizes: if a wajib act or recitation of Fatiha, Qunut, or Eid Takbirat is left, sajdah sahw becomes necessary. The next page continues with a new point (marked 'd'): if the follower forgets, neither the imam nor the follower is obligated to prostrate for it. Then it details scenarios regarding forgetting the first sitting: if the person remembers while closer to sitting, he returns and recites tashahhud; if closer to standing, he does not return and does sajdah sahw. Forgetting the last sitting and standing for a fifth rak'ah: if he has not yet performed sajdah in the fifth, he returns to sitting, cancels the fifth, and does sajdah sahw. If he has performed a sajdah in the fifth, the fard prayer becomes invalid (batil) and converts to nafl, requiring a sixth rak'ah to complete the nafl. Another scenario: if he sits in the fourth for the tashahhud and then stands for the fifth thinking it's the first sitting, he returns to sitting if he hasn't prostrated in the fifth, then makes salam and does sajdah sahw. These rulings establish the precise method to rectify various forgetfulness errors. The hadith proofs for the follower's sahw not obligating the imam include a marfu' hadith from Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) stating that there is no sahw upon those behind the imam; a follower's sahw is covered by the imam. A statement of Hammad also confirms that if the imam forgets, the follower prostrates; if the follower forgets, nothing is upon them. Additional hadith from Mughirah ibn Shu'bah supports the ruling on returning to sitting before fully standing. The final Urdu principle reiterates that the imam's sahw obligates the follower to prostrate because the imam is a guarantor (damin), while the follower's sahw does not affect the imam.

Key Terms
الْقَعْدَةُ الْأُولَى (al-qa'dah al-ula): The first sitting in prayer after the first two rak'ahs in a prayer of three or four rak'ahs.
الْقَعْدَةُ الْأَخِيرَةُ (al-qa'dah al-akhirah): The final sitting in prayer for the concluding tashahhud.
نَفْل (nafl): Voluntary prayer. In the context of forgetting, a fard prayer that becomes nafl due to an error in rak'ah count.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person forgets the last sitting and stands for a fifth rak'ah. He performs sajdah in that fifth rak'ah. What is the ruling?
A) He returns to sitting and does sajdah sahw.
B) His fard prayer becomes invalid and converts to nafl; he must add a sixth rak'ah.
C) He continues the fifth rak'ah and then does sajdah sahw.
D) He stops the prayer and restarts.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rules for forgetting sitting are precise: return if closer to sitting for the first, and for the last, return only before sajdah in the fifth; after sajdah, the prayer converts to nafl.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Sujud al-Sahw: Extra Rak'ah and Doubt in Rak'ah Count
Rulings on adding an extra rak'ah and on doubt in rak'ah count with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on adding a fifth rak'ah and on doubt in rak'ah count, apply the appropriate remedy (add sixth rak'ah, repeat prayer, or rely on dominant assumption), and explain the hadith proofs.

Core Idea
If you add a fifth rak'ah, add a sixth; if you doubt the count, repeat if first time else rely on dominant assumption.

This passage from al-Quduri's matn addresses two common forgetfulness scenarios in prayer: mistakenly performing an extra rak'ah, and uncertainty about the number of rak'ahs performed. The Hanafi school provides clear remedies that preserve the validity of the prayer while requiring prostration of forgetfulness. The rulings are supported by prophetic hadith and companion traditions, and there are important intra-Hanafi and cross-madhhab differences to note.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the first paragraph of the Arabic text. There are two distinct rulings: (1) what to do if one performs a fifth rak'ah, and (2) what to do if one doubts the number of rak'ahs (three or four). Note the conditions for each.
The first ruling applies when the fifth rak'ah is completed with a prostration (sajdah).
2
Locate the proofs (dalil)
The text cites multiple proofs: a statement of Qatada (tabi'i), a hadith from Ibn Mas'ud (marfu'), and a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri (marfu'). Identify each and note that they are ahad hadith (zanni al-thubut).
The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud shows the Prophet added sujud al-sahw after being informed he prayed five.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For the extra rak'ah ruling, the Prophet's action (fi'l) of prostrating after being told indicates the prayer remained valid and required sahw. In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action in an explanatory context indicates wujub. For doubt, the hadith commands to 'throw away doubt and build on certainty' – this is the basis for repeating when first-time doubt occurs.
The Hanafi principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub, but here it's fi'l al-nabi which is also evidence of wujub under certain conditions.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The Urdu marginal note clarifies a critical ikhtilaf: if one forgets the last sitting and prostrates the fifth rak'ah, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold the fard is batil (void), while Imam Muhammad says it is valid with sahw. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is the invalidating view.
This difference stems from whether the last sitting (qa'dah akhirah) is considered a rukn (pillar) or a wajib. It is a rukn, so omitting it invalidates the prayer.
5
Apply the rulings to scenarios
Now synthesise: For an extra rak'ah, add a sixth to make the two nafl, then perform sujud al-sahw. For doubt: first occurrence → repeat entire prayer; frequent → build on dominant assumption; if no dominant assumption, build on certainty (the smaller number). Perform sujud al-sahw in all cases.
The principle for frequent doubt is based on ease and prevention of waswasa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ سُجُودِ السَّهْو
فَإِنْ قَيَّدَ الْخَامِسَةَ بِسَجْدَةٍ ضَمَّ إلَيْهَا رَكْعَةً أُخْرَى وَقَدْ تَمَّتْ صَلَاتُهُ وَيَسْجُدُ لِلسَّهْوِ وَالرَّكْعَتَانِ لَهُ نَافِلَةٌ
وَمَنْ شَكَ فِي صَلَاتِهِ فَلَمْ يَدْرِ أَثَلَاثًا صَلَّى أَمْ أَرْبَعًا وَكَانَ ذَلِكَ أَوَّلَ مَا عَرَضَ لَهُ اسْتَأْنَفَ الصَّلَاةَ وَإِنْ كَانَ الشَّكُ يَعْرِضُ لَهُ كَثِيرًا بَنَى عَلَى غَالِبِ ظَنِّهِ
وَجْهٌ (١) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِنْ سَهَا الْمُؤْتَمُّ لَمْ يَلْزَمُ الْإِمَامَ عَنْ قَتَادَةَ فِي رَجُلٍ صَلَّى الظُّهْرَ خَمْسًا قَالَ: «يَزِيدُ إِلَيْهَا رَكْعَةً فَتَكُونُ صَلَاةَ الظُّهْرِ وَرَكَعَتَيْنِ بَعْدَهَا، وَإِذَا صَلَّى الصُّبْحَ ثَلَاثًا صَلَّى إِلَيْهَا رَابِعَةً فَتَكُونُ رَكْعَتَانِ تَطَوُّعًا، وَسَجَدَ سَجْدَتَيْنِ وَهُوَ جَالِسٌ»
وَجْهٌ (٢) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِنْ سَهَا الْمُؤْتَمُّ لَمْ يَلْزَمُ الْإِمَامَ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ قَالَ: صَلَّى بِنَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم خَمْسًا فَقُلْنَا: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ! أَزِيدَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ؟ قَالَ: «وَمَا ذَاكَ؟» قَالُوا: صَلَّيْتَ خَمْسًا. قَالَ: «إِنَّمَا أَنَا بَشَرٌ مِثْلُكُمْ أَذْكُرُ كَمَا تَذْكُرُونَ وَأَنْسَى كَمَا تَنْسَوْنَ» ثُمَّ سَجَدَ سَجْدَتَيِ السَّهْوِ
وَجْهٌ (١) لِثُبُوتِ وَإِنْ سَهَا الْمُؤْتَمُّ لَمْ يَلْزَمُ الْإِمَامَ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ فِي الَّذِي لَا يَدْرِي ثَلَاثًا صَلَّى أَوْ أَرْبَعًا قَالَ: «يُعِيدُ حَتَّى يَحْفَظَ»
وَجْهٌ (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِنْ سَهَا الْمُؤْتَمُّ لَمْ يَلْزَمُ الْإِمَامَ عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «إِذَا شَكَّ أَحَدُكُمْ فِي صَلَاتِهِ فَلَمْ يَدْرِ كَمْ صَلَّى؟ ثَلَاثًا أَمْ أَرْبَعًا فَلْيَطْرَحِ الشَّكَّ وَلْيَبْنِ عَلَى مَا اسْتَيْقَنَ ثُمَّ يَسْجُدُ سَجْدَتَيْنِ قَبْلَ أَنْ يُسَلِّمَ»
أَصْلٌ: إِذَا سَهَا فِي الْقَعْدَةِ الْأَخِيرَةِ وَسَجَدَ سَجْدَةَ الْخَامِسَةِ فَالْفَرْضُ بَاطِلٌ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ لِأَنَّ الْقَعْدَةَ الْأَخِيرَةَ فَرْضٌ تَرَكَهَا.
وَأَمَّا عَلَى الصَّفْحَةِ التَّالِيَةِ: إِنْ كَانَ لَهُ ظَنٌّ بَنَى عَلَيْهِ، وَإِلَّا بَنَى عَلَى الْيَقِينِ. وَإِذَا شَكَّ أَحَدُكُمْ فَلْيَتَحَرَّ الصَّوَابَ ثُمَّ لِيَسْجُدْ سَجْدَتَيْنِ.
أَصْلٌ: مَنْ شَكَّ فِي صَلَاتِهِ فَإِنْ كَانَ أَوَّلَ مَا عَرَضَ لَهُ اسْتَأْنَفَ، وَإِلَّا بَنَى عَلَى غَالِبِ ظَنِّهِ.
أَصْلٌ: إِذَا سَجَدَ الْخَامِسَةَ فَمِنَ السُّنَّةِ أَنْ يَضُمَّ إِلَيْهَا سَادِسَةً لِتَكُونَ نَافِلَةً.
Chapter of Prostration of Forgetfulness. If he ties the fifth with a prostration, he adds another rak'ah to it, and his prayer is complete, and he prostrates for forgetfulness, and the two rak'ahs are supererogatory for him. Whoever doubts in his prayer and does not know whether he prayed three or four, and that happens for the first time, he restarts the prayer. If doubt occurs to him frequently, he builds on his dominant assumption. Proof (1): Statement of the follower for establishing... from Qatada... Proof (2): The hadith for establishing... from Abdullah... Proof (1): for establishing... from Ibn Umar... Proof (1): The hadith for establishing... from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri... Principle: If he forgets in the last sitting and prostrates the fifth, the obligatory prayer is invalid according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf because the last sitting is an obligation that he left. As for the next page: If he has an assumption he builds on it, otherwise he builds on certainty. When one of you doubts, let him seek the correct then prostrate two prostrations. Principle: Whoever doubts in his prayer, if it is the first time he experiences it, he restarts; otherwise he builds on his dominant assumption. Principle: When he prostrates the fifth, it is sunnah to add a sixth to it to make it supererogatory.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's matn covers two major rulings regarding sahw (forgetfulness) in prayer: the addition of an extra rak'ah, and doubt about the number of rak'ahs prayed. The author then provides hadith proofs and additional principles. The first ruling: if someone mistakenly performs a fifth rak'ah (in a four-rak'ah prayer), he should add a sixth rak'ah so that the two extra rak'ahs become nafl (supererogatory), and his original fard prayer is valid. He must also perform the prostrations of forgetfulness (sujud al-sahw). The hadith from Qatada (a tabi'i) and from Ibn Mas'ud (marfu') support this. The second ruling: if a person doubts whether he prayed three or four rak'ahs, and this is the first time such doubt occurs, he must repeat the entire prayer from the beginning. However, if he is frequently plagued by doubts (waswasa), he should act upon his dominant assumption (ghalib al-dhann). If he has no dominant assumption, he builds on certainty (yaqin), i.e., the fewer number. The hadith from Ibn Umar (mawquf) and Abu Sa'id al-Khudri (marfu') are cited as proofs. Additionally, an Urdu marginal note clarifies an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: if the forgetfulness occurs in the last sitting (qa'dah akhirah) and one performs the prostration of a fifth rak'ah, the fard prayer becomes invalid according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, because the last sitting is a fard (obligatory) pillar that was omitted. However, Imam Muhammad may differ. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to later Hanafi scholars is that the prayer is invalid and must be repeated. The note also reiterates the sunnah of adding a sixth rak'ah to make the extra ones nafl.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for errors in prayer such as addition, omission, or doubt.
الشك (al-shakk): Doubt about the number of rak'ahs performed in prayer, requiring recourse to certainty or dominant assumption.
الظن الغالب (al-dhann al-ghalib): Dominant assumption or preponderant belief about the number of rak'ahs, used in case of frequent doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person mistakenly prays five rak'ahs in Zuhr, what should he do?
A) Repeat the prayer from the beginning
B) Add a sixth rak'ah and perform sujud al-sahw
C) Perform sujud al-sahw only
D) Continue as is without any action

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides clear remedies for forgetfulness in prayer: add a sixth rak'ah for an extra fifth, repeat for first-time doubt, and rely on dominant assumption for frequent doubt—always followed by sujud al-sahw.

Ruling on Making Up Prayers Missed Due to Unconsciousness
Ruling with proof from Companion's action

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up prayers missed due to unconsciousness and identify the threshold of five prayers, citing the proof from the action of Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
Five or fewer prayers missed due to unconsciousness are made up; more than five are not required.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on qada' (make-up) for prayers missed during unconsciousness. Imam al-Quduri's matn provides a clear threshold: five prayers or less are wajib to make up, while more than five are not. We will explore the proof from the action of the Companion Ibn Umar and the underlying usul principle that distinguishes the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making up prayers missed during a period of unconsciousness. The ruling distinguishes based on the number: five or fewer prayers must be made up (wajib) when the person recovers; if more than five are missed, no make-up is required.
The threshold of five corresponds to the five daily prayers.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the practice of Abdullah ibn Umar, who is reported to have been unconscious for a day and a night (five prayer times) and also for a month, and in both cases he did not make up the missed prayers.
The source references Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Hanafi jurists derive from Ibn Umar's action that the obligation to make up prayers is limited. Since he did not make up after a day and night (five prayers), it indicates that for a duration of five prayers or less, make-up is required (by other evidence), but for longer durations, it is not obligatory.
The hadith is zanni in both transmission (thubut) and meaning (dalala).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa's principle is that the ruling is based on the habitual state of the person (what normally occurs), while the Sahibayn require actual occurrence. This affects borderline cases where the exact duration of unconsciousness is uncertain.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) follows the matn's categorical distinction.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, count the number of fard prayers missed during unconsciousness. If the count is five or less, make them up. If the count is six or more, no make-up is required, even if the unconsciousness lasts weeks or months.
The ruling applies to both fard and wajib prayers; nafl prayers are not made up.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ صَلَاةِ الْمَرِيضِ وَمَنْ أُغْمِيَ عَلَيْهِ خَمْسَ صَلَوَاتٍ فَمَا دُونَهَا قَضَاهَا إِذَا صَحَ وَإِنْ فَاتَهُ بِالْإِغْمَاءِ أَكْثَرَ مِنْ ذَلِكَ لَمْ يَقْضِ ه: (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ صَلَّى قَاعِدًا يَرْكَعُ وَيَسْجُدُ لِمَرَضِ بِهِ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ، عَنْ نَافِع قَالَ: «أُغْمِيَ عَلَى ابْنِ عُمَرَ يَوْمًا وَلَيْلَةً فَلَمْ يَقْضِ مَا فَاتَهُ، «أَنَّ ابْنَ عُمَرَ أُغْمِيَ عَلَيْهِ شَهْرًا فَلَمْ يَقْضِ مَا فَاتَهُ، وَصَلَّى يَوْمَهُ الَّذِي أَفَاقَ فِيهِ،(مصنف عبدالرزاق بَابُ صَلَاةِ الْمَرِيضِ عَلَى الدَّابَّةِ، وَصَلَاةِ الْمُغْمَى عَلَيْهِ ، نمبر 4153/4152/مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَا يُعِيدُ الْمُغْمَى عَلَيْهِ مِنَ الصَّلَاةِ، نمبر 6585) اصول : اگر کوئی چیز عام طور پر ہوتی رہتی ہو تو گویا ہر وقت کا وہی حکم ہے جو اکثر حالت ہے، اور صاحبین کی اصول یہ ہے کہ جب تک وہ چیز متحقق نہ ہو جائے تو تب تک اس کا اعتبار نہیں۔
Chapter on the prayer of the sick and one who becomes unconscious. If five prayers or less are missed, he makes them up when he recovers. If more than that are missed due to unconsciousness, he does not make them up. h: (1) The statement of a Companion as proof. And whoever prays sitting, he bows and prostrates due to illness. From Abdullah ibn Umar, from Nafi' who said: 'Ibn Umar became unconscious for a day and a night and did not make up what he missed.' ... 'Ibn Umar became unconscious for a month and did not make up what he missed, and he prayed on the day he regained consciousness.' (Sources). Principle: If something habitually occurs, then its ruling is based on the common state; and the principle of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that until that thing is actualized, it is not considered.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling (hukm) from Imam al-Quduri's matn on the prayer of a sick or unconscious person. The Hanafi ruling distinguishes between short and long duration of unconsciousness: if five or fewer prayers are missed, they must be made up (wajib); if more than five are missed, they are not made up (i.e., no obligation). The proof (dalil) is the action of Ibn Umar, who did not make up prayers after being unconscious for a day and a night (which equates to five prayers) or even for a month. This indicates that the obligation to make up prayers is limited to a small number. The principle (usul) added by the commentator explains the underlying legal maxim: when a condition (like consciousness) is habitual, the ruling is based on that habitual state (Imam Abu Hanifa's view), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require the actual occurrence of the condition for its consideration. This nuance affects borderline cases but does not change the core ruling presented here.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed prayer after its time has passed.
إغماء (ighma'): Unconsciousness that prevents awareness and prayer.
أصول (usul): Legal principle or maxim underlying the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, how many prayers missed due to unconsciousness must be made up?
A) All missed prayers regardless of number
B) Five or fewer prayers must be made up; more is not required
C) None, unconsciousness cancels all prayer obligations
D) Only the prayer at the time of regaining consciousness

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab limits qada' for unconsciousness to five or fewer prayers, based on the precedent of Ibn Umar.

Sajdahs of Recitation: Number, Obligation, and Proofs
States the number of sajdah tilawah and its obligation upon reciter and listener.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sujud al-tilawah (14 sajdahs, wajib upon reciter and listener) and identify the key proofs from the Sunnah that establish this ruling.

Core Idea
Sujud al-tilawah is wajib on the reciter and listener for 14 specific verses.

This passage opens the chapter on sujud al-tilawah in al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. It presents the core Hanafi ruling: there are fourteen places of prostration in the Quran, and performing the prostration is wajib (obligatory) upon both the person reciting (tali) and the person hearing (sami'). This ruling places the Hanafi school in contrast with the Shafi'i school, which regards it as sunnah. To demonstrate the strength of the position, the commentator (sharih) adduces multiple hadiths from the Prophet ﷺ and actions of the Companions as evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the opening line: 'The prostrations of recitation in the Quran are fourteen sajdahs… And the prostration is obligatory in these places upon the reciter and the listener.' This is the central fatwa (mufta bihi) of the Hanafi school.
Memorize the number 14 and the inclusion of both reciter and listener.
2
Note the Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Recall that the Shafi'i school classifies sujud al-tilawah as sunnah (recommended), not wajib. This difference means that the Hanafi position requires stronger evidence to override the default permissibility.
The passage’s multiple proofs are specifically marshalled to establish wujub (obligation).
3
Analyse the Primary Dalil
The hadith of 'Uqbah ibn Amir (Sunan Abi Dawud) contains the Prophet’s explicit statement: 'Are there two sajdahs in Surah al-Hajj?' He said: 'Yes, and whoever does not prostrate them, let him not recite them.' The imperative structure indicates obligation (al-amr yufidu al-wujub in Hanafi usul).
This hadith also confirms that Surah al-Hajj contains two sajdahs, justifying the count of 14.
4
Examine the Supporting Proofs
The commentator provides additional evidence: (a) Ibn 'Umar narrating the Prophet’s consistent practice of prostrating while reciting (Bukhari, Muslim); (b) Ibn 'Abbas stating that Sād is not from the 'determined' prostrations yet the Prophet prostrated (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) – implying that even if not part of the 14, it is still practised; (c) the Companion statement that the sajdah is upon the one who hears it (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah); (d) the action of 'Umar prostrating on the pulpit while reciting Surah al-Nahl.
These remove any doubt that the ruling applies to listeners and that the Prophet’s practice was consistent.
5
Understand the Hanafi Istidlal (Legal Reasoning)
Each hadith is cited to prove a specific part of the ruling: the count (14), the wujub (obligation), and the inclusion of the listener. The Hanafi method uses the principle that a command (amr) from the Prophet indicates obligation unless there is a contrary indicator (qarinah). Here, no such indicator exists, so the ruling is wajib.
This is a classic example of applying usul al-fiqh to derive a ruling from ahad hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ سُجُودِ التَّلَاوَةِ بَابُ سُجُودِ التَّلَاوَةِ ا سُجُودُ التَّلَاوَةِ فِي الْقُرْآنِ أَرْبَعَ عَشْرَةَ سَجْدَةً إِلَى آخِرِهِ ص لَا يَسْأَمُونَ لَ وَالسُّجُودُ وَاجِبٌ فِي هَذِهِ الْمَوَاضِعِ عَلَى التَّالِي وَالسَّامِعِ وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت سُجُودُ التَّلَاوَةِ فِي الْقُرْآنِ أَرْبَعَ عَشْرَةَ سَجْدَةً \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: فِي سُورَةِ الْحَجَ الْأُولَى عَزِيمَةٌ وَالْآخِرَةُ تَعْلِيمٌ، وَكَانَ لَا يَسْجُدُ فِيهَا،(مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ كَمْ فِي الْقُرْآنِ مِنْ سَجْدَةٍ، نمبر 5892) وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت سُجُودُ التَّلَاوَةِ فِي الْقُرْآنِ أَرْبَعَ عَشْرَةَ سَجْدَةً \ أَنَّ عُقْبَةَ بْنَ عَامِرٍ حَدَّثَهُ، قَالَ: قُلْتُ لِرَسُولِ اللَّهِ : أَفِي سُورَةِ الْحَجَ سَجْدَتَانِ؟ قَالَ: «نَعَمْ، وَمَنْ لَمْ يَسْجُدُهُمَا، فَلَا يَقْرَأَهُمَا، سنن ابوداود، بَابُ تَفْرِيع أَبْوَابِ السُّجُودِ، وَكَمْ سَجْدَةً فِي الْقُرْآنِ، نمبر 1402/) ل وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَالسُّجُودُ وَاجِبٌ فِي هَذِهِ الْمَوَاضِعِ عَلَى التَّالِي \ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسِ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: «{ص} لَيْسَ مِنْ عَزَائِمِ السُّجُودِ، وَقَدْ رَأَيْتُ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَسْجُدُ فِيهَا، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ سَجْدَةِ ص نمبر 1069/سنن ابوداود بَابُ السُّجُودِ في ص،نمبر1409/سنن ترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي السَّجْدَةِ في ص نمبر 577) وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَالسُّجُودُ وَاجِبٌ فِي هَذِهِ الْمَوَاضِع عَلَى التَّالِي \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ قَالَ: «كَانَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقْرَأُ السَّجْدَةَ وَنَحْنُ عِنْدَهُ، فَيَسْجُدُ وَنَسْجُدُ مَعَهُ، فَنَزْدَحِمُ، حَتَّى مَا يَجِدُ أَحَدُنَا جبْهَتِهِ مَوْضِعًا يَسْجُدُ عَلَيْهِ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ ازْدِحَامِ النَّاسِ إِذَا قَرَأَ الْإِمَامُ السَّجْدَةَ، نمبر 1076/ مسلم شریف، بَابُ سُجُودِ التَّلَاوَةِ، نمبر 575) وجه (۳) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَالسُّجُودُ وَاجِبٌ فِي هَذِهِ الْمَوَاضِعِ عَلَى التَّالِي \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ قَالَ: «إِنَّمَا السَّجْدَةُ عَلَى مَنْ سَمِعَهَا ، مصنف ابن ابي شيبه مَنْ قَالَ السَّجْدَةُ عَلَى مَنْ جَلَسَ لَهَا وَمَنْ سَمِعَهَا ، نمبر 4225) وجه : (۴) الحديث لثبوت وَالسُّجُودُ وَاجِبٌ فِي هَذِهِ الْمَوَاضِع عَلَى التَّالِي \ عُمَرَ بْنِ الْخَطَّابِ : «قَرَأَ يَوْمَ الْجُمُعَةِ عَلَى الْمِنْبَرِ بِسُورَةِ النَّحْلِ، حَتَّى إِذَا جَاءَ السَّجْدَةَ نَزَلَ فَسَجَدَ، وَسَجَدَ اصول : قرآن کریم میں چودہ مقامات ایسے ہیں جن کو پڑھنے یا سننے سے سجدہ واجب ہو جاتا ہے۔
Chapter on the prostration of recitation. Chapter on the prostration of recitation. The prostrations of recitation in the Quran are fourteen sajdahs up to its end. [Stray text: 'ص لَا يَسْأَمُونَ لَ'] And the prostration is obligatory in these places upon the reciter and the listener. Evidence (1): The hadith to establish the prostration of recitation in the Quran are fourteen sajdahs: from Ibn Abbas who said: 'In Surah al-Hajj, the first is a determined prostration and the latter is instruction, and he would not prostrate in it.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq). Evidence (2): The hadith to establish the prostration of recitation in the Quran are fourteen sajdahs: that Uqbah ibn Amir narrated: I said to the Messenger of Allah: 'Are there two sajdahs in Surah al-Hajj?' He said: 'Yes, and whoever does not prostrate them, let him not recite them.' (Sunan Abi Dawud). [Stray mark] Evidence (1) to establish that the prostration is obligatory in these places upon the reciter: from Ibn Abbas may Allah be pleased with them both who said: 'Sad is not from the determined prostrations, and I saw the Prophet prostrate in it.' (Bukhari, etc.). Evidence (2) to establish that the prostration is obligatory in these places upon the reciter: from Ibn Umar who said: 'The Prophet would recite a sajdah while we were with him, and he would prostrate and we would prostrate with him, until one of us could not find a place for his forehead to prostrate upon.' (Bukhari, Muslim). Evidence (3) The statement of a Companion to establish that the prostration is obligatory in these places upon the reciter: from Ibn Umar who said: 'The sajdah is only upon the one who hears it.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). Evidence (4) The hadith to establish that the prostration is obligatory in these places upon the reciter: Umar ibn al-Khattab recited on Friday on the pulpit Surah al-Nahl, and when he came to the sajdah, he descended and prostrated, and [others] prostrated. Principle: There are fourteen places in the Quran for which prostration becomes obligatory upon reciting or hearing.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the chapter on Sujud al-Tilawah (prostration of recitation) from al-Quduri's matn with its proofs. The ruling (hukm) states that there are fourteen sajdahs in the Quran, and the prostration is wajib (obligatory) upon both the reciter (tali) and the listener (sami'). This is the Hanafi position, distinguishing it from other schools that may consider it sunnah. The commentator provides multiple proofs (wujuh) to support each part of the ruling: (1) hadith from Ibn Abbas indicating that Surah Sad is not from the determined prostrations, yet the Prophet prostrated, showing it is still recommended (but Hanafis count it as one of the fourteen? Actually the text says 'إِلَى آخِرِهِ' meaning 'up to its end' and mentions Sad; there is nuance). (2) The hadith of Uqbah ibn Amir confirms two sajdahs in Surah al-Hajj, so the Hanafi count of 14 includes both. (3) Hadith of Ibn Umar shows the Prophet's practice of prostrating during recitation. (4) The statement of Ibn Umar that the obligation is on the one who hears, indicating it is wajib on the listener as well. (5) The action of Umar ibn al-Khattab prostrating on the pulpit while reciting. The Urdu principle summarizes that there are fourteen places in the Quran where prostration becomes wajib upon reciting or hearing.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing specific verses of the Quran.
تالي (tali): The person who recites the verse of prostration.
سامع (sami'): The person who hears the recitation of a prostration verse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the number of sajdahs of recitation in the Quran and their legal status?
A) 11 sajdahs, sunnah
B) 14 sajdahs, wajib upon the reciter and listener
C) 14 sajdahs, wajib only on the reciter
D) 15 sajdahs, sunnah upon both

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school considers sujud al-tilawah as wajib on both the reciter and listener for exactly 14 Quranic verses, supported by explicit prophetic commands and consistent practice.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Sujud al-Tilawah: Rulings for Imam and Ma'mum
Matn with proofs on sujud al-tilawah in congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on sujud al-tilawah when the imam recites, when the ma'mum recites, and when hearing from someone outside prayer, and explain the principle that an incomplete prostration does not suffice.

Core Idea
The imam's recitation obligates prostration for both; the ma'mum's does not; hearing from outside requires post-prayer prostration.

Sujud al-tilawah is a wajib act upon reciting or hearing a prostration verse. This lesson focuses on the rulings that arise in congregational prayer: what happens when the imam recites, when the ma'mum recites, and when someone hears the verse from a person not in their prayer. We will explore the proofs from the Sunnah and the principle that an incomplete prostration cannot replace a complete one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read each conditional sentence in the matn: 'when the imam recites', 'if the ma'mum recites', 'if they hear from someone not in prayer'. Isolate the specific situation.
Each scenario has a distinct ruling.
2
State the ruling
For each scenario, extract the explicit ruling from the matn: the imam and follower prostrate; the follower's recitation does not oblige the imam; hearing from outside requires prostration after prayer, not during.
Pay attention to the Arabic verbs: سَجَدَهَا, لَمْ يَلْزَمُ, لَمْ يَسْجُدُوهَا.
3
Locate the proof
Find the hadith or athar cited as wajh for each ruling. For the imam prostrating, it is the hadith of Ibn 'Umar. For hearing from outside, the athar of Tawus.
The proofs are given after the matn in the commentary.
4
Apply the principle of mutaba'ah
Understand why the imam's recitation obligates the follower: because of following (mutaba'ah). Conversely, the follower's recitation does not obligate the imam because the imam is not following the follower.
This principle is explained in the Urdu commentary.
5
Distinguish complete vs incomplete prostration
If the congregation prostrates in prayer for a verse heard from outside, it is incomplete and must be repeated after prayer. This is a key distinction: the intention matters.
The Urdu commentary states: 'ناقص سے کامل سجدہ ادا نہیں ہوتا'.
