بَابُ سُجُودِ التِّلَاوَةِ وَإِذَا تَلَا الْإِمَامُ آيَةَ سَجْدَةٍ سَجَدَهَا وَسَجَدَ الْمَأْمُومُ مَعَهُ ، وَإِنْ تَلَا الْمَأْمُومُ لَمْ يَلْزَمُ الْإِمَامَ وَلَا الْمُؤْتَمَ السُّجُودُ وَإِنْ سَمِعُوا وَهُمْ فِي الصَّلَاةِ آيَةَ سَجْدَةٍ مِنْ رَجُلٍ لَيْسَ مَعَهُمْ فِي الصَّلَاةِ لَمْ يَسْجُدُوهَا فِي الصَّلَاةِ وَسَجَدُوهَا بَعْدَ الصَّلَاةِ فَإِنْ سَجَدُوهَا فِي الصَّلَاةِ لَمْ تُجْزِهِمْ وَلَمْ تُفْسِدْ عَلَيْهِمْ الصَّلَاةِ وَمَنْ تَلَا آيَةَ سَجْدَةٍ فَلَمْ يَسْجُدْهَا حَتَّى دَخَلَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ فَتَلَاهَا وَسَجَدَ أَجْزَأَتْهُ السَّجْدَةُ عَنْ التَّلَاوَتَيْنِ وَإِنْ تَلَاهَا فِي غَيْرِ الصَّلَاةِ فَسَجَدَ لَهَا ثُمَّ دَخَلَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ فَتَلَاهَا سَجَدَ لَهَا وَلَمْ تُجْزِتُهُ السَّجْدَةُ الْأُولَى . وَمَنْ كَرَّرَ تِلَاوَةَ سَجْدَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ فِي مَجْلِسِ وَاحِدٍ أَجْزَأَتْهُ سَجْدَةٌ وَاحِدَةٌ النَّاسُ، حَتَّى إِذَا كَانَتِ الْجُمُعَةُ الْقَابِلَةُ، قَرَأَ بِمَا، حَتَّى إِذَا جَاءَ السَّجْدَةَ، قَالَ: يَا أَيُّهَا النَّاسُ، إِنَّا نَمُرُّ بِالسُّجُودِ، فَمَنْ سَجَدَ فَقَدْ أَصَابَ، وَمَنْ لَمْ يَسْجُدْ فَلَا إِثْمَ عَلَيْهِ. وَلَمْ يَسْجُدْ عُمَرُ وَزَادَ نَافِعٌ، عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما : إِنَّ اللهَ لَمَّ يَفْرِضِ السُّجُودَ إِلَّا أَنْ نَشَاءَ،(بخاري شريف، بَابُ مَنْ رَأَى أَنَّ الله عز وجل لَم يُوجب السُّجُودَ ، نمبر 1077) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا تَلَا الْإِمَامُ آيَةَ سَجْدَةٍ سَجَدَهَا عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ قَالَ: «كَانَ النَّبِيُّ يَقْرَأُ السَّجْدَةَ وَنَحْنُ عِنْدَهُ ، فَيَسْجُدُ وَنَسْجُدُ مَعَهُ، فَنَزْدَحِمُ ، حَتَّى مَا يَجِدُ أَحَدُنَا لِجَبْهَتِهِ مَوْضِعًا يَسْجُدُ عَلَيْهِ، (بخاري شريف، بَابُ ازْدِحَامِ النَّاسِ إِذَا قَرَأَ الْإِمَامُ السَّجْدَةَ ، نمبر 1076) د وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ سَمِعُوا وَهُمْ فِي الصَّلَاةِ آيَةَ سَجْدَةٍ مِنْ رَجُلٍ عَنْ طَاوُسٍ، في الرَّجُلِ سَمِعَ السَّجْدَةَ وَهُوَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ قَالَ: «لَا يَسْجُدُ، مصنف ابن ابي شيبه،يَسْمَعُ السَّجْدَةَ قُرِئَتْ وَهُوَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ مَنْ قَالَ لَا يُسْجَدُ، نمبر 4303) توجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ تَلَا آيَةَ سَجْدَةٍ فَلَمْ يَسْجُدْهَا عَنْ مُجَاهِدٍ قَالَ: «إِذَا قَرَأْتَ السَّجْدَةَ أَجْزَأَكَ أَنْ تَسْجُدَ بِمَا مَرَّةً، مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، الرَّجُلُ يَقْرَأُ السَّجْدَةَ ثُمَّ يُعِيدُ قِرَاءَتَهَا كَيْفَ يَصْنَعُ ،نمبر 4200) دوجه:(۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ كَرَّرَ تِلَاوَةَ سَجْدَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ فِي مَجْلِسِ وَاحِدٍ عَنْ أَبِي عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ، أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَقْرَأُ السَّجْدَةَ فَيَسْجُدُ، ثُمَّ يُعِيدُهَا فِي مَجْلِسِهِ ذَلِكَ مِرَارًا لَا يَسْجُدُ،(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، الرَّجُلُ يَقْرَأُ السَّجْدَةَ ثُمَّ يُعِيدُ قِرَاءَتَهَا كَيْفَ يَصْنَعُ، نمبر 4201) اصول: اگر دوران نماز امام نے آیت سجدہ تلاوت کیا تو مقتدی پر بھی سجدہ واجب ہو گا متابعت کی وجہ سے۔ وَمَنْ أَرَادَ السُّجُودَ كَبَّرَ وَلَمْ يَرْفَعْ يَدَيْهِ وَسَجَدَ وَلَا تَشَهدَ عَلَيْهِ وَلَا سَلَامَ وجه:(۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ كَرَّرَ تِلَاوَةَ سَجْدَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ فِي مَجْلِسِ وَاحِدٍ عَنْ مُجَاهِدٍ قَالَ: «إِذَا قَرَأْتَ السَّجْدَةَ أَجْزَأَكَ أَنْ تَسْجُدَ بِمَا مَرَّةً، (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، الرَّجُلُ يَقْرَأُ السَّجْدَةَ ثُمَّ يُعِيدُ قِرَاءَتَهَا كَيْفَ يَصْنَعُ ،نمبر 4200) وجه (۳) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ كَرَّرَ تِلَاوَةَ سَجْدَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ فِي مَجْلِسِ وَاحِدٍ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ فِي الرَّجُلِ يَقْرَأُ السَّجْدَةَ ثُمَّ يُعِيدُ قِرَاءَتَهَا، قَالَ: «تُجْزِنُهُ السَّجْدَةُ الْأُولَى،،(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، الرَّجُلُ يَقْرَأُ السَّجْدَةَ ثُمَّ يُعِيدُ قِرَاءَتَهَا كَيْفَ يَصْنَعُ ،نمبر 4199) ووجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ أَرَادَ السُّجُودَ كَبَّرَ وَلَمْ يَرْفَعْ يَدَيْهِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْن مُسْلِمٍ قَالَ: كَانَ أَي، إِذَا قَرَأَ السَّجْدَةَ قَالَ: «اللَّهُ أَكْبَرُ» ثُمَّ سَجَدَ، (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَنْ قَالَ: إِذَا قَرَأْتَ السَّجْدَةَ فَكَبَرْ وَاسْجُدْ، نمبر 4187) وجه (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ أَرَادَ السُّجُودَ كَبَّرَ وَلَمْ يَرْفَعْ يَدَيْهِ عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَيْرٍ، «أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَقْرَأُ السَّجْدَةَ فَيَرْفَعُ رَأْسَهُ وَلَا يُسَلِّمُ، قَالَ «كَانَ الْحَسَنُ، يَقْرَأُ بِنَا سُجُودَ الْقُرْآنِ وَلَا يُسَلِّمُ، (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه ، مَنْ كَانَ لَا يُسَلَّمُ مِنَ السَّجْدَةِ، نمبر 4183/4184) وجه : (۳) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ أَرَادَ السُّجُودَ كَبَّرَ وَلَمْ يَرْفَعْ يَدَيْهِ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا سَمِعَهُ وَهُوَ عَلَى غَيْر وُضُوءِ فَلْيَتَوَضَّأَ ، ثُمَّ لِيَقْرَأْ فَلْيَسْجُدْ فَإِنْ كَانَ لَا يُحْسِنُهَا قَرَأَ غَيْرَهَا، ثُمَّ يَسْجُدُ (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، فِي الرَّجُلِ يَسْجُدُ السَّجْدَةَ وَهُوَ عَلَى غَيْرِ وُضُوءٍ، نمبر 4324) اصول: اگر خارج نماز میں کسی مصلی کی آیت سجدہ سنی تو اس شخص پر سجدہ واجب ہو گا۔ اصول: اگر مقتدی نے آیت سجدہ تلاوت کیا تو امام پر سجدہ نہیں ہو گا ورنہ اصل کا تابع ہو نالازم آئے گا۔ اصول : اصول ہے کہ ناقص سے کامل سجدہ ادا نہیں ہو تا ، لہذا اگر امام یا کسی مصلی نے خارج صلاۃ میں پڑھنے والے کا آیت سجدہ سنا اور اپنی نماز میں ہی سجدہ تلاوت کر لیا تو یہ ناقص سجدہ ہوا جبکہ کامل سجدہ واجب تھا۔
Chapter of Sujud al-Tilawah. And when the Imam recites an ayah of sajdah, he prostrates it and the follower prostrates with him. And if the follower recites, neither the Imam nor the follower is obliged to prostrate. And if they hear while in prayer an ayah of sajdah from a man not with them in prayer, they do not prostrate it in the prayer and prostrate it after the prayer. And if they prostrate it in the prayer, it does not suffice them and does not invalidate their prayer. And whoever recites an ayah of sajdah and does not prostrate it until he enters the prayer, then recites it and prostrates, that prostration suffices for both recitations. And if he recites it outside the prayer and prostrates for it, then enters the prayer and recites it, he prostrates for it and the first prostration does not suffice him. And whoever repeats the recitation of one sajdah in one sitting, one prostration suffices him... the people, until when the next Friday came, he recited with... until when he came to the sajdah, he said: 'O people, we pass by prostrations, so whoever prostrates has done correctly, and whoever does not prostrate, there is no sin upon him.' And 'Umar did not prostrate. And Nafi' added from Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with them): 'Allah did not prescribe the prostration unless we wish.' (Bukhari, chapter on those who believe Allah did not oblige prostration, no. 1077) Evidence: (1) The hadith to prove: 'When the Imam recites an ayah of sajdah, he prostrates it' from Ibn 'Umar said: 'The Prophet used to recite the sajdah while we were with him, and he would prostrate and we prostrate with him, and we would crowd such that none of us found a place for his forehead to prostrate on.' (Bukhari, chapter on crowding when the Imam recites the sajdah, no. 1076) Some evidence: (1) The saying of the Tabi'i to prove: 'And if they hear while in prayer an ayah of sajdah from a man' from Tawus regarding a man who hears the sajdah while in prayer, he said: 'He does not prostrate.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on one who hears the sajdah recited while in prayer, those who say do not prostrate, no. 4303) Attention: (a) The hadith to prove: 'And whoever recites an ayah of sajdah and does not prostrate it' from Mujahid said: 'When you recite the sajdah, it suffices you to prostrate once.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on the man who recites the sajdah then repeats its recitation, how should he act?, no. 4200) Some evidence: (1) The saying of the Tabi'i to prove: 'And whoever repeats the recitation of one sajdah in one sitting' from Abu 'Abd al-Rahman that he would recite the sajdah and prostrate, then repeat it in that same sitting multiple times and not prostrate. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on the man who recites the sajdah then repeats its recitation, how should he act?, no. 4201) Principle: If during prayer the Imam recites an ayah of sajdah, the follower is also obligated to prostrate due to following. And whoever intends to prostrate says takbir and does not raise his hands and prostrates, and there is no tashahhud upon him nor salam. Evidence: (2) The saying of the Tabi'i to prove: 'And whoever repeats the recitation of one sajdah in one sitting' from Mujahid said: 'When you recite the sajdah, it suffices you to prostrate once.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on the man who recites the sajdah then repeats its recitation, how should he act?, no. 4200) Evidence (3) The saying of the Tabi'i to prove: 'And whoever repeats the recitation of one sajdah in one sitting' from Ibrahim regarding a man who recites the sajdah then repeats its recitation, he said: 'The first prostration suffices him.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on the man who recites the sajdah then repeats its recitation, how should he act?, no. 4199) And evidence: (1) The saying of the Tabi'i to prove: 'And whoever intends to prostrate says takbir and does not raise his hands' from 'Abdullah bin Muslim said: 'He used to, when he recited the sajdah, say Allahu Akbar then prostrate.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on one who said: When you recite the sajdah, say takbir and prostrate, no. 4187) Evidence (2) The saying of the Tabi'i to prove: 'And whoever intends to prostrate says takbir and does not raise his hands' from Sa'id bin Jubayr that he used to recite the sajdah and raise his head and not say salam. He said: 'Al-Hasan used to recite the Qur'anic prostrations with us and not say salam.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on those who did not say salam from the prostration, no. 4183/4184) Evidence: (3) The saying of the Tabi'i to prove: 'And whoever intends to prostrate says takbir and does not raise his hands' from Ibrahim said: 'When he hears it while not in wudu, let him perform wudu, then recite, then prostrate. And if he does not know it, let him recite another, then prostrate.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on the man who prostrates for the sajdah while not in wudu, no. 4324) Principle: If outside prayer one hears the ayah of sajdah from a person praying, that person is obligated to prostrate. Principle: If the follower recites an ayah of sajdah, the Imam is not obligated to prostrate, otherwise following would require it. Principle: The principle is that an incomplete prostration does not fulfill a complete prostration. Therefore, if the Imam or a person in prayer hears an ayah of sajdah from someone reciting outside prayer and performs the sajdah al-tilawah within his prayer, this is an incomplete prostration, whereas a complete prostration was obligatory.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is a set of rulings from the matn of al-Quduri on Sujud al-Tilawah, followed by proofs (wajh) from hadith and athar, and Urdu commentary. The chapter begins by establishing the ruling for the imam: if he recites an ayah of sajdah during prayer, he must prostrate, and the followers must prostrate with him out of following (mutaba'ah). This is proven by the hadith of Ibn 'Umar where the Prophet would prostrate and they would prostrate with him. If the follower (ma'mum) recites the ayah, neither the imam nor the follower is obligated to prostrate in that prayer? The text seems to say 'لَمْ يَلْزَمُ' meaning it is not binding. The Urdu commentary clarifies that this is because the follower's recitation does not impose obligation on the imam; otherwise the principle of following would require it, but here it is not required. If the congregation hears an ayah of sajdah from someone not in their prayer (e.g., a reciter outside), they do not prostrate in the prayer but must prostrate after the prayer. If they mistakenly prostrate in the prayer, it does not suffice (since it is incomplete) but does not invalidate the prayer. This is supported by the athar of Tawus. The text then discusses cases of reciting the same ayah multiple times: if one recites an ayah outside prayer and does not prostrate, then enters prayer and recites it again and prostrates, that one prostration suffices for both recitations. But if he prostrates outside prayer first, then recites it again in prayer, he must prostrate again and the first does not suffice. If he repeats the same ayah in one sitting, one prostration suffices. These are proven by athar of Mujahid, Abu 'Abd al-Rahman, and Ibrahim. The manner of prostration: one says takbir, does not raise hands, prostrates, and there is no tashahhud or salam. This is proven by athar of 'Abdullah bin Muslim, Sa'id bin Jubayr, and Al-Hasan. The Urdu commentary adds that if one hears the ayah from a person praying outside, it is obligatory to prostrate. Also, if the follower recites, the imam does not have to prostrate. And that an incomplete prostration cannot replace a complete one; thus, prostrating within prayer for an ayah heard from outside is insufficient.

Key Terms
سجود التلاوة (sujud al-tilawah): Prostration performed upon reciting or hearing a specific verse of the Quran that contains a command or reference to prostration.
المأموم (al-ma'mum): The follower praying behind an imam in congregation.
متابعة (mutaba'ah): Following the imam in all actions of prayer; the principle that the ma'mum must not precede the imam and must follow him in wajib acts like sujud al-tilawah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person is praying alone and hears a sajdah verse from a reciter outside the prayer, what should he do according to the Hanafi school?
A) He should prostrate immediately during his prayer.
B) He should not prostrate at all because he is in prayer.
C) He should complete his prayer, then prostrate after the prayer.
D) He should make an intention and prostrate after the prayer only if he wants.

Key Takeaway
In congregational prayer, the imam's recitation of a sajdah verse obligates prostration for both; the ma'mum's recitation does not; hearing from outside requires post-prayer prostration because an incomplete act cannot fulfill a complete obligation.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Sujud al-Tilawah: Repeated Recitations and Manner of Prostration
Rulings on repeated recitations and manner of prostration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling that one prostration suffices for multiple recitations of the same verse in one sitting, and describe the correct manner of sujud al-tilawah (takbir, not raising hands, no tashahhud, no salam).

Core Idea
Repeating the same ayah in one sitting requires only one prostration; the prostration is performed with takbir, without raising hands, and without tashahhud or salam.

Sujud al-tilawah has specific guidelines when the same verse is recited multiple times, and a specific method of performance. This lesson covers the ruling that one prostration suffices for repeated recitations in one sitting, and the details of how to perform the prostration: saying takbir, not raising the hands, and the absence of tashahhud and salam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the repetition scenario
Read the matn: 'And whoever repeats the recitation of one sajdah in one sitting, one prostration suffices him.' Also the conditional clauses about reciting before entering prayer and after.
The key is the phrase 'in one sitting' (في مجلس واحد).
2
State the ruling on multiple recitations
If the same ayah is recited multiple times in one sitting (majlis), only one prostration is wajib. If recited in different sittings, each requires its own prostration.
The matn also addresses when a recitation occurs partially outside prayer and partially inside.
3
Identify the proofs
The athar of Mujahid, Abu 'Abd al-Rahman, and Ibrahim all state that one prostration suffices for multiple recitations.
These are cited in the commentary after the matn.
4
Describe the manner of prostration
The matn says: 'And whoever intends to prostrate says takbir and does not raise his hands and prostrates, and there is no tashahhud upon him nor salam.'
The proofs are from 'Abdullah bin Muslim and Sa'id bin Jubayr.
5
Apply the conditions
Ensure the person is in a state of wudu (if outside prayer) and not in janabah. The prostration is a single sujood, not two.
These conditions are from the earlier part of the passage.

إِلَّا أَنْ نَشَاءَ،(بخاري شريف، بَابُ مَنْ رَأَى أَنَّ الله عز وجل لَم يُوجب السُّجُودَ ، نمبر 1077) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا تَلَا الْإِمَامُ آيَةَ سَجْدَةٍ سَجَدَهَا عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ قَالَ: السَّجْدَةَ ثُمَّ يُعِيدُ قِرَاءَتَهَا كَيْفَ يَصْنَعُ ،نمبر 4200) وجه (۳) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ كَرَّرَ تِلَاوَةَ سَجْدَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ فِي مَجْلِسِ وَاحِدٍ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ فِي الرَّجُلِ يَقْرَأُ السَّجْدَةَ ثُمَّ يُعِيدُ قِرَاءَتَهَا، قَالَ: «تُجْزِنُهُ السَّجْدَةُ الْأُولَى،،(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، الرَّجُلُ يَقْرَأُ السَّجْدَةَ ثُمَّ يُعِيدُ قِرَاءَتَهَا كَيْفَ يَصْنَعُ ،نمبر 4199) ووجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ أَرَادَ السُّجُودَ كَبَّرَ وَلَمْ يَرْفَعْ يَدَيْهِ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْن مُسْلِمٍ قَالَ: كَانَ أَي، إِذَا قَرَأَ السَّجْدَةَ قَالَ: «اللَّهُ أَكْبَرُ» ثُمَّ سَجَدَ، (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَنْ قَالَ: إِذَا قَرَأْتَ السَّجْدَةَ فَكَبَرْ وَاسْجُدْ، نمبر 4187) وجه (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ أَرَادَ السُّجُودَ كَبَّرَ وَلَمْ يَرْفَعْ يَدَيْهِ عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَيْرٍ، «أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَقْرَأُ السَّجْدَةَ فَيَرْفَعُ رَأْسَهُ وَلَا يُسَلِّمُ، قَالَ «كَانَ الْحَسَنُ، يَقْرَأُ بِنَا سُجُودَ الْقُرْآنِ وَلَا يُسَلِّمُ، (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه ، مَنْ كَانَ لَا يُسَلَّمُ مِنَ السَّجْدَةِ، نمبر 4183/4184) وجه : (۳) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ أَرَادَ السُّجُودَ كَبَّرَ وَلَمْ يَرْفَعْ يَدَيْهِ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ قَالَ: «إِذَا سَمِعَهُ وَهُوَ عَلَى غَيْر وُضُوءِ فَلْيَتَوَضَّأَ ، ثُمَّ لِيَقْرَأْ فَلْيَسْجُدْ فَإِنْ كَانَ لَا يُحْسِنُهَا قَرَأَ غَيْرَهَا، ثُمَّ يَسْجُدُ (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، فِي الرَّجُلِ يَسْجُدُ السَّجْدَةَ وَهُوَ عَلَى غَيْرِ وُضُوءٍ، نمبر 4324) اصول: اگر خارج نماز میں کسی مصلی کی آیت سجدہ سنی تو اس شخص پر سجدہ واجب ہو گا۔ اصول: اگر مقتدی نے آیت سجدہ تلاوت کیا تو امام پر سجدہ نہیں ہو گا ورنہ اصل کا تابع ہو نالازم آئے گا۔ اصول : اصول ہے کہ ناقص سے کامل سجدہ ادا نہیں ہو تا ، لہذا اگر امام یا کسی مصلی نے خارج صلاۃ میں پڑھنے والے کا آیت سجدہ سنا اور اپنی نماز میں ہی سجدہ تلاوت کر لیا تو یہ ناقص سجدہ ہوا جبکہ کامل سجدہ واجب تھا۔
Chapter of Sujud al-Tilawah. And when the Imam recites an ayah of sajdah, he prostrates it and the follower prostrates with him. And if the follower recites, neither the Imam nor the follower is obliged to prostrate. And if they hear while in prayer an ayah of sajdah from a man not with them in prayer, they do not prostrate it in the prayer and prostrate it after the prayer. And if they prostrate it in the prayer, it does not suffice them and does not invalidate their prayer. And whoever recites an ayah of sajdah and does not prostrate it until he enters the prayer, then recites it and prostrates, that prostration suffices for both recitations. And if he recites it outside the prayer and prostrates for it, then enters the prayer and recites it, he prostrates for it and the first prostration does not suffice him. And whoever repeats the recitation of one sajdah in one sitting, one prostration suffices him... the people, until when the next Friday came, he recited with... until when he came to the sajdah, he said: 'O people, we pass by prostrations, so whoever prostrates has done correctly, and whoever does not prostrate, there is no sin upon him.' And 'Umar did not prostrate. And Nafi' added from Ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with them): 'Allah did not prescribe the prostration unless we wish.' (Bukhari, chapter on those who believe Allah did not oblige prostration, no. 1077) Evidence: (1) The hadith to prove: 'When the Imam recites an ayah of sajdah, he prostrates it' from Ibn 'Umar said: 'The Prophet used to recite the sajdah while we were with him, and he would prostrate and we prostrate with him, and we would crowd such that none of us found a place for his forehead to prostrate on.' (Bukhari, chapter on crowding when the Imam recites the sajdah, no. 1076) Some evidence: (1) The saying of the Tabi'i to prove: 'And if they hear while in prayer an ayah of sajdah from a man' from Tawus regarding a man who hears the sajdah while in prayer, he said: 'He does not prostrate.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on one who hears the sajdah recited while in prayer, those who say do not prostrate, no. 4303) Attention: (a) The hadith to prove: 'And whoever recites an ayah of sajdah and does not prostrate it' from Mujahid said: 'When you recite the sajdah, it suffices you to prostrate once.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on the man who recites the sajdah then repeats its recitation, how should he act?, no. 4200) Some evidence: (1) The saying of the Tabi'i to prove: 'And whoever repeats the recitation of one sajdah in one sitting' from Abu 'Abd al-Rahman that he would recite the sajdah and prostrate, then repeat it in that same sitting multiple times and not prostrate. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on the man who recites the sajdah then repeats its recitation, how should he act?, no. 4201) Principle: If during prayer the Imam recites an ayah of sajdah, the follower is also obligated to prostrate due to following. And whoever intends to prostrate says takbir and does not raise his hands and prostrates, and there is no tashahhud upon him nor salam. Evidence: (2) The saying of the Tabi'i to prove: 'And whoever repeats the recitation of one sajdah in one sitting' from Mujahid said: 'When you recite the sajdah, it suffices you to prostrate once.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on the man who recites the sajdah then repeats its recitation, how should he act?, no. 4200) Evidence (3) The saying of the Tabi'i to prove: 'And whoever repeats the recitation of one sajdah in one sitting' from Ibrahim regarding a man who recites the sajdah then repeats its recitation, he said: 'The first prostration suffices him.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on the man who recites the sajdah then repeats its recitation, how should he act?, no. 4199) And evidence: (1) The saying of the Tabi'i to prove: 'And whoever intends to prostrate says takbir and does not raise his hands' from 'Abdullah bin Muslim said: 'He used to, when he recited the sajdah, say Allahu Akbar then prostrate.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on one who said: When you recite the sajdah, say takbir and prostrate, no. 4187) Evidence (2) The saying of the Tabi'i to prove: 'And whoever intends to prostrate says takbir and does not raise his hands' from Sa'id bin Jubayr that he used to recite the sajdah and raise his head and not say salam. He said: 'Al-Hasan used to recite the Qur'anic prostrations with us and not say salam.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on those who did not say salam from the prostration, no. 4183/4184) Evidence: (3) The saying of the Tabi'i to prove: 'And whoever intends to prostrate says takbir and does not raise his hands' from Ibrahim said: 'When he hears it while not in wudu, let him perform wudu, then recite, then prostrate. And if he does not know it, let him recite another, then prostrate.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on the man who prostrates for the sajdah while not in wudu, no. 4324) Principle: If outside prayer one hears the ayah of sajdah from a person praying, that person is obligated to prostrate. Principle: If the follower recites an ayah of sajdah, the Imam is not obligated to prostrate, otherwise following would require it. Principle: The principle is that an incomplete prostration does not fulfill a complete prostration. Therefore, if the Imam or a person in prayer hears an ayah of sajdah from someone reciting outside prayer and performs the sajdah al-tilawah within his prayer, this is an incomplete prostration, whereas a complete prostration was obligatory.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is a set of rulings from the matn of al-Quduri on Sujud al-Tilawah, followed by proofs (wajh) from hadith and athar, and Urdu commentary. The chapter begins by establishing the ruling for the imam: if he recites an ayah of sajdah during prayer, he must prostrate, and the followers must prostrate with him out of following (mutaba'ah). This is proven by the hadith of Ibn 'Umar where the Prophet would prostrate and they would prostrate with him. If the follower (ma'mum) recites the ayah, neither the imam nor the follower is obligated to prostrate in that prayer? The text seems to say 'لَمْ يَلْزَمُ' meaning it is not binding. The Urdu commentary clarifies that this is because the follower's recitation does not impose obligation on the imam; otherwise the principle of following would require it, but here it is not required. If the congregation hears an ayah of sajdah from someone not in their prayer (e.g., a reciter outside), they do not prostrate in the prayer but must prostrate after the prayer. If they mistakenly prostrate in the prayer, it does not suffice (since it is incomplete) but does not invalidate the prayer. This is supported by the athar of Tawus. The text then discusses cases of reciting the same ayah multiple times: if one recites an ayah outside prayer and does not prostrate, then enters prayer and recites it again and prostrates, that one prostration suffices for both recitations. But if he prostrates outside prayer first, then recites it again in prayer, he must prostrate again and the first does not suffice. If he repeats the same ayah in one sitting, one prostration suffices. These are proven by athar of Mujahid, Abu 'Abd al-Rahman, and Ibrahim. The manner of prostration: one says takbir, does not raise hands, prostrates, and there is no tashahhud or salam. This is proven by athar of 'Abdullah bin Muslim, Sa'id bin Jubayr, and Al-Hasan. The Urdu commentary adds that if one hears the ayah from a person praying outside, it is obligatory to prostrate. Also, if the follower recites, the imam does not have to prostrate. And that an incomplete prostration cannot replace a complete one; thus, prostrating within prayer for an ayah heard from outside is insufficient.

Key Terms
تكرار التلاوة (tikrar al-tilawah): Repeating the recitation of the same sajdah verse multiple times.
مجلس واحد (majlis wahid): One sitting or session; the time period during which a person remains in the same place without a significant break.
تكبيرة الإحرام للسجود (takbirat al-ihram li al-sujud): The takbir said when initiating sujud al-tilawah; it is wajib in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct way to perform sujud al-tilawah according to the Hanafi school?
A) Say takbir, raise hands, prostrate twice, then say tashahhud and salam.
B) Say takbir, do not raise hands, prostrate once, no tashahhud or salam.
C) Say takbir, raise hands, prostrate once, then say salam.
D) No takbir, just prostrate once, then say tashahhud.

Key Takeaway
Repeating the same sajdah verse in one sitting requires only one prostration; the prostration is performed with takbir, without raising hands, and without tashahhud or salam.

Praying Four Rakats in Travel: Validity and Consequences
Ruling on praying four in travel with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying four rakats in travel and apply the condition of sitting for tashahhud to determine the prayer's validity.

Core Idea
Sitting for tashahhud separates fard from nafl; without it, the prayer becomes invalid.

This lesson examines what happens if a traveler prays four rakats instead of two. The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer: the presence or absence of the sitting in the second rakat changes the ruling entirely. The attached proofs strengthen this position, while the Shafi'i counterargument is addressed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is praying four rakats for a four-rakat fard (e.g., Zuhr) while traveling. The normal fard is two rakats due to qasr.
This ruling applies only to the traveler who intends to pray the fard.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
Scenario A: The traveler sits in the second rakat for the duration of tashahhud. Scenario B: He does not sit (e.g., stands directly after second sajdah).
The sitting is a marker that separates the first two rakats from the last two.
3
Apply the ruling
In Scenario A: The first two rakats count as the fard, and the last two become nafl (supererogatory). The prayer is valid. In Scenario B: The entire prayer is invalid because the fard was not properly isolated; the extra two rakats corrupted it.
If invalid, the prayer must be repeated.
4
Locate the dalil
The strongest evidence is the saying of Ibn Mas'ud: 'Whoever prays four in travel, repeats the prayer.' This shows that completing four invalidates the original fard. Additionally, the Prophet's consistent practice of two rakats in travel (hadith of Anas and Ibn Umar) supports the obligation.
These hadith are from Bukhari and Musannaf Abdurrazzaq.
5
Evaluate the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school argues that completing four is permissible based on Uthman's practice at Mina and the Quranic phrase 'la junah' (no blame). The Hanafi response: Uthman's action was his ijtihad, but the Sunnah is decisive; 'la junah' negates sin for shortening, not permission to complete. Ibn Mas'ud's explicit command to repeat overrides.
Practical difference: Hanafi must repeat if no sitting; Shafi'i considers it valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وجه :(۲) الحديث لثبوت فَرْضُ الْمُسَافِرِ عِنْدَنَا فِي كُلِّ صَلَاةٍ سَمِعْتُ أَنَسًا يَقُولُ: «خَرَجْنَا مَعَ التي الله مِنَ الْمَدِينَةِ إِلَى مَكَّةَ، فَكَانَ يُصَلِّي رَكْعَتَيْنِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ، حَتَّى رَجَعْنَا إِلَى الْمَدِينَةِ، قُلْتُ: أَقَمْتُمْ
بمَكَّةَ شَيْئًا ؟ قَالَ : أَقَمْنَا بِمَا عَشْرًا، بخاري شريف مَا جَاءَ فِي التَّقْصِير وكَمْ يُقِيمُ حَتَّى يَقْصُرَ ، 1081) وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت فَرْضُ الْمُسَافِرِ عِنْدَنَا فِي كُلّ صَلَاةٍ \ أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ ابْنَ عُمَرَ يَقُولُ: صَحِبْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ ، فَكَانَ لا يَزِيدُ فِي السَّفَرِ عَلَى رَكْعَتَيْنِ، وَأَبَا بَكْرٍ وَعُمَرَ وَعُثْمَانَ كَذَلِكَ ( بخاري شريف، بَابُ مَنْ لَمْ يَتَطَوَّعْ فِي السَّفَرِ دُبُرَ الصَّلَاةِ وَقَبْلَهَا، نمبر 1102) وجه (۱) دليل الشافعى الحديث لثبوت فَرْضُ الْمُسَافِرِ عِنْدَنَا فِي كُلَّ صَلَاةٍ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ الله قَالَ: «صَلَّيْتُ مَعَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم مِنَى رَكْعَتَيْنِ، وَأَبِي بَكْرٍ وَعُمَرَ، وَمَعَ عُثْمَانَ صَدْرًا مِنْ إِمَارَتِهِ ثُمَّ أَتَها، (بخاري شريف ، بَابُ الصَّلَاةِ بِمِنِّى، نمبر 1082)
وجه:(۲) دليل الشافعى الايةُ لثبوت فَرْضُ الْمُسَافِرِ عِنْدَنَا فِي كُلِّ صَلَاةٍ \ ﴿وَإِذَا ضَرَبْتُمْ فِي
الْأَرْضِ فَلَيْسَ عَلَيْكُمْ جُنَاحٌ أَن تَقْصُرُوا مِنَ الصَّلوة (سورة النساء 4، نمبر 101) وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَرْضُ الْمُسَافِرِ عِنْدَنَا فِي كُلِّ صَلَاةٍ \ أَنَّ ابْنَ مَسْعُودٍ قَالَ: «مَنْ صَلَّى فِي السَّفَرِ أَرْبَعًا أَعَادَ الصَّلَاةَ ، (مصنف عبدالرزاق بَابُ مَنْ أَتَمَّ فِي السَّفَرِ، نمبر 4466) ه وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ خَرَجَ مُسَافِرًا صَلَّى رَكْعَتَيْنِ \ عَنْ أَنَسٍ قَالَ: «صَلَّيْتُ مَعَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِالْمَدِينَةِ أَرْبَعًا وَبِذِي الْحَلَيْفَةِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ»، (بخاري شريف، بَابٌ: يَقْصُرُ إِذَا خَرَجَ مِنْ مَوْضِعِهِ، نمبر 689)
الظُّهْرَ
وجه (۲) قول الصحابى لثبوت وَمَنْ خَرَجَ مُسَافِرًا صَلَّى رَكْعَتَيْنِ \ أَنَّ عَلِيًّا لَمَّا خَرَجَ إِلَى الْبَصْرَةِ رَأَى حُمَّا فَقَالَ: «لَوْلَا هَذَا الخُصُّ لَصَلَّيْنَا رَكْعَتَيْنِ». فَقُلْتُ: مَا خُصَّا؟ قَالَ: «بَيْتٌ مِنْ قَصَبِ (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ : الْمُسَافِرِ مَتَى يَقْصُرُ إِذَا خَرَجَ مُسَافِرًا، نمبر 4319) اصول: فرائض پورے ہونے کے بعد نوافل کو فرائض کے ساتھ ملالیا تو فرض کراہیت کیساتھ ادا ہو جائے گا۔
Then if he prays four (rakats) and sits in the second (rakat) for the measure of tashahhud, two rakats suffice for his obligation and the other two are supererogatory for him. And if he does not sit in the second for the measure of tashahhud, his prayer is invalid. And whoever goes out as a traveler prays two rakats when he leaves the houses of the town. Proof (2): Hadith to establish the obligation of the traveler with us in every prayer: I heard Anas saying: 'We went out with the Prophet from Medina to Mecca, and he used to pray two rakats two rakats until we returned to Medina.' I said: 'Did you stay in Mecca anything?' He said: 'We stayed ten days.' (Bukhari, 1081). Proof (3): Hadith to establish the obligation of the traveler with us in every prayer: that he heard Ibn Umar say: 'I accompanied the Messenger of Allah and he never increased in travel beyond two rakats, and Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman likewise.' (Bukhari, 1102). Proof (1): Shafi'i's proof: Hadith from Abdullah (Ibn Mas'ud) who said: 'I prayed with the Prophet at Mina two rakats, and with Abu Bakr and Umar, and with Uthman in the early part of his caliphate, then he completed them.' (Bukhari, 1082). Proof (2): Shafi'i's proof: The verse: 'And when you travel in the land, there is no blame upon you for shortening the prayer.' (Surah An-Nisa 4:101). Proof (1): Saying of a Companion to establish the obligation of the traveler with us in every prayer: that Ibn Mas'ud said: 'Whoever prays four in travel, repeats the prayer.' (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, 4466). Proof (1): Hadith to establish 'whoever goes out as a traveler prays two rakats': from Anas who said: 'I prayed with the Prophet in Medina four, and at Dhu al-Hulayfah two.' (Bukhari, 689). And: Zuhr. Proof (2): Saying of a Companion to establish 'whoever goes out as a traveler prays two rakats': that when Ali went out to Basra, he saw al-Humma (?) and said: 'Were it not for this khuss (hut), we would pray two rakats.' I said: 'What is khuss?' He said: 'A house of reeds.' (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, 4319). Principle: After the fard is completed, if supererogatory (nafl) is attached to the fard, then the fard is performed with dislike.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage addresses two subsidiary issues of the traveler's prayer. First: if a traveler mistakenly (or deliberately) prays four rakats, the validity depends on whether he sits for tashahhud in the second rakat. If he sits, the first two count as fard (obligatory) and the next two become nafl (supererogatory). If he does not sit, the entire prayer is invalid because the fard was not properly separated. Second: the point at which qasr begins — when the traveler leaves the houses of his town (the built-up area). The author then provides extensive proofs: (2) and (3) are Hanafi proofs for the obligation of two rakats from Anas and Ibn Umar, showing the Prophet always shortened. Then two Shafi'i proofs: the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud who noted that Uthman completed at Mina later (showing completion is permissible), and the Quranic verse that uses 'no blame' (la junah) which suggests permission, not obligation. The Hanafi response is given via Ibn Mas'ud's strong statement: 'Whoever prays four in travel, repeats the prayer.' That indicates it is invalid to complete. Then proofs for the start of qasr: Anas's hadith that the Prophet prayed two at Dhu al-Hulayfah (outside Medina), and Ali's reported statement that were it not for the hut (khuss), they would have prayed two, implying that leaving the town's buildings triggers qasr. The final Urdu usul note clarifies the status of the prayer if one adds nafl after the fard in travel: the fard is performed but with karahah (dislike).

Key Terms
تشهد (tashahhud): The obligatory sitting recitation in the second rakat of prayer.
نافلة (nāfilah): Supererogatory prayer; voluntary extra prayer beyond the fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is valid, but he must perform sujud al-sahw
B) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated
C) The first two rakats count as fard, the last two as nafl
D) The prayer is valid and complete

Key Takeaway
The validity of praying four rakats in travel hinges entirely on whether the traveler sits for tashahhud in the second rakat; without it, the prayer is invalid.

When Does Qasr Begin? Leaving the Town's Houses
Ruling on the start of qasr with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the trigger point for qasr according to the Hanafi school and apply it to determine when a traveler must pray two rakats.

Core Idea
Qasr begins when the traveler physically leaves the built-up area of the town.

Knowing exactly when the obligation reduces to two rakats is essential for the traveler. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi criterion: departure from the town's houses, not mere intention or leaving the city limits. Two strong proofs from the practice of the Prophet and the action of Ali reinforce this.

Guided Path
1
State the rule
The matn states: 'Whoever goes out as a traveler prays two rakats when he leaves the houses of the town.'
The rule applies to a person who intends travel and departs.
2
Identify the condition
The trigger is physical departure from the built-up area (بيوت المصر). The traveler must have left behind the continuous houses of the town.
Intention alone is not sufficient; actual exit is required.
3
Examine the first proof
Anas reported that the Prophet prayed four rakats in Medina (where he was a resident) and two rakats at Dhu al-Hulayfah (a location outside Medina). This shows that qasr began as soon as he left the town's houses.
Dhu al-Hulayfah is the miqat for Hajj, about 10 km from Medina.
4
Examine the second proof
When Ali went out to Basra, he saw a hut (خص) at the edge of town and said: 'Were it not for this hut, we would pray two rakats.' This indicates that the presence of a building (even a hut) means he is still within the town's zone, so qasr does not start until he is beyond all buildings.
The 'humma' in the text is likely a reference to a fever or an obstacle; the key point is Ali's statement about the hut.
5
Apply to practice
A traveler must check if he has left the last houses of his town. If he is still within the built-up area (including suburbs with continuous buildings), he must pray full prayers. Once he crosses the boundary, he shortens.
In modern cities, this translates to leaving the urban area.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِن صَلَّى أَرْبَعًا وَقَعَدَ فِي الثَّانِيَةِ مِقْدَارَ التَّشَهُدِ أَجْزَأَتْهُ رَكْعَتَانِ عَنْ فَرْضِهِ وَكَانَتْ الْأُخْرَيَانِ لَهُ نَافِلَةٌ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَقْعُدُ فِي الثَّانِيَةِ قَدْرَ التَّشَهُدِ بَطَلَتْ صَلَاتُهُ هي وَمَنْ خَرَجَ مُسَافِرًا صَلَّى رَكْعَتَيْنِ إِذَا فَارَقَ بُيُوتَ الْمِصْرِ

وجه :(۲) الحديث لثبوت فَرْضُ الْمُسَافِرِ عِنْدَنَا فِي كُلِّ صَلَاةٍ سَمِعْتُ أَنَسًا يَقُولُ: «خَرَجْنَا مَعَ التي الله مِنَ الْمَدِينَةِ إِلَى مَكَّةَ، فَكَانَ يُصَلِّي رَكْعَتَيْنِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ، حَتَّى رَجَعْنَا إِلَى الْمَدِينَةِ، قُلْتُ: أَقَمْتُمْ
بمَكَّةَ شَيْئًا ؟ قَالَ : أَقَمْنَا بِمَا عَشْرًا، بخاري شريف مَا جَاءَ فِي التَّقْصِير وكَمْ يُقِيمُ حَتَّى يَقْصُرَ ، 1081) وجه (۳) الحديث لثبوت فَرْضُ الْمُسَافِرِ عِنْدَنَا فِي كُلّ صَلَاةٍ \ أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ ابْنَ عُمَرَ يَقُولُ: صَحِبْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ ، فَكَانَ لا يَزِيدُ فِي السَّفَرِ عَلَى رَكْعَتَيْنِ، وَأَبَا بَكْرٍ وَعُمَرَ وَعُثْمَانَ كَذَلِكَ ( بخاري شريف، بَابُ مَنْ لَمْ يَتَطَوَّعْ فِي السَّفَرِ دُبُرَ الصَّلَاةِ وَقَبْلَهَا، نمبر 1102) وجه (۱) دليل الشافعى الحديث لثبوت فَرْضُ الْمُسَافِرِ عِنْدَنَا فِي كُلَّ صَلَاةٍ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ الله قَالَ: «صَلَّيْتُ مَعَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم مِنَى رَكْعَتَيْنِ، وَأَبِي بَكْرٍ وَعُمَرَ، وَمَعَ عُثْمَانَ صَدْرًا مِنْ إِمَارَتِهِ ثُمَّ أَتَها، (بخاري شريف ، بَابُ الصَّلَاةِ بِمِنِّى، نمبر 1082)
وجه:(۲) دليل الشافعى الايةُ لثبوت فَرْضُ الْمُسَافِرِ عِنْدَنَا فِي كُلِّ صَلَاةٍ \ ﴿وَإِذَا ضَرَبْتُمْ فِي
الْأَرْضِ فَلَيْسَ عَلَيْكُمْ جُنَاحٌ أَن تَقْصُرُوا مِنَ الصَّلوة (سورة النساء 4، نمبر 101) وجه (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَرْضُ الْمُسَافِرِ عِنْدَنَا فِي كُلِّ صَلَاةٍ \ أَنَّ ابْنَ مَسْعُودٍ قَالَ: «مَنْ صَلَّى فِي السَّفَرِ أَرْبَعًا أَعَادَ الصَّلَاةَ ، (مصنف عبدالرزاق بَابُ مَنْ أَتَمَّ فِي السَّفَرِ، نمبر 4466) ه وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ خَرَجَ مُسَافِرًا صَلَّى رَكْعَتَيْنِ \ عَنْ أَنَسٍ قَالَ: «صَلَّيْتُ مَعَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بِالْمَدِينَةِ أَرْبَعًا وَبِذِي الْحَلَيْفَةِ رَكْعَتَيْنِ»، (بخاري شريف، بَابٌ: يَقْصُرُ إِذَا خَرَجَ مِنْ مَوْضِعِهِ، نمبر 689)
الظُّهْرَ
وجه (۲) قول الصحابى لثبوت وَمَنْ خَرَجَ مُسَافِرًا صَلَّى رَكْعَتَيْنِ \ أَنَّ عَلِيًّا لَمَّا خَرَجَ إِلَى الْبَصْرَةِ رَأَى حُمَّا فَقَالَ: «لَوْلَا هَذَا الخُصُّ لَصَلَّيْنَا رَكْعَتَيْنِ». فَقُلْتُ: مَا خُصَّا؟ قَالَ: «بَيْتٌ مِنْ قَصَبِ (مصنف عبدالرزاق، بَابُ : الْمُسَافِرِ مَتَى يَقْصُرُ إِذَا خَرَجَ مُسَافِرًا، نمبر 4319) اصول: فرائض پورے ہونے کے بعد نوافل کو فرائض کے ساتھ ملالیا تو فرض کراہیت کیساتھ ادا ہو جائے گا۔
Then if he prays four (rakats) and sits in the second (rakat) for the measure of tashahhud, two rakats suffice for his obligation and the other two are supererogatory for him. And if he does not sit in the second for the measure of tashahhud, his prayer is invalid. And whoever goes out as a traveler prays two rakats when he leaves the houses of the town. Proof (2): Hadith to establish the obligation of the traveler with us in every prayer: I heard Anas saying: 'We went out with the Prophet from Medina to Mecca, and he used to pray two rakats two rakats until we returned to Medina.' I said: 'Did you stay in Mecca anything?' He said: 'We stayed ten days.' (Bukhari, 1081). Proof (3): Hadith to establish the obligation of the traveler with us in every prayer: that he heard Ibn Umar say: 'I accompanied the Messenger of Allah and he never increased in travel beyond two rakats, and Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman likewise.' (Bukhari, 1102). Proof (1): Shafi'i's proof: Hadith from Abdullah (Ibn Mas'ud) who said: 'I prayed with the Prophet at Mina two rakats, and with Abu Bakr and Umar, and with Uthman in the early part of his caliphate, then he completed them.' (Bukhari, 1082). Proof (2): Shafi'i's proof: The verse: 'And when you travel in the land, there is no blame upon you for shortening the prayer.' (Surah An-Nisa 4:101). Proof (1): Saying of a Companion to establish the obligation of the traveler with us in every prayer: that Ibn Mas'ud said: 'Whoever prays four in travel, repeats the prayer.' (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, 4466). Proof (1): Hadith to establish 'whoever goes out as a traveler prays two rakats': from Anas who said: 'I prayed with the Prophet in Medina four, and at Dhu al-Hulayfah two.' (Bukhari, 689). And: Zuhr. Proof (2): Saying of a Companion to establish 'whoever goes out as a traveler prays two rakats': that when Ali went out to Basra, he saw al-Humma (?) and said: 'Were it not for this khuss (hut), we would pray two rakats.' I said: 'What is khuss?' He said: 'A house of reeds.' (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, 4319). Principle: After the fard is completed, if supererogatory (nafl) is attached to the fard, then the fard is performed with dislike.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage addresses two subsidiary issues of the traveler's prayer. First: if a traveler mistakenly (or deliberately) prays four rakats, the validity depends on whether he sits for tashahhud in the second rakat. If he sits, the first two count as fard (obligatory) and the next two become nafl (supererogatory). If he does not sit, the entire prayer is invalid because the fard was not properly separated. Second: the point at which qasr begins — when the traveler leaves the houses of his town (the built-up area). The author then provides extensive proofs: (2) and (3) are Hanafi proofs for the obligation of two rakats from Anas and Ibn Umar, showing the Prophet always shortened. Then two Shafi'i proofs: the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud who noted that Uthman completed at Mina later (showing completion is permissible), and the Quranic verse that uses 'no blame' (la junah) which suggests permission, not obligation. The Hanafi response is given via Ibn Mas'ud's strong statement: 'Whoever prays four in travel, repeats the prayer.' That indicates it is invalid to complete. Then proofs for the start of qasr: Anas's hadith that the Prophet prayed two at Dhu al-Hulayfah (outside Medina), and Ali's reported statement that were it not for the hut (khuss), they would have prayed two, implying that leaving the town's buildings triggers qasr. The final Urdu usul note clarifies the status of the prayer if one adds nafl after the fard in travel: the fard is performed but with karahah (dislike).

Key Terms
مصر (miṣr): The town or settlement; its houses mark the boundary for beginning qasr.
خص (khuss): A hut or temporary shelter made of reeds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a traveler begin to shorten prayers?
A) When he intends to travel
B) When he leaves the houses of the town
C) After traveling three days
D) When he reaches the destination

Key Takeaway
Qasr is triggered by physically leaving the built-up area of the town, not by intention or distance.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Ruling on Traveler Praying Four with Tashahhud
Ruling on traveler's four-rak'ah prayer with second-rak'ah tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a traveler prays four rak'ahs and sits for tashahhud in the second, and identify the consequence of omitting the sitting.

Core Idea
If a traveler sits for tashahhud in the second rak'ah of a four-rak'ah prayer, the first two count as fard; if not, the prayer is invalid.

This passage from Imam al-Quduri's matn addresses a specific scenario: a traveler who ends up praying four rak'ahs but sits for tashahhud in the second. The Hanafi ruling salvages the prayer by counting the first two rak'ahs as the obligatory prayer and the last two as nafl. However, if the traveler fails to sit for the tashahhud, the entire prayer becomes invalid. This ruling is an exception that hinges on the presence of the sitting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition
The act is a traveler praying four rak'ahs. The critical condition is sitting in the second rak'ah for the duration of the tashahhud (miqdar al-tashahhud).
The condition is not part of the original intention; it occurs after starting the prayer.
2
Apply the ruling when condition is met
If the traveler sits in the second rak'ah for tashahhud, the first two rak'ahs suffice for his fard obligation, and the remaining two become nafl (supererogatory).
The sitting signals the completion of the fard prayer, allowing the extra rak'ahs to be repurposed.
3
Apply the ruling when condition is absent
If the traveler does not sit in the second rak'ah for tashahhud, the prayer is invalid (batil). Neither the first two nor the last two count as a valid prayer.
Without the sitting, the fard is incomplete and the additional rak'ahs have no valid basis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ صَلَّى أَرْبَعًا وَقَعَدَ فِي الثَّانِيَةِ مِقْدَارَ التَّشَهُدِ أَجْزَأَتْهُ رَكْعَتَانِ عَنْ فَرْضِهِ وَكَانَتْ الْأُخْرَيَانِ لَهُ نَافِلَةٌ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَقْعُدُ فِي الثَّانِيَةِ قَدْرَ التَّشَهُدِ بَطَلَتْ صَلَاتُهُ
If he prays four and sits in the second to the extent of the tashahhud, two rak'ahs suffice him for his obligatory prayer, and the other two are supererogatory for him. If he does not sit in the second to the extent of the tashahhud, his prayer is invalid.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from Imam al-Quduri's matn on the prayer of a traveler. It addresses a scenario where a traveler mistakenly intends to pray four rak'ahs but sits for tashahhud in the second. In that case, the first two rak'ahs count as his fard (obligatory prayer), and the remaining two become nafl (supererogatory). This is because the obligation is only two rak'ahs, and the sitting indicates the intention to end the prayer, thus completing the fard. However, if he does not sit in the second, the entire prayer is invalid because he failed to end the fard properly and added extra rak'ahs without a valid separation. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
مِقْدَارَ التَّشَهُدِ (miqdār al-tashahhud): The amount of time it takes to recite the tashahhud (the testimony of faith) in the sitting position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a traveler prays four rak'ahs of zuhr without sitting for tashahhud in the second rak'ah, what is the ruling?
A) His prayer is valid and the first two count as fard.
B) His prayer is invalid.
C) His prayer is valid and all four count as nafl.
D) He must repeat the prayer but it is still valid.

Key Takeaway
The first two rak'ahs count as fard only if the traveler sits for tashahhud in the second; otherwise, the prayer is invalid.

Salah — Prayer

When the Traveler Begins Qasr
Defines the starting point for qasr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exact condition for beginning qasr according to the Hanafi school and identify the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Qasr begins when you leave the city houses—intention alone is not enough.

In this lesson, we examine a concise ruling from al-Quduri's matn. It pinpoints the exact moment a traveler must start shortening prayers: physical departure from the built-up area. This is not merely a matter of distance but of physically leaving one's town. The ruling is supported by the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as narrated by Anas ibn Malik.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text rules on the act of prayer for a traveler: he prays two rak'ahs when he separates from the houses of his city. The hukm is that qasr is wajib (obligatory) at that point.
Wajib means obligatory with evidence that is zanni in transmission or meaning; if omitted, the prayer is valid but sinful.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Anas (ra) where he prayed with the Prophet four in Medina and two at Dhu al-Hulayfah, which is outside Medina. This shows the Prophet shortened only after leaving the city.
Hadith is ahad but accepted in fiqh rulings.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key point: the Prophet prayed four in Medina (his residence) and two at Dhu al-Hulayfah (a place outside Medina). The change occurred after leaving the city limits, not upon intention or departure from home only.
This establishes the marker: leaving the continuous built-up area.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider qasr a rukhsah (license) not wajib, and may begin at different points (e.g., distance threshold). The Hanafi position is based on the immediate practice of the Salaf.
The dispute is over the nature of qasr: wajib vs. sunnah/rukhsah.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school adopts the view that qasr is wajib due to numerous ahadith and the practice of the Companions. The mufta bihi is that the traveler must shorten upon leaving the houses.
This is the relied-upon position from zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ خَرَجَ مُسَافِرًا صَلَّى رَكْعَتَيْنِ إِذَا فَارَقَ بُيُوتَ الْمِصْرِ
Whoever goes out as a traveler prays two rak'ahs when he separates from the houses of the city.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the matn of al-Quduri. It establishes the starting point for qasr (shortening) in travel: a person must physically leave the built-up area of his town. This is based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his Companions. The word 'm.s.r' (مصر) refers to a major city or town. The condition is that one must have left the continuous buildings; merely intending to travel or leaving the city limits is not sufficient. Once he has left the houses, he may pray two rak'ahs for the obligatory prayers.

Key Terms
بُيُوتَ الْمِصْرِ (buyūt al-miṣr): The houses/buildings of the city; the continuous built-up area of a settlement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, when does a traveler begin praying two rak'ahs?
A) When he intends to travel.
B) When he leaves the houses of his city.
C) When he reaches a distance of 48 miles.
D) After three days of travel.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires the traveler to start qasr only after physically leaving the continuous built-up area of his city, as proven by the Prophet's practice.
